Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
12 min
Establishing Hadd and Kaffarah by Dalalah al-Nass
Demonstrating that dalalah can prove hadd and kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of dalalah al-nass to derive a general ruling from a specific text and distinguish it from qiyas based on epistemological authority.

Core Idea
Dalalah al-nass is definitive; it can establish hudud, unlike speculative qiyas.

In this passage, the author argues that dalalah al-nass (implication of the text) is a fully valid and decisive source for deriving legal rulings, even the most serious ones like hudud penalties. The text contrasts dalalah with qiyas, emphasizing that dalalah is immediately understood by any Arabic speaker and does not require the ijtihad of a mujtahid. This distinction is crucial because hudud require definitive proof, and dalalah provides that certainty. You will work through the examples of stoning for zina and expiation for breaking the fast to see how dalalah operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit ruling in the source text
First, locate the explicit hukm (ruling) in the text. For the hadith of Ma'iz, the explicit ruling is that Ma'iz was stoned for zina. Note that this ruling is established by the expression ('ibarah) of the text.
The explicit ruling applies only to Ma'iz as an individual if we stop at the literal wording.
2
Recognize the additional implication (dalalah)
Now look beyond the explicit wording. The Prophet's action of stoning Ma'iz was because he was muhsan (married and free). The text implies that the hadd of stoning attaches to the attribute of being muhsan, not to the person. This is dalalah al-nass: a necessary linguistic implication (iltizam).
This implication is understood by any Arabic speaker without the need for qiyas.
3
Compare with qiyas
Unlike qiyas, which requires ijtihad to identify the 'illa (effective cause) and extend the ruling, dalalah is immediate and certain. The author points out that qiyas is often zanni (speculative) and therefore cannot establish hudud, whereas dalalah is qat'i (definitive).
Qiyas with a stated 'illa (mansusah) can also be definitive, but the default for inferred 'illa is zanni.
4
Apply the principle to the examples
Work through the two examples: (1) From the hadith of Ma'iz, derive the general rule that every muhsan adulterer is stoned. (2) From the hadith of the man who broke his fast intentionally, derive the general rule that any Muslim in that situation must perform kaffarah. In both cases, the general ruling is derived by dalalah, not qiyas.
These rulings could also be established by explicit texts, but the passage uses them to illustrate dalalah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab significance
The Hanafi school's acceptance of dalalah for hudud is distinctive. Other schools may require explicit nass or use qiyas. Understand why the Hanafis insist on dalalah being qat'i: because it is grounded in linguistic custom, not speculative reasoning.
This affects the evidentiary weight: dalalah is as strong as explicit text in the Hanafi hierarchy.

Source Text

كما روى البخاري عن أبي هريرة له، * والقياس وأما إذا كان بعلة منصوصة فيساوي الدلالة في القطعية وإثبات الحدود.
And what is established by implication of the text is like what is established by indication, so that the establishment of hadd penalties and expiations through the implication of texts is valid. It was from - legally or rationally, and likewise analogy is excluded. So on this, his statement 'not deduction by opinion' is a confirmation of his statement 'linguistically', and a refutation of those who claim that implication of the text is clear analogy. Because analogy is often speculative and hadd penalties cannot be established by it, unlike implication of the text. And analogy is only grasped by a mujtahid and requires reflection and deduction, unlike implication which is known by anyone who knows the Arabic language without needing to arrange premises and reflection. And implication is not denied by those who deny analogy. To this the author points with his statement: like the prohibition of saying 'uff' etc. In His statement: 'So do not say to them uff' (17:23), its placed meaning is the prohibition of uttering the word 'uff' only, and this is established by the expression of the text. So by this prohibition of 'uff', the prohibition of beating, insults, and anything that harms them is known without ijtihad and reflection. Because anyone who knows the Arabic language, even if not a mujtahid, knows from this very statement that beating is prohibited and forbidden. And this meaning is established by implication of the text because it is a necessary implication (iltizami) of its original meaning. In the expression there is leniency, and it would be better to say: like the prohibition of beating which is inferred from the prohibition of 'uff'. Then he clarified the difference between implication and analogy with his statement: 'And what is established by implication etc.' in that they are both definitive or that they are attributed to the text, unlike analogy because it is attributed to opinion. Listening? By implication of texts without analogy, this is a clear difference between them, because implication is definitive and analogy, when based on an inferred effective cause, is speculative, and hadd penalties can only be established by a definitive method, so it is valid to establish them by the former but not the latter. Example of establishing hadd by implication of the text: establishing the hadd of stoning for zina against Ma'iz, which was established by expression of the text. His story as narrated by al-Tirmidhi: that Ma'iz al-Aslami came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said, 'I have committed zina.' He turned away, then he came from his other side and said, 'I have committed zina.' He turned away, then he came from his left side and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina.' He ordered him in the fourth time, and he was taken out to al-Harrah and stoned with stones [al-Tirmidhi no. 428]. The Prophet ordered stoning for Ma'iz not because he was Ma'iz and a Companion, but because he committed zina while being muhsan. So it is known by implication of the text that anyone in that situation is to be stoned, even though this ruling can also be established by expression from other texts. And an example of establishing expiations by implication: establishing the expiation upon the man other than the one who had intercourse with his wife deliberately during Ramadan in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him), as narrated by al-Bukhari from Abu Hurayra. *Analogy: if it is based on a stated effective cause, it equals implication in definitiveness and in establishing hadd penalties.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage argues that dalalah al-nass is a fully valid and definitive source for establishing even the most serious of rulings, including hadd penalties (e.g., stoning for zina) and kaffarat (expiation for breaking Ramadan fast). The author repeats the key point that dalalah, unlike qiyas, is definitive (qat'i) and known by all Arabic speakers without need for ijtihad. This is why hadd penalties, which require definitive proof, can be established through dalalah but not through speculative analogy. Two examples are given. First, the case of Ma'iz: the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered stoning for him. While the explicit wording of the hadith establishes the stoning for Ma'iz as an individual, dalalah al-nass tells us that the ruling applies to any muhsan adulterer, because the reason for the stoning was his being muhsan, not his person. Thus, the general rule 'any muhsan adulterer is stoned' is derived by dalalah from this specific instance. Second, the case of a man who intentionally had intercourse with his wife during Ramadan day. Although the explicit hadith may only mention one man, dalalah al-nass extends the ruling of kaffarah (expiation) to all such cases. The passage also notes that if analogy is based on a stated cause (illa mansusah), it is definitive and can also establish hadd penalties, but the default for qiyas with inferred cause is speculative. Thus, dalalah remains superior for certainty.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed penalties for crimes against God's rights, such as stoning for zina, requiring definitive proof.
الكفارات (al-kaffarat): Expiation acts for certain sins, e.g., freeing a slave, fasting, etc.
ظني (zanni): Speculative, not certain. Qiyas is typically zanni unless the 'illa is stated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept the derivation of the general rule of stoning for muhsan adulterers from the case of Ma'iz via dalalah al-nass?
A) Because the hadith explicitly states the ruling for all muhsan people
B) Because the Prophet's action implies that the hadd applies to anyone in the same condition (muhsan), and this is understood linguistically without analogy
C) Because the Companions made a consensus
D) Because analogy (qiyas) from Ma'iz is the only way

Key Takeaway
Dalalah al-nass is a definitive mode of inference that can establish even the most serious rulings, such as hudud, without needing analogy.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Qada bil-Mithl and Marriage with Ambiguous Mahr: The Principle of Tabaddul al-Milk
Explaining qada bil-mithl and its application to marriage mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tabaddul al-milk to distinguish between qada and ada in the case of an unspecified mahr, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Change of ownership legally transforms an object, turning a judgment into performance.

The Hanafi school categorizes compensation for wrongful taking into comprehensible and non-comprehensible similars. This lesson explores how the principle of tabaddul al-milk (change of ownership) affects the classification of paying the value of an unspecified slave as mahr, turning a judgment into performance. We will trace the proof from the Hadith of Barira and understand the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of qada bil-mithl
The passage distinguishes between comprehensible similar (for fungibles) and non-comprehensible similar (for life/limbs). This sets up the analogy for the marriage case.
2
Analyze the marriage case: unspecified slave as mahr
The husband gives an average slave or its value. Why is giving value considered 'qada fi hukm al-ada'? Because the object is legally transformed due to change of ownership.
3
Extract the principle of tabaddul al-milk from the Hadith
The Hadith of Barira shows that the same meat changed from charity to gift when ownership changed. This proves that change of ownership changes the legal identity of the object.
4
Apply the principle to the marriage case
Because the slave's ownership changes from seller to husband to wife, the object becomes legally different at each stage. Thus, handing over the value is like handing over a new object, making it akin to performance.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i objection
Shafi'i says unknown mahr leads to gharar, invalidating the contract. Hanafi response: the uncertainty is resolved by reference to the average, and the principle of tabaddul al-milk supports validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضمان الغصب قضاء بمثل معقول، وضمان النفس والأطراف بالمال قضاء بمثل غير معقول. وإذا تزوج على عبد بغير عينه كان تسليمه القيمة قضاء هو في حكم الأداء، حتى تجبر على القبول كما لو أتاها بالمسمّى. المرأة أي قبول القيمة - لأن العبد إذا كان في ملك سيّده كان شخصاً آخر، ثم إذا اشتراه الزوج كان شخصا آخر، وإذا سلّمه إليها كان شخصا آخر؛ وذلك لأن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً، والدليل في ذلك ما رواه الشيخان عن عائشة لما قالت: دخل رسول الله والبرمة تفور بلحم، فقرب إليه خبز وأدم من أدم البيت فقال: ألم أربُرمةً فيها لحم؟ قالوا: بلى، ولكن ذلك لحم تُصدّق به على بريرة وأنت لا تأكل الصدقة، قال: "هو عليها صدقة ولنا هدية". فعلم أن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً، فكان الزوج لم يسلّم إليها ما وقع عليه العقد، بل سلّم إليها غيره؛ لأنه قبل التسليم كان مملوكاً للزوج، وتبدل الملك العين حكما كما عرفت ولهذا ينفذ إعتاق الزوج إياه؛ لأنه مملوكه ولا ينفذ إعتاق المرأة فيه قبل التسليم إليها. وهذا مثمرة كونه شبيهاً بالقضاء، ولما كانت ذات العبد موجودة في الحالين ووصف المملوكية متغيّر فيهما جعل يوجب تبدل أداء شبيها بالقضاء نظراً إلى الذات، ولم يجعل العكس. ولما فرغ عن أنواع الأداء شرع في أنواع القضاء. وضمان الغصب : أي الشيء المغصوب بالمثل فيما إذا غصب مثليا واستهلكه ووجد المثل فيما بين الناس أو بالقيمة فيما لم يكن له مثل أو كان له مثل ولكن انصرم عن أيدي الناس. قضاء بمثل معقول: أما الأول فظاهر؛ لكونه مثلا صورةً ومعنى، وأما الثاني فهو مثل معنى وإن لم يكن صورةً فالأول كامل، والثاني قاصر، فهذا نظير للقضاء بمثل معقول مع تسميه غير معقول: إذ لا مماثلة بين الفائت من النفس والأطراف وبين المال، أما صورة فظاهر، وأما معنى فلأن المال مملوك والآدمي مالك، وإنما شرع الله الدية لئلا تهدر النفس المحترمة مجاناً، وهذا نظير للقضاء بمثل غير معقول تسليمه أي الزوج القيمة إلى المرأة. بالمسمّى وهو العبد المتوسط تجبر على القبول فكذا تجبر على قبول القيمة، وهذا نظير للقضاء الذي في معنى الأداء. وحاصله إذا تزوّج الرجل امرأة وجعل مهرها عبداً غير معين بأن قال: نكحتك على عبد، فصحت التسمية عندنا خلافا للشافعي، فحينئذ إن اشترى عبداً وسطاً وسلّمه إليها كان أداء، وإن أتاها قيمة عبد وسط كان قضاء؛ إذ هو تسليم مثل الواجب ولكنه في معنى الأداء؛ إذ العبد هنا مجهول الوصف لا يمكن تسليمه، إلا بأن يسلّم عبداً وسطاً، والوسط لا يتحقق بغير التقويم، فصارت القيمة أصلا بهذا الوجه، فكان تسليم القيمة مثل تسليم العبد الوسط، فكان أداء من هذا الوجه حتى تجبر المرأة على قبول القسمة، كما تجبر على قبول عبد وسط بخلاف العبد المعين والمكيل والموزون الموصوف؛ لأن المسمّى معلوم جنساً ووصفا، فكانت قيمته قضاء خالصاً،
And the guarantee of usurpation is a judgment by a similar that is comprehensible, and the guarantee of life and limbs is a judgment by a similar that is not comprehensible. And if a man marries a woman on an unspecified slave, then giving the value is a judgment that is in the ruling of performance, such that she is forced to accept it just as if he had given her the specified (slave). The woman (i.e., acceptance of the value) - because when the slave was in the possession of his master, he was a different person; then when the husband bought him, he was a different person; and when he handed him over to her, he was a different person. That is because change of ownership legally necessitates change of the object. The evidence for that is what the two shaykhs narrated from Aisha: she said, 'The Messenger of Allah entered while the cooking pot was boiling with meat. Bread and some relish of the house were brought near to him. He said, 'Didn't I see a pot with meat?' They said, 'Yes, but that meat was given in charity to Barira, and you do not eat charity.' He said, 'It is charity for her and a gift for us.' So it is known that change of ownership legally necessitates change of the object. Thus the husband did not hand over to her what the contract fell upon, but rather handed over something else to her; because before handing over it was owned by the husband, and change of ownership (changes) the object legally as you know. Therefore the husband's manumission of it is effective because it is his property, and the woman's manumission of it is not effective before it is handed over to her. This is the fruit of it being similar to judgment. And since the essence of the slave existed in both states and the attribute of being owned changed in them, it was made to necessitate change, making performance similar to judgment in consideration of the essence, and not the reverse. And when he finished with the types of performance, he proceeded to the types of judgment. And the guarantee of usurpation: i.e., the usurped thing is by the like in the case when one usurps a fungible item and consumes it and the like is found among people, or by value when it has no like or has a like but has disappeared from people's hands. It is a judgment by a comprehensible similar: as for the first, it is apparent because it is a like in form and meaning; and as for the second, it is a like in meaning even if not in form. So the first is complete, and the second is deficient. This is analogous to judgment by a comprehensible similar along with its being called non-comprehensible: since there is no similarity between what is lost from life and limbs and between property, as for form it is apparent, and as for meaning because property is owned and the human is an owner. Allah has legislated blood money so that a respected life is not wasted in vain. This is analogous to judgment by a non-comprehensible similar: the husband's handing over of the value to the woman. The specified (slave) is the average slave; she is forced to accept it, so too she is forced to accept the value. This is analogous to judgment that is in the meaning of performance. The summary: if a man marries a woman and makes the mahr an unspecified slave by saying, 'I marry you on a slave,' then the specification is valid according to us contrary to al-Shafi'i. Then if he buys an average slave and hands it over to her, it is performance; and if he brings the value of an average slave, it is judgment because it is handing over the like of the obligation, but it is in the meaning of performance because the slave here is of unknown description and cannot be handed over except by handing over an average slave, and the average cannot be realized without valuation. So the value becomes the principal in this respect, making the handing over of the value like the handing over of the average slave. Thus it is performance from this aspect such that the woman is forced to accept the division, just as she is forced to accept an average slave, contrary to the case of a specified slave or measured or weighed items that are described; because the specified is known in genus and description, so its value is purely a judgment.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining two types of qada (judicial compensation) and their application to marriage contracts. The author first distinguishes between ضمان الغصب (guarantee of usurpation) which is قضاء بمثل معقول (judgment by a comprehensible similar) because the compensation matches the lost item in both form and meaning when the lost item is a fungible found in the market, or in meaning alone when only value is given. In contrast, ضمان النفس (guarantee of life) and ضمان الأطراف (guarantee of limbs) are قضاء بمثل غير معقول (judgment by a non-comprehensible similar) because there is no similarity between a human person and money; blood money (diyah) is legislated as a substitute. The author then applies this to a marriage case: if a man marries a woman with an unspecified slave as mahr (e.g., "I marry you on a slave"), he must give an average slave. If he gives the value of an average slave, it is qada but in the ruling of ada (performance) because the woman is forced to accept it. The reasoning relies on the legal principle that change of ownership (تبدل الملك) changes the legal identity of an object, proved by the Hadith of Barira where the Prophet accepted meat that was charity for her but became a gift for him after ownership changed. The passage also notes the Hanafi position that specifying an unspecified slave is valid, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The key takeaway is that the same act (handing over value) can be classified as qada in one sense and ada in another, depending on the nature of the obligation.

Key Terms
ضمان الغصب (daman al-ghasb): Guarantee for usurped property; compensation for illegally taking another's property.
قضاء بمثل معقول (qada' bi-mithl ma'qul): A judgment by a similar that is comprehensible, where the compensation matches the lost item in form and meaning.
تبدل الملك (tabaddul al-milk): Change of ownership; legally changes the identity of an object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the marriage case where the mahr is an unspecified slave, why is handing over the value considered 'qada fi hukm al-ada'?
A) Because the value is always qada and never ada.
B) Because the slave is unknown, so value is the only option.
C) Because the woman is forced to accept the value, just as she would accept an average slave, due to change of ownership.
D) Because the husband is unable to provide a slave.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of tabaddul al-milk allows a value payment to function as performance, validating an unspecified mahr contract.

Two Indicators of Sabab: Attribution and Recurrence
Explains two methods to identify sabab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two indicators of a cause (sabab) in Hanafi usul—attribution and recurrence—and apply them to determine the cause of a ruling.

Core Idea
A cause is known by attribution to it and recurrence with it.

In Hanafi usul, identifying the cause (sabab) of a ruling is crucial for analogy (qiyas) and understanding legal obligations. This passage introduces two key indicators: linguistic attribution (idafah) and empirical recurrence (takarrur). We will explore each indicator and see how they guide the jurist in pinpointing the cause.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sabab from shart
Understand that the original (asl) in attribution is to the cause; attribution to a condition is metaphorical.
This distinction is foundational in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify attribution as a primary indicator
When a ruling is attributed to a thing linguistically, it suggests that thing is the cause, as in 'prayer of Dhuhr' (salat al-zuhr).
Attribution is originally for distinction, so it points to the most specific thing—the cause.
3
Identify recurrence as a secondary indicator
If a ruling recurs with the recurrence of a thing, that thing is likely the cause.
Recurrence signals that the thing is the apparent cause of the ruling.
4
Apply the indicators to a simple case
Consider 'zakat of wealth' (zakat al-mal): the ruling is attributed to wealth, and zakat obligation recurs with the annual recurrence of wealth meeting the nisab. Thus wealth is the cause.
Recurrence here is through the description of growth.

Source Text

كتاب الله تعالى
فصل في بيان أسباب الشرائع
حكم الأصل في إضافة الشيء إلى الشيء]
وإنما يعرف السبب بنسبة الحكم إليه وتعلقه به؛ لأن الأصل في إضافة الشيء إلى الشيء المضاف إليه أن يكون سبباً له. وإنما يضاف إلى الشرط مجازاً، وكذا إذا لازمه فتكرّر بتكرّره دلّ أنه يضاف إليه، وفي صدقة الفطر إنما جعلنا الرأس سبباً، والفطر شرطاً مع وجود الإضافة إليهما؛ لأن وصف المؤونة يرجح الرأس في كونه سبباً، جواب إذا أي وقته ولما فرغ عن إثبات هذا الأصل شرع في بيان أمارة كون الشيء سبباً فقال: وإنما يعرف السبب إلخ: يعني علامة كون الشيء سببا لشيء أمران: أحدهما أن يضاف الحكم إليه، كقولك: صلاة الظهر، وصوم الشهر، وحج البيت، وحدّ الشرب، وكفارة القتل، وأن يتعلق به بأن لا يوجد بدونه ويحدث به. سببا له: أي للشيء المضاف وأن يكون الشيء المضاف حادثاً بالمضاف إليه، كقولك: كسب فلان أي حدث بفعله؛ لأن الإضافة لما كانت موضوعة للتميز كان الأصل فيها الإضافة إلى أخص الأشياء ليحصل التميز، وأخص الأشياء بالحكم إنما هو سببه؛ لأنه يثبت به فكانت الإضافة إليه أصلا ولما كان يتوهم أن الشيء كما يضاف إلى السبب يُضاف إلى الشرط مجازاً لعلاقة المشابهة؛ لأن الحكم يوجد عنده أيضا فشابه الشرط العلةَ هذا الوجه، ولا عبرة بالمجاز؛ لأن المعتبر هو الحقيقة، وثانيهما ما بينه المصنّف بقوله: وإنما يضاف إلخ. من يضاف إليه: يعنى كما أن الإضافة دليل على السببية كذلك ملازمة الشيء بالشيء وتكرّره بتكرره دليل على السببية؛ لأن الأمور تضاف إلى أسبابها الظاهرة، فلما تكرّر الشيء دلّ على أنه حادث به؛ إذ هو السبب الظاهر لحدوثه. والوجوب فيما نحن فيه أمر حادث فلا بدله من سبب يضاف إليه وليس ههنا إلا الأمر أو الوقت والأمر لا يصلح أن يضاف إليه؛ لأنه لا يدلّ على التكرار ولا يحتمله كما عرفت، فتعين الوقت للسببية. لأن وصف المؤونة إلخ جواب سؤال يرد هنا، وهو أن صدقة الفطر كما يضاف إلى الرأس ويقال: زكاة الرأس، كما في قول الشاعر : زكاة رؤوس الناس بكرة فطرهم بقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صاع من التمر يضاف إلى الفطر فيقال: صدقة الفطر، فبأي وجه جعلتم الرأس سبباً والفطر شرطاً دون عكسه، مع أن الإضافة إلى الفطر أكثر؟ تقرير الجواب: أنه لما وقع التعارض بينهما في السببية لوجود الإضافة رجّحنا الرأس لأجل وصف المؤونة، أي القيام بكفاية المتعلّقين؛ لأن صدقة الفطر إنما وجبت وجوب المؤونة؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: " وابدأ بمن تعول". رواه البخاري [رقم: ١٤٢٦] وعن أبي هريرة وحكيم ومسلم عن حكيم وحده، فعلم أنه أجراها محرى المؤونة، = وتكرّر الوجوب بتكرّر الفطر بمنزلة تكرّر وجوب الزكاة بتكرّر الحول. السبب بتجدد الوصف بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه] لأن الوصف الذي لأجله كان الرأس سبباً وهو المؤونة يتجدد بتجدّد الزمان، كما للوجوب أن النماء الذي لأجله كان المال سبباً لوجوب الزكاة، يتجدد بتجدد الحول، ويصير السبب بتجدّد الوصف بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه. وعلى هذا تكرر العشر والخراج مع اتحاد السبب، وهو الأرض النامية في العشر حقيقةً بالخارج، وفي الخراج حكما بالتمكن من الزراعة. والأصل في وجوب المؤونة هو الرأس؛ لأنه يلي عليه دون الوقت؛ إذ الرأس هو المحتاج إلى المؤونة دون الوقت، ولما كان يرد عليه أن الترجيح للوقت؛ لأن وجوب الصدقة يتكرّر بتكرره، وهذا علامة السبب لا يوجد في الرأس؛ لأنه لا تكرّر فيه أجاب عنه بقوله : وتكرّر الوجوب إلخ : يعني تكرر وجوب الصدقة ليس بتكرر الشرط الذي هو الفطر، بل بسبب تكرر السبب وهو الرأس، وهو وإن لم يكن متكرّراً حقيقةً لكنه جعل متكرراً تقديراً؛ لأجل تكرر الفطر أي وقته، كما أن المال الذي هو سبب الزكاة جعل متكرّرا تقديراً لأجل تكرر الحول الذي هو شرط كأنه متكرّر ، فكذا الحال في الرأس. المؤونة يتجدد إلخ: يعني لما صار الرأس سبباً لوجوب الصدقة بوصف المؤونة كما عرفت وهي تتجدّد بتجدد وقت الفطر كان الرأس بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه لتجدد وصفه، كما أن النصاب سبب لوجوب الزكاة بوصف النماء، والنماء يتجدّد ويتكرّر بتكرر الحول صار المال متكرراً بنفسه لتكرر وصفه، حتى يتكرر وجوب الزكاة في نصاب واحد بتكرر الحول. وعلى هذا: الطريق وهو أن السبب يتكرر بتكرّر الوصف تكرر العشر إلخ. مع اتحاد السبب إلخ: يعني مع أن السبب للعشر والخراج واحد وهو الأرض النامية حقيقةً في العشر، والأرض النامية تقديراً في الخراج بأن يتمكن النماء من الزراعة يتكرّر وجوبهما بسبب تكرر وصف السبب، وهو الخارج حقيقة في العشر، والتمكن في الخراج، وذلك لأن بتكرر الوصف جعل السبب متكرّرا تقديراً فيتكرر الحكم بتكرّره التقديري، فإذا حدث الخارج من الأرض تحقيقاً يجب العشر، وإن اصطلمت الأرض آفة يسقط تيسيرًا بحال المسلم، وبتكرر الوجوب يتكرر النماء، وإذا وجد التمكن من الزراعة وجب الخراج، سواء زرع الأرض أو عطلها؛ لأنه يليق بحال الكافر المتوغل في الدنيا. المؤون في "المغرب" مانه يمونه أي قام بكفايته.
And the cause is known by attributing the ruling to it and its connection with it; because the original principle in attributing a thing to a thing is that the attributed thing is a cause for it. And it is only attributed to a condition metaphorically. Similarly, if it is inseparable and recurs with its recurrence, it indicates that it is attributed to it. And in Sadaqat al-Fitr, we made the head (person) the cause and the breaking of fast (Fitr) the condition, despite the existence of attribution to both, because the characteristic of maintenance (mu'unah) gives weight to the head being the cause. The answer when: i.e., its time. And when he finished establishing this principle, he began to explain the indicator of a thing being a cause, saying: And the cause is known, etc.: meaning, the sign of a thing being a cause for something is two things: One is that the ruling is attributed to it, as you say: the prayer of Dhuhr, the fast of the month, the Hajj of the House, the hadd of drinking, the expiation of killing, and that it is connected to it such that it does not exist without it and occurs with it. A cause for it: i.e., for the attributed thing, and that the attributed thing occurs by the attributed-to, as you say: so-and-so's earning, i.e., it occurred by his action. Because since attribution is placed for distinction, the original in it is attribution to the most specific things to achieve distinction, and the most specific thing to the ruling is its cause, because it is established by it, so attribution to it is the original. And because it might be imagined that a thing, just as it is attributed to the cause, is also attributed to the condition metaphorically due to similarity, because the ruling also exists with it, so the condition resembles the cause in this respect, and metaphor is not considered because what is considered is the reality. And the second is what the author explained by his saying: And it is only attributed, etc. to what it is attributed to: meaning, just as attribution is evidence of causality, similarly the inseparability of a thing from a thing and its recurrence with its recurrence is evidence of causality; because matters are attributed to their apparent causes. So when a thing recurs, it indicates that it occurs by it, since it is the apparent cause for its occurrence. And obligation in our subject is an occurring matter, so it must have a cause to which it is attributed, and here there is only the command or the time. The command is not suitable to be attributed to it because it does not indicate recurrence nor can it bear it, as you know, so the time is determined for causality. Because the characteristic of maintenance, etc. is the answer to a question that arises here, namely that Sadaqat al-Fitr, just as it is attributed to the head and it is said: zakat of the head, as in the poet's saying: Zakat of the heads of people at the time of their breaking fast, by the saying of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'A sa' of dates', it is attributed to the breaking of fast and is called: Sadaqat al-Fitr. So by what reasoning did you make the head the cause and the breaking of fast the condition and not the opposite, even though attribution to the breaking of fast is more frequent? The substance of the answer: when there was conflict between them in causality due to the existence of attribution, we gave preponderance to the head because of the characteristic of maintenance, i.e., undertaking the sufficient maintenance of dependents; because Sadaqat al-Fitr was obligated as an obligation of maintenance, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'And begin with those you support.' Related by Bukhari [no. 1426], and from Abu Huraira and Hakim, and Muslim from Hakim alone. Thus it is known that He placed it in the position of maintenance. = And the recurrence of obligation with the recurrence of the breaking of fast is like the recurrence of the obligation of zakat with the recurrence of the year. The cause by the renewal of the description is like something that renews itself.] Because the description on account of which the head was a cause, namely maintenance, renews with the renewal of time, just as for obligation, the growth on account of which wealth was a cause for the obligation of zakat renews with the renewal of the year, and the cause becomes, by the renewal of the description, like something that renews itself. And on this basis, the 'ushr and kharaj recur despite the unity of the cause, namely the land that grows, in 'ushr really by the produce, and in kharaj legally by the ability to cultivate. And the original in the obligation of maintenance is the head, because it pertains to it and not the time, since the head is the one in need of maintenance, not the time. And when it was objected that the preponderance should be for the time because the obligation of the charity recurs with its recurrence, and this is a sign of a cause that does not exist in the head because there is no recurrence in it, he answered it with his saying: And the recurrence of obligation, etc.: meaning, the recurrence of the obligation of charity is not due to the recurrence of the condition which is the breaking of fast, but rather due to the recurrence of the cause which is the head. And although it is not really recurrent, it is made recurrent by estimation because of the recurrence of the breaking of fast, i.e., its time, just as wealth, which is the cause of zakat, is made recurrent by estimation because of the recurrence of the year which is the condition, as if it were recurrent. So similarly is the case with the head. The maintenance renews, etc.: meaning, when the head became a cause for the obligation of charity by the description of maintenance, as you know, and it renews with the renewal of the time of breaking of fast, the head becomes like something that renews itself due to the renewal of its description, just as the nisab is a cause for the obligation of zakat by the description of growth, and growth renews and recurs with the recurrence of the year, wealth becomes recurrent by itself due to the recurrence of its description, so that the obligation of zakat recurs on one nisab with the recurrence of the year. And on this basis: the way, namely that the cause recurs with the recurrence of the description, the 'ushr recurs, etc., despite the unity of the cause, etc.: meaning, even though the cause for 'ushr and kharaj is one, namely the land that grows, really in 'ushr, and the land that grows by estimation in kharaj by being able to cultivate, their obligations recur due to the recurrence of the description of the cause, which is the produce really in 'ushr and the ability in kharaj. And because by the recurrence of the description, the cause is made recurrent by estimation, so the ruling recurs with its estimated recurrence. So when produce actually emerges from the land, 'ushr is obligatory; if a calamity strikes the land, it falls away as a facilitation for the Muslim. And with the recurrence of obligation, the growth recurs. And when the ability to cultivate is found, kharaj is obligatory, whether he cultivates the land or leaves it idle, because it befits the state of the disbeliever deeply immersed in this world. 'Mu'un' in 'al-Mughrib' is 'ma yamuunuhu', i.e., he undertook his maintenance.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains the methods for identifying the cause (sabab) of a legal ruling. The author begins by stating that a cause is known through two indicators: first, the attribution (idafah) of the ruling to a particular thing, and second, the recurrence (takarrur) of the ruling with the recurrence of that thing. He emphasizes that the original, literal attribution is to the cause, while attribution to a condition (shart) is metaphorical. The key example discussed is Sadaqat al-Fitr. Although the charity is attributed both to the head (zakat al-ra's) and to the breaking of fast (sadaqat al-fitr), the Hanafi school considers the head (the person) as the cause and the breaking of fast as the condition. The reason given is the characteristic of maintenance (mu'unah): the Prophet's hadith 'Begin with those you support' indicates that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like a maintenance obligation, and the head is the one who requires maintenance. The author then addresses an objection: if recurrence of the ruling with the condition (the breaking of fast) is a sign of the cause, then the time (Fitr) should be the cause. He responds by explaining that the cause (the head) is made recurrent by estimation due to the recurrence of its description (maintenance), which renews with each year. This is analogous to zakat, where wealth (the cause) is not literally recurrent, but its description (growth) recurs with the passing of years, making the obligation recur. Similarly, for 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax), the land is the single cause, but the recurrence of produce or ability to cultivate causes the obligation to recur. This demonstrates the Hanafi usul principle that a cause can be considered recurrent by estimation when its description recurs.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause to which a ruling is attributed and without which the ruling does not exist; identified by attribution and/or recurrence.
شرط (shart): A condition that accompanies the ruling but is not the cause; attribution to it is metaphorical.
إضافة (idafah): Linguistic attribution; the grammatical construction that indicates a relationship, originally oriented to the cause.
مؤونة (mu'unah): Maintenance or support; the characteristic that makes the head the cause in Sadaqat al-Fitr.
تكرر (takarrur): Recurrence; if a ruling recurs with the recurrence of a thing, that thing is likely the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an indicator that something is a cause (sabab) of a ruling?
A) The thing is frequently mentioned in legal texts
B) The ruling is attributed to the thing linguistically and/or recurs with its recurrence
C) The thing is always present when the ruling is observed
D) The thing is a command from the Lawgiver

Key Takeaway
A cause is identified through literal attribution and/or recurrence; metaphorical attribution to a condition is not sufficient.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
10 min
The Case of Sadaqat al-Fitr: Determining the Cause via Maintenance and Estimated Recurrence
Resolves conflict in Sadaqat al-Fitr example using maintenance and estimated recurrence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the head (ra's) is the cause of Sadaqat al-Fitr in the Hanafi school, using the concept of maintenance (mu'unah) and the principle of estimated recurrence.

Core Idea
Maintenance makes the head the cause; recurrence of the time makes the head recurrent by estimation.

The example of Sadaqat al-Fitr illustrates how the indicators of attribution and recurrence can conflict. This passage shows how the Hanafi school resolves the conflict by appealing to the underlying characteristic (wasf) of maintenance and by reasoning that the cause is considered recurrent when its description recurs. Understanding this case is crucial for mastering the Hanafi method of identifying legal causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two attributions
Sadaqat al-Fitr is attributed to both the head (zakat al-ra's) and the time of breaking fast (sadaqat al-fitr). This creates a conflict in identifying the cause.
The phrase 'zakat al-ra's' is found in poetry, while 'sadaqat al-fitr' is common in hadith.
2
Understand the conflict
Both attributions suggest causality, but the school must determine which is the true cause and which is metaphorical.
The indicator of recurrence points to the time because the obligation recurs annually with Fitr.
3
Apply the hadith evidence for maintenance
The Prophet's hadith 'Begin with those you support' indicates that Sadaqat al-Fitr is a maintenance obligation (mu'unah). Maintenance pertains to the head (the supported person), not the time.
This textual evidence (dalil) gives preponderance to the head as the cause.
4
Understand estimated recurrence
The head does not literally recur each year, but its description (maintenance) renews annually. The cause is considered recurrent by estimation (takdir) because its description recurs.
This resolves the objection that recurrence is a sign of the cause and the head lacks recurrence.
5
Apply the analogy to other rulings
Similarly, in zakat, wealth is the cause but its description (growth) recurs with the year, making the wealth recurrent by estimation. In 'ushr and kharaj, land is the cause, but its description (produce or ability to cultivate) recurs.
This demonstrates the general Hanafi principle that a cause is considered recurrent if its description recurs.

وقع التعارض بينهما في السببية لوجود الإضافة رجّحنا الرأس لأجل وصف المؤونة، أي القيام بكفاية المتعلّقين؛ لأن صدقة الفطر إنما وجبت وجوب المؤونة؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: " وابدأ بمن تعول". رواه البخاري [رقم: ١٤٢٦] وعن أبي هريرة وحكيم ومسلم عن حكيم وحده، فعلم أنه أجراها محرى المؤونة، = وتكرّر الوجوب بتكرّر الفطر بمنزلة تكرّر وجوب الزكاة بتكرّر الحول. السبب بتجدد الوصف بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه] لأن الوصف الذي لأجله كان الرأس سبباً وهو المؤونة يتجدد بتجدّد الزمان، كما للوجوب أن النماء الذي لأجله كان المال سبباً لوجوب الزكاة، يتجدد بتجدد الحول، ويصير السبب بتجدّد الوصف بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه. وعلى هذا تكرر العشر والخراج مع اتحاد السبب، وهو الأرض النامية في العشر حقيقةً بالخارج، وفي الخراج حكما بالتمكن من الزراعة. والأصل في وجوب المؤونة هو الرأس؛ لأنه يلي عليه دون الوقت؛ إذ الرأس هو المحتاج إلى المؤونة دون الوقت، ولما كان يرد عليه أن الترجيح للوقت؛ لأن وجوب الصدقة يتكرّر بتكرره، وهذا علامة السبب لا يوجد في الرأس؛ لأنه لا تكرّر فيه أجاب عنه بقوله : وتكرّر الوجوب إلخ : يعني تكرر وجوب الصدقة ليس بتكرر الشرط الذي هو الفطر، بل بسبب تكرر السبب وهو الرأس، وهو وإن لم يكن متكرّراً حقيقةً لكنه جعل متكرراً تقديراً؛ لأجل تكرر الفطر أي وقته، كما أن المال الذي هو سبب الزكاة جعل متكرّرا تقديراً لأجل تكرر الحول الذي هو شرط كأنه متكرّر ، فكذا الحال في الرأس. المؤونة يتجدد إلخ: يعني لما صار الرأس سبباً لوجوب الصدقة بوصف المؤونة كما عرفت وهي تتجدّد بتجدد وقت الفطر كان الرأس بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه لتجدد وصفه، كما أن النصاب سبب لوجوب الزكاة بوصف النماء، والنماء يتجدّد ويتكرّر بتكرر الحول صار المال متكرراً بنفسه لتكرر وصفه، حتى يتكرر وجوب الزكاة في نصاب واحد بتكرر الحول. وعلى هذا: الطريق وهو أن السبب يتكرر بتكرّر الوصف تكرر العشر إلخ. مع اتحاد السبب إلخ: يعني مع أن السبب للعشر والخراج واحد وهو الأرض النامية حقيقةً في العشر، والأرض النامية تقديراً في الخراج بأن يتمكن النماء من الزراعة يتكرّر وجوبهما بسبب تكرر وصف السبب، وهو الخارج حقيقة في العشر، والتمكن في الخراج، وذلك لأن بتكرر الوصف جعل السبب متكرّرا تقديراً فيتكرر الحكم بتكرّره التقديري، فإذا حدث الخارج من الأرض تحقيقاً يجب العشر، وإن اصطلمت الأرض آفة يسقط تيسيرًا بحال المسلم، وبتكرر الوجوب يتكرر النماء، وإذا وجد التمكن من الزراعة وجب الخراج، سواء زرع الأرض أو عطلها؛ لأنه يليق بحال الكافر المتوغل في الدنيا. المؤون في "المغرب" مانه يمونه أي قام بكفايته.
And the cause is known by attributing the ruling to it and its connection with it; because the original principle in attributing a thing to a thing is that the attributed thing is a cause for it. And it is only attributed to a condition metaphorically. Similarly, if it is inseparable and recurs with its recurrence, it indicates that it is attributed to it. And in Sadaqat al-Fitr, we made the head (person) the cause and the breaking of fast (Fitr) the condition, despite the existence of attribution to both, because the characteristic of maintenance (mu'unah) gives weight to the head being the cause. The answer when: i.e., its time. And when he finished establishing this principle, he began to explain the indicator of a thing being a cause, saying: And the cause is known, etc.: meaning, the sign of a thing being a cause for something is two things: One is that the ruling is attributed to it, as you say: the prayer of Dhuhr, the fast of the month, the Hajj of the House, the hadd of drinking, the expiation of killing, and that it is connected to it such that it does not exist without it and occurs with it. A cause for it: i.e., for the attributed thing, and that the attributed thing occurs by the attributed-to, as you say: so-and-so's earning, i.e., it occurred by his action. Because since attribution is placed for distinction, the original in it is attribution to the most specific things to achieve distinction, and the most specific thing to the ruling is its cause, because it is established by it, so attribution to it is the original. And because it might be imagined that a thing, just as it is attributed to the cause, is also attributed to the condition metaphorically due to similarity, because the ruling also exists with it, so the condition resembles the cause in this respect, and metaphor is not considered because what is considered is the reality. And the second is what the author explained by his saying: And it is only attributed, etc. to what it is attributed to: meaning, just as attribution is evidence of causality, similarly the inseparability of a thing from a thing and its recurrence with its recurrence is evidence of causality; because matters are attributed to their apparent causes. So when a thing recurs, it indicates that it occurs by it, since it is the apparent cause for its occurrence. And obligation in our subject is an occurring matter, so it must have a cause to which it is attributed, and here there is only the command or the time. The command is not suitable to be attributed to it because it does not indicate recurrence nor can it bear it, as you know, so the time is determined for causality. Because the characteristic of maintenance, etc. is the answer to a question that arises here, namely that Sadaqat al-Fitr, just as it is attributed to the head and it is said: zakat of the head, as in the poet's saying: Zakat of the heads of people at the time of their breaking fast, by the saying of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'A sa' of dates', it is attributed to the breaking of fast and is called: Sadaqat al-Fitr. So by what reasoning did you make the head the cause and the breaking of fast the condition and not the opposite, even though attribution to the breaking of fast is more frequent? The substance of the answer: when there was conflict between them in causality due to the existence of attribution, we gave preponderance to the head because of the characteristic of maintenance, i.e., undertaking the sufficient maintenance of dependents; because Sadaqat al-Fitr was obligated as an obligation of maintenance, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'And begin with those you support.' Related by Bukhari [no. 1426], and from Abu Huraira and Hakim, and Muslim from Hakim alone. Thus it is known that He placed it in the position of maintenance. = And the recurrence of obligation with the recurrence of the breaking of fast is like the recurrence of the obligation of zakat with the recurrence of the year. The cause by the renewal of the description is like something that renews itself.] Because the description on account of which the head was a cause, namely maintenance, renews with the renewal of time, just as for obligation, the growth on account of which wealth was a cause for the obligation of zakat renews with the renewal of the year, and the cause becomes, by the renewal of the description, like something that renews itself. And on this basis, the 'ushr and kharaj recur despite the unity of the cause, namely the land that grows, in 'ushr really by the produce, and in kharaj legally by the ability to cultivate. And the original in the obligation of maintenance is the head, because it pertains to it and not the time, since the head is the one in need of maintenance, not the time. And when it was objected that the preponderance should be for the time because the obligation of the charity recurs with its recurrence, and this is a sign of a cause that does not exist in the head because there is no recurrence in it, he answered it with his saying: And the recurrence of obligation, etc.: meaning, the recurrence of the obligation of charity is not due to the recurrence of the condition which is the breaking of fast, but rather due to the recurrence of the cause which is the head. And although it is not really recurrent, it is made recurrent by estimation because of the recurrence of the breaking of fast, i.e., its time, just as wealth, which is the cause of zakat, is made recurrent by estimation because of the recurrence of the year which is the condition, as if it were recurrent. So similarly is the case with the head. The maintenance renews, etc.: meaning, when the head became a cause for the obligation of charity by the description of maintenance, as you know, and it renews with the renewal of the time of breaking of fast, the head becomes like something that renews itself due to the renewal of its description, just as the nisab is a cause for the obligation of zakat by the description of growth, and growth renews and recurs with the recurrence of the year, wealth becomes recurrent by itself due to the recurrence of its description, so that the obligation of zakat recurs on one nisab with the recurrence of the year. And on this basis: the way, namely that the cause recurs with the recurrence of the description, the 'ushr recurs, etc., despite the unity of the cause, etc.: meaning, even though the cause for 'ushr and kharaj is one, namely the land that grows, really in 'ushr, and the land that grows by estimation in kharaj by being able to cultivate, their obligations recur due to the recurrence of the description of the cause, which is the produce really in 'ushr and the ability in kharaj. And because by the recurrence of the description, the cause is made recurrent by estimation, so the ruling recurs with its estimated recurrence. So when produce actually emerges from the land, 'ushr is obligatory; if a calamity strikes the land, it falls away as a facilitation for the Muslim. And with the recurrence of obligation, the growth recurs. And when the ability to cultivate is found, kharaj is obligatory, whether he cultivates the land or leaves it idle, because it befits the state of the disbeliever deeply immersed in this world. 'Mu'un' in 'al-Mughrib' is 'ma yamuunuhu', i.e., he undertook his maintenance.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains the methods for identifying the cause (sabab) of a legal ruling. The author begins by stating that a cause is known through two indicators: first, the attribution (idafah) of the ruling to a particular thing, and second, the recurrence (takarrur) of the ruling with the recurrence of that thing. He emphasizes that the original, literal attribution is to the cause, while attribution to a condition (shart) is metaphorical. The key example discussed is Sadaqat al-Fitr. Although the charity is attributed both to the head (zakat al-ra's) and to the breaking of fast (sadaqat al-fitr), the Hanafi school considers the head (the person) as the cause and the breaking of fast as the condition. The reason given is the characteristic of maintenance (mu'unah): the Prophet's hadith 'Begin with those you support' indicates that Sadaqat al-Fitr is like a maintenance obligation, and the head is the one who requires maintenance. The author then addresses an objection: if recurrence of the ruling with the condition (the breaking of fast) is a sign of the cause, then the time (Fitr) should be the cause. He responds by explaining that the cause (the head) is made recurrent by estimation due to the recurrence of its description (maintenance), which renews with each year. This is analogous to zakat, where wealth (the cause) is not literally recurrent, but its description (growth) recurs with the passing of years, making the obligation recur. Similarly, for 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax), the land is the single cause, but the recurrence of produce or ability to cultivate causes the obligation to recur. This demonstrates the Hanafi usul principle that a cause can be considered recurrent by estimation when its description recurs.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause to which a ruling is attributed and without which the ruling does not exist; in Sadaqat al-Fitr, it is the head.
شرط (shart): A condition that accompanies the ruling but is not the cause; in Sadaqat al-Fitr, it is the time of breaking fast.
إضافة (idafah): Linguistic attribution; in Sadaqat al-Fitr, the ruling is attributed to both head and time.
مؤونة (mu'unah): Maintenance or support; the characteristic that makes the head the cause in Sadaqat al-Fitr.
تكرر (takarrur): Recurrence; in Sadaqat al-Fitr, the obligation recurs annually, but this is due to the recurrence of the cause's description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Sadaqat al-Fitr, why does the Hanafi school consider the head (ra's) the cause rather than the time of breaking fast (Fitr)?
A) Because the head is mentioned first in the phrase 'zakat al-ra's'
B) Because the head has the characteristic of maintenance (mu'unah), as supported by the hadith 'Begin with those you support'
C) Because the time of breaking fast is not a real condition
D) Because the head recurs literally every year

Key Takeaway
When attribution conflicts, the characteristic indicated by textual evidence determines the cause; the cause is considered recurrent if its description recurs.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
12 min
Sunnah: Definition, Types, and Application to Adhan Rulings
Defines Sunnah, classifies, and applies to adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sunnah according to the Hanafi school, distinguish between Sunnat al-Huda and Sunnat al-Zawa'id, and apply this classification to interpret the rulings (makruh, no harm, etc.) in the chapter of adhan.

Core Idea
Sunnah is the Prophet's path; its two types determine whether abandonment brings blame or not.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text provides a rigorous definition of Sunnah and divides it into two categories based on the consequence of abandonment. The commentator then applies this classification to explain the varied rulings given by Imam Muhammad on adhan practices. Understanding this usul framework is essential for correctly determining fiqh rulings in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of Sunnah
Find the sentence defining Sunnah as 'the path followed in the religion' and note its ruling: required but not fard or wajib.
The definition applies to Sunnat al-Huda, not absolute Sunnah.
2
Identify the two types
Sunnat al-Huda (e.g., congregational prayer, adhan) and Sunnat al-Zawa'id (e.g., Prophet's habitual actions like sitting and dressing).
Also called sunnah mu'akkadah and mustahabb respectively.
3
Analyze the consequence of abandonment
For Sunnat al-Huda: sin and dislike (karahah); for Sunnat al-Zawa'id: no sin or dislike. Note the hadith evidence.
The hadith 'alaykum bi sunnati' commands reviving the Sunnah.
4
Apply to adhan rulings
Trace Imam Muhammad's expressions (makruh, he has sinned, no harm) to the two types: 'makruh' and 'he has sinned' indicate Sunnat al-Huda; 'no harm' indicates Sunnat al-Zawa'id.
Where 'yu'id' (repeats) appears, that is from the ruling of wajib, not sunnah.
5
Draw the usul lesson
The classification of Sunnah is a key Hanafi principle that resolves apparent contradictions in textual rulings.

التارك والسنة نوعان: سنة الهدى، وتاركها يستوجب إساءة وكراهة. والزوائد، وتاركها
المطلقة
أحدهما
أي يستحق
أي وثانيهما سنة الزوائد لا يستوجب إساءة وكراهة، كسير النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في قيامه وقعوده ولباسه.
بالبدن. وقوله: 'بلا عذر' احتراز عن الترك بعذر، فإن التارك بالعذر الشرعي لايكون فاسقاً. شبهة سواء كان الشبهة في ثبوت ذلك الدليل كخبر الواحد أو في دلالته كالعام المخصوص البعض والمجمل والمؤوّل على اليقين لما في دليله من الشبهة. استخف بأخبار الآحاد بأن لا يرى العمل واجباً لا أن يتهاون بها، فإن التهاون بالشرع كفر. متأوّلا فلا أي فإن ترك العمل بأخبار الآحاد بطريق التأويل بأن يقول: هذا الخبر ضعيف أو مخالف لكتاب، فلا يفسق فيه؛ لأن هذا الترك ليس لأجل الهوى بل لأجل التحقيق والتدقيق كما توارث به العلماء. الطريقة المسلوكة سواء سلكها النبي أو الصحابة.
يطالب المرء بإقامتها : احترز به عن النفل؛ لأنه غير مطالب من غير افتراض احترز به عن الفرض. ولا وجوب احترز به عن الواجب، وهذا التعريف والحكم لسنة الهدى لا لمطلق السنة، والتقسيم الثاني لمطلق السنة. ثم استدلّ على قوله : يطالب المرء بإقامتها بقوله : لأنها إلخ. أمرنا بإحيائها لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام:
'عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين المهديين'. رواه أحمد وأبو داود رقم: ٤٦٧٠] والترمذي وابن ماجة. اللائمة أي الملامة في الدنيا وحرمان الشفاعة في العقبى بتركها وهذا تفريع على قوله: 'فيطالب المرء بإقامتها'. سنة الهدى: كالجماعة والأذان والإقامة وكراهة: وهو اللوم والعتاب، حتى لو أصر أهل مصر على تركها يُقاتلوا بالسلاح من جانب الإمام، كما وردت به الأحاديث الصحيحة والآثار القوية. كسير النبي إلخ السير جمع السيرة، وهي الخصلة، فخصاله لل في القيام والقعود واللباس وغيره لم تصدر منه على وجه العبادة قصداً بل على سبيل العادة، فيثاب المرء على فعلها ولا يعاقب على تركها.

وعلى هذا تخرّج الألفاظ المذكورة في باب الأذان من قوله: يكره، أو قد أساء،
أو لا بأس به، وحيث قيل: يعيد، فذلك من حكم الوجوب

أنه
وعلى هذا أي على أن السنة نوعان نوع يوجب تركها إساءة وكراهة ونوع لايوجب تركها ذلك. يكره إلخ يعني لما ثبت أن السنة بعضها يوجب إساءة وكراهة تركها، وبعضها لا اختلف أجوبة ذكرها محمد محله في 'المبسوط' في باب الأذان فحيث لزم ترك السنة المؤكدة، أي سنة الهدى قال في جوابه: يكره، وقد أساء، كما قال: ويكره الأذان قاعداً ، ويكره تكرار الأذان في مسجد محلة لمخالفة السنة، وإن صلّى أهل مصر بجماعة وإقامة فقد أساء وترك السنة المشهورة، وحيث لزم ترك سنة الزوائد قال في جوابه ولا بأس كما قال ولا بأس بأن يؤذن رجل ويقيم آخر ، ففي كل موضع قال: قد أساء أو يكره يعلم أنه من حكم سنة الهدى؛ لأن الإساءة والكراهة لايلزم إلا بتركها، وفي موضع قال: لا بأس يعلم أنه من حكم سنة الزوائد؛ لأن عدم البأس إنما يكون بتركها.
بغير
أذان
من حكم الوجوب كما قال: ولا يؤذن للصلاة قبل دخول وقته ويعاد في الوقت. أقول: إنما أورد المصنف هذا لإتمام الفائدة، وإلا فلا دخل له في المبحث؛ لأن الكلام في السنة لا في الواجب.
Chapter on Azimah and Rukhsah. By the body, not as knowledge. And Wajib is what has been established as obligatory by a proof that contains shubhah (ambiguity), and its ruling is binding (luzum) in practice, up to certainty, so that its denier is not declared a disbeliever, and its abandoner becomes sinful if he belittles akhbar al-ahad, but if he interprets (ta'wil) then no. Because definitive knowledge is cut off. The Sunnah and its types and rulings. And the Sunnah is the path followed in the religion, and its ruling is that a person is required to establish it without it being farad or wajib; because it is a path we are commanded to revive, so he deserves blame for abandoning it. The one who abandons it, and the Sunnah is of two types: Sunnat al-Huda, whose abandoner incurs sin and dislike (karahah), and Sunnat al-Zawa'id, whose abandoner does not incur sin and dislike. One of them, i.e., deserves. And the second is Sunnat al-Zawa'id, which does not incur sin and dislike, like the conduct (sirah) of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his standing, sitting, and clothing. By the body. And his saying: 'without excuse' is a restriction against abandonment with an excuse, for the one who abandons with a legal excuse is not sinful. Shubhah, whether the ambiguity is in the establishment of the proof, like khabar al-wahid, or in its indication (dalalah), like the general (amm) that is specified (makhsus) in part, and the ambiguous (mujmal) and the interpreted (mu'awwal) up to certainty, because there is ambiguity in its proof. Belittles akhbar al-ahad means he does not consider acting upon them as obligatory, not that he neglects them, for neglect of the Shari'ah is disbelief. Interpreting (ta'wil), no, i.e., if he abandons acting upon akhbar al-ahad through ta'wil by saying: this hadith is weak or contradicts the Book, then he is not sinful; because this abandonment is not for desire but for verification and scrutiny, as the scholars have transmitted. The path followed, whether it was followed by the Prophet or the Companions. 'A person is required to establish it': he restricts (ihtiraz) from nafl, because he is not required; from farad, he restricts; and from wajib, he restricts. And this definition and ruling for Sunnat al-Huda, not for absolute Sunnah, and the second division is for absolute Sunnah. Then he adduced evidence for his saying 'a person is required to establish it' by his saying: 'because it is...' We are commanded to revive it due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'You must hold to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.' Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud (no. 4670), al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. Blame (la'imah) means censure in this world and deprivation of intercession in the Hereafter for abandoning it, and this is a corollary of his saying 'a person is required to establish it'. Sunnat al-Huda: like congregation, adhan, and iqamah; and dislike: it is blame and reproach, such that if the people of a city persist in abandoning it, they are fought with weapons by the Imam, as established by sound hadiths and strong reports. 'Conduct of the Prophet etc.' al-sirah is the plural of sirah, meaning trait, so his traits (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) in standing, sitting, clothing, etc., were not done by him as acts of worship intentionally, but as habit; so a person is rewarded for doing them but not punished for leaving them. And upon this the mentioned expressions in the chapter of adhan are based: his saying: 'disliked (makruh),' or 'he has sinned,' or 'there is no harm,' and where it is said: 'he repeats (yu'id),' that is from the ruling of wajib. The saying of Muhammad: The saying indicates that. And upon this, i.e., that the Sunnah is of two types: a type whose abandonment causes sin and dislike, and a type whose abandonment does not cause that. 'Disliked etc.' means since it is established that some Sunnah causes sin and dislike for abandoning it, and some does not, the answers mentioned by Muhammad, its place in al-Mabsut in the chapter of adhan, varied. So where the abandonment of the confirmed Sunnah (i.e., Sunnat al-Huda) is necessary, he said in his answer: 'disliked, and he has sinned,' as he said: 'It is disliked to perform adhan while sitting,' and 'It is disliked to repeat the adhan in a neighborhood mosque due to contradicting the Sunnah,' and 'If the people of a city prayed with congregation and iqamah, he has sinned and abandoned the famous Sunnah.' And where the abandonment of Sunnat al-Zawa'id is necessary, he said in his answer: 'There is no harm,' as he said: 'There is no harm if one man gives adhan and another gives iqamah.' So in every place he said 'he has sinned' or 'disliked,' it is known that it is from the ruling of Sunnat al-Huda, because sin and dislike only follow from its abandonment. And in a place he said 'there is no harm,' it is known that it is from the ruling of Sunnat al-Zawa'id, because the absence of harm only occurs from its abandonment. Without adhan. From the ruling of wajib, as he said: 'Adhan is not given for prayer before its time enters, and it is repeated at the time.' I say: The author only mentioned this to complete the benefit, otherwise it has no relevance to the discussion, because the talk is about Sunnah, not about wajib.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on definitions and classifications from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. It begins with the definition of wajib: an obligation established by a proof containing some ambiguity (shubhah), such as khabar al-wahid or a general text that has been specified. Its denier is not a disbeliever, but its abandoner becomes a sinner if he belittles such proofs; however, if he abandons through legitimate interpretation (ta'wil), he is not sinful. The main focus is the definition of Sunnah: the path followed in the religion, whether by the Prophet or the Companions. Its ruling is that a person is required to establish it, but it is not fard or wajib. The commentator notes that this definition applies specifically to Sunnat al-Huda, not the absolute Sunnah. Sunnah is divided into two types: (1) Sunnat al-Huda (e.g., congregational prayer, adhan, iqamah) – abandoning it incurs sin and dislike (karahah), and if a whole city persists, the Imam may fight them; (2) Sunnat al-Zawa'id (e.g., the Prophet's habitual actions like standing, sitting, dressing) – abandoning it does not incur sin or dislike, and a person is rewarded for doing it but not punished for leaving it. The passage then applies this classification to the rulings in the chapter on adhan, citing Imam Muhammad's answers in al-Mabsut: where the abandonment involves Sunnat al-Huda, the ruling is 'he has sinned' or 'it is disliked'; where it involves Sunnat al-Zawa'id, the ruling is 'no harm.' The commentator concludes by noting that the author included this to complete the benefit, though the discussion is about Sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligation established by a proof with ambiguity (shubhah), such as khabar al-wahid.
السنة (al-sunnah): The path followed in the religion; a recommended practice that is required to be upheld but not obligatory.
سنة الهدى (sunnat al-huda): The confirmed Sunnah whose abandoner incurs sin and dislike (karahah), like congregational prayer and adhan.
سنة الزوائد (sunnat al-zawa'id): The extra Sunnah consisting of the Prophet's habitual actions (e.g., way of sitting, dress); no blame for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, what is the ruling on abandoning Sunnat al-Huda?
A) No sin or dislike
B) Sin and dislike (karahah)
C) Disbelief (kufr)
D) Obligation to repeat (i'ada)

Key Takeaway
Sunnah is classified into two types in Hanafi usul, and this classification directly determines the fiqh ruling for actions like adhan.

The Definition and Divisions of Sunna in Hanafi Usul
Defining Sunna as a source of law and distinguishing it from Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Sunna, distinguish it from Hadith, and identify its three types (verbal, practical, approbative).

Core Idea
Sunna is broader than Hadith: it includes the Prophet's sayings, actions, and tacit approvals, and also the sayings and actions of the Companions.

In this passage, the author transitions from discussing the first principle (Quran) to the second: Sunna. Since the basic definition of Sunna is well-known, he immediately moves to its divisions. He defines Sunna linguistically and legally, clarifies its relationship to Hadith, and distinguishes three categories: verbal, practical, and approbative. Understanding this foundational distinction is crucial for proper istinbat (legal derivation) because the Hanafi school treats Sunna as an independent source that includes materials beyond the Prophet's direct words.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Sunna from Hadith
Read the passage carefully to identify how the author defines Sunna vs. Hadith. Note that Sunna includes sayings, actions, and tacit approvals of the Prophet, as well as sayings and actions of the Companions. Hadith is restricted to the Prophet's sayings alone.
The author uses 'Sunna' deliberately to encompass the broader scope.
2
Identify the three types of Sunna
The passage mentions qawli (verbal), fi'li (practical), and taqriri/sukuti (approbative/tacit) Sunna. For each, think of a concrete example from the life of the Prophet.
Taqrir (tacit approval) occurs when the Prophet remains silent in the presence of an action or statement, thereby endorsing it.
3
Understand the disagreement with Muhaddithin
The passage notes that some hadith scholars equate Sunna, Hadith, and Khabar, while others differentiate between Hadith and Khabar. The Hanafi position is that Sunna is the broadest category.
This disagreement has implications for classification of reports in usul.
4
Apply the definition
Given a report from a Companion (e.g., 'Umar introducing the tarawih prayer), determine whether it qualifies as Sunna in the Hanafi sense. Since it is a practice of a Companion, it would be included in the Hanafi definition of Sunna.
This illustrates why Hanafi jurists often cite actions of the Companions as evidence.

Source Text

باب السنة
الأصل الثاني السنة
وفي مسألتنا هما سواء، فصار كالمدبر إذا جنى لزم مولاه الأقل من الأرش ومن القيمة بخلاف العبد لما قلنا.
باب في بيان أقسام السنة
اعلم أن سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم جامعة للأمر والنهي والخاص والعام وسائر الأقسام التي
هما: أي القصر والإكمال، سواء بدليل بناء أحدهما على الآخر واتحادهما في الشرط والاسم، فلا يتضمن التخير رفقاً بل يتعين اليسر في القصر. فصار أي ما ذكرنا من تعين القصر في حق المسافر. كالمدبر إذا جنى إلخ يعني ما ذكرنا من أن اليسر متعين في قصر المسافر فلا يفيد التخير نظير لمسألة المدبر، فإن المدبر إذا جنى جناية بأن أتلف مال إنسان يلزم على المولى ما هو الأقل من القيمة ومن الأرش عينا لاتحاد الجنس؛ لأن القيمة من جنس الأرش فيتعين الرفق في الأقل خاصة، كما يتعين الرفق في قصر المسافر، فلا يتخير بين قيمة المدبر وبين أرش الجناية، لعدم تضمن التخير رفقاً.
لما قلنا: فإنه إذا جنى جناية يتخير المولى بين دفع العبد بعينه إلى ولي الجناية وبين دفع أرش الجناية وإن كان قيمة العبد أقل أو أكثر من الأرش، وذلك لما قلنا في تخير العبد المأذون في الجمعة من أن التخير بين الشيئين المتغايرين يفيد الرفق، وفي العبد أيضا أمران متغايران: أحدهما دفع العبد بعينه، والثاني دفع الأرش، فإنهما مختلفان صورة ومعنى، فإن أحدهما مال والآخر رقبة، وعند التغير لا يتعين الرفق في الأقل عدداً، بل يتضمن كل واحد منهما رفقاً، فيفيد التخير رفقاً كما في العبد المأذون في الجماعة يفيد التخير بين الجمعة والظهر المتغايرين رفقاً. ولما فرغ عن الأصل الأول، وهو كتاب الله شرع في الأصل الثاني وهو السنة، ولما كان تعريفها مشهوراً عند الأنام أعرض عنه وشرع في تقسيمها. السنة: السنة في اللغة الطريقة والعادة، وفي الشرع تطلق على العبادات النافلة التي يتعلق بفعلها الثواب ولا يتعلق بتركها العقاب، وأيضاً يطلق على ما صدر من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم غير القرآن والفرق بينها وبين الحديث هو أن السنة تطلق على قوله وفعله وسكوته عليه السلام وعلى أقوال الصحابة وأفعالهم والحديث يطلق على قوله عليه السلام خاصة، فلذا أورد المصنف لفظ السنة ليشمل الجميع، وعند المحدثين: السنة والخبر والحديث بمعنى واحد، حيث يطلق كل واحد منها على قوله وفعله وسكوته وعلى قول الصحابي والتابعي وفعلهما وسكوتهما، وخص بعضهم الحديث بالمرفوع والموقوف؛ إذ المقطوع أثر عنده، وبعضهم فرق بين الحديث والخبر فقال: ما جاء منه عليه السلام أو من الصحابي أو التابعي فهو حديث، وما فيه أحوال السلاطين والأخبار الماضية خبر سنة رسول الله: أي قوله عليه السلام خاصة.
سكوته: والمراد بالسكوت أنه فعل أحد أو قال شيئا في حضرته عليه السلام ولم ينكر عليه بل سكت وقرر، ويقال للأول السنة القولية، وللثاني الفعلية، وللثالث التقريرية والسكوتية.
Chapter on Sunna. The second principle: Sunna. In our issue, they are equal, so it becomes like the mudabbar if he commits a crime, the master is liable for the lesser of the blood money and the value, unlike the slave for what we said. Chapter on explaining the divisions of Sunna. Know that the Sunna of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) encompasses command and prohibition, the specific and the general, and all the divisions that... They are: i.e., the shortening and the completion, equal by evidence of one building upon the other and their unity in condition and name, so the choice does not involve ease, rather ease is determined in shortening. So it became what we mentioned of the determination of shortening for the traveler. Like the mudabbar if he commits a crime etc. means what we mentioned that ease is determined in the traveler's shortening, so it does not benefit choice similar to the issue of the mudabbar, for the mudabbar if he commits a crime by destroying someone's property, the master is liable for the lesser of the value and the blood money in kind due to unity of genus; because the value is of the same genus as the blood money, so ease is determined in the lesser, just as ease is determined in the traveler's shortening, so he does not have a choice between the value of the mudabbar and the blood money of the crime, due to lack of ease in the choice. For what we said: If he commits a crime, the master has a choice between handing over the slave himself to the guardian of the crime and paying the blood money even if the value of the slave is less or more than the blood money, and that is for what we said in the choice of the authorized slave in Friday: that choice between two different things benefits ease, and in the slave also there are two different things: one is handing over the slave himself, and the second is paying the blood money, for they differ in form and meaning, for one is property and the other is a person, and upon difference, ease is not determined in the lesser number, rather each contains ease, so choice benefits ease as in the authorized slave in the congregation benefits choice between Friday and zuhr which are different with ease. And when he finished with the first principle, which is the Book of God, he began the second principle, which is Sunna, and since its definition was well-known among people, he turned away from it and began its division. Sunna: Sunna in language is the way and custom, and in law it is applied to supererogatory acts of worship, the performance of which is rewarded and the omission of which is not punished, and also it is applied to what issued from the Prophet (peace be upon him) other than the Quran, and the difference between it and Hadith is that Sunna applies to his sayings, actions, and tacit approvals and to the sayings and actions of the Companions, while Hadith applies to his sayings specifically. Therefore, the author used the word Sunna to include all. And according to the Muhaddithin: Sunna, Khabar, and Hadith are synonymous, each applying to his sayings, actions, and tacit approvals and to the sayings and actions of the Companion and the Tabi'i, and some restricted Hadith to the marfu' and mawquf; for the maqtu' is considered athar, and some distinguished between Hadith and Khabar saying: what comes from him (peace be upon him) or from the Companion or the Tabi'i is Hadith, while what concerns the conditions of rulers and past news is Khabar. The Sunna of the Messenger of God: i.e., his sayings specifically. His tacit approval: what is meant by tacit approval is that someone did something or said something in his presence (peace be upon him) and he did not object but remained silent and acquiesced. The first is called the verbal Sunna, the second the practical, and the third the approbative (tacitly approved).
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion of Sunna as the second source of law in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by concluding the previous topic on 'azima and rukhsa with an analogy to the mudabbar slave, then transitions to the new chapter. He defines Sunna linguistically as 'way' (tariqa) and 'custom' ('ada). In legal terminology (shar'), Sunna has two common usages: (1) supererogatory acts of worship (nawafil) which are rewarded but not sinful to omit, and (2) everything that came from the Prophet (peace be upon him) other than the Quran—this includes his sayings (qawl), actions (fi'l), and tacit approvals (sukut or taqrir). The passage distinguishes Sunna from Hadith: according to the author, Sunna is broader, applying also to the sayings and actions of the Companions, whereas Hadith is specifically limited to the Prophet's sayings. This is why the author uses the term Sunna to encompass all these categories. The passage then clarifies that according to the Muhaddithin (hadith scholars), the terms Sunna, Khabar, and Hadith are often synonymous. However, some differentiate: Hadith can be marfu' (attributed to Prophet) or mawquf (attributed to Companion), while maqtu' (attributed to Tabi'i) is called athar. Some also distinguish between Hadith and Khabar: Khabar refers to historical reports about rulers or past events, while Hadith refers to reports from the Prophet or his Companions/Tabi'in. Finally, the passage explains the three divisions of Sunna: qawliyya (verbal), fi'liyya (practical), and taqririyya/sukutiyya (approbative/tacit).

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunna): ما صدر من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم غير القرآن من قول وفعل وتقرير، ويشمل أقوال الصحابة وأفعالهم عند المصنف
الحديث (al-hadith): يطلق على قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خاصة عند المصنف
التقرير (al-taqrir): سكوت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على فعل أو قول صدر بحضرته ولم ينكره

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما الفرق بين السنة والحديث عند المصنف؟
A) لا فرق بينهما
B) السنة تشمل قول النبي وفعله وتقريره وأقوال الصحابة وأفعالهم، والحديث يختص بقول النبي
C) السنة خاصة بالعبادات النافلة
D) الحديث أعم من السنة

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines Sunna broadly to include the Prophet's sayings, actions, tacit approvals, and the practices of the Companions, making it a richer source of law than the narrower category of Hadith.

Definition and Scope of Sunnah in Hanafi Usul
Defines Sunnah and its components

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sunnah linguistically and technically, distinguish it from Hadith and Khabar, and identify the three types of Sunnah (qawli, fi'li, taqriri) according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Sunnah in Hanafi usul includes the Prophet's statements, actions, tacit approvals, and the statements and actions of the Companions.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of Sunnah, the second primary source of Islamic law after the Qur'an. The author distinguishes Sunnah from Hadith and Khabar, and outlines the three categories: verbal, practical, and tacit. Understanding this definition is crucial for later discussions on how the Sunnah functions as a source of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
The author states that sunnah linguistically means way or habit (الطريقة والعادة). Note that technical definitions build on this.
2
Extract the technical Shari'ah definition
The author gives two technical usages: (1) supererogatory acts of worship (النافلة), and (2) what emanated from the Prophet ﷺ other than the Qur'an. This second usage is the concern of usul al-fiqh.
The first usage is fiqhi, the second is usuli.
3
Distinguish Sunnah from Hadith and Khabar
The author explains that Sunnah includes qawl, fi'l, and sukut of the Prophet, as well as aqwal and af'al of the Companions. Hadith is restricted to the Prophet's speech. Khabar, according to some, refers to historical reports.
Hanafi usul gives the Companions' statements and actions legislative value; other schools do not.
4
List the three types of Sunnah
Based on the author's explanation, Sunnah is divided into qawliyyah (verbal), fi'liyyah (practical), and taqririyyah/sukutiyyah (tacit approval). Each type has different legal authority.
Tacit approval indicates permissibility.
