الوسائط التي بينه وبين النبي ويقول : قال النبي كذا، وهو على أربعة أقسام؛ لأنه إما يرسله الصحابي أو التابعي أو من دونهم من تبع التابعين، أو هو مرسل من وجه دون وجه، فالأول هو الأول، والثاني هو الثاني والثالث هو الثالث والرابع هو الرابع. وأما عند المحدثين فسقوط السند إن كان أوّله أي من المصنّف وهو المعلّق، ومن صوره أن يحذف جميع السند ويقول: قال النبي ، ومنها أن يحذف إلا الصحابي، أو إلا التابعي والصحابي معاً. من ومنها أن يحذف شيخه ويضيف إلى من فوقه، وإن كان السقوط من آخر السند بعد التابعي فهو المرسل بأن يقول التابعي: قال النبي كذا. ثم لا يخلو إما إن كان السقوط باثنين فصاعداً مع التوالي فهو المعضل، وإلا أي إن لم يكن السقوط باثنين مع التوالي، أو سقط واحد فقط أو أكثر من اثنين لكن بشرط عدم التوالي فهو المنقطع. ومسند وهو خلاف المرسل بأن يقول الراوي: حدثنا فلان عن فلان عن رسول الله . فالمرسل من الصحابي: بأن يقول: قال النبي كذا مثلا، ولايذكر شيخه. هذا إذا كان رواية الصحابي من صحابي آخر، وإلا فالإرسال عن الصحابي غير متصوّر ؛ إذ لا واسطة بينه وبين رسول الله . وهذا هو القسم الأول. محمول على السماع مقبول بالإجماع؛ لأن إرساله بإسقاط صحابي متوسط بينه وبين= * كلها: دفع لما يتوهم أن التواتر ليس بمخصوص للسنة؛ لأنه يوجد في الكتاب أيضا فدفعه بقوله: "كلها" والحاصل إن وجد بعض الأبحاث ولكن كلها لاتوجد فيه. فافهم.
Chapter of Sunnah. The second principle: Sunnah. And in our issue, both are equal, so it became like the mudabbar when it commits a tort, the lesser of the blood-money and the value is incumbent upon its master, meaning in the issue of the traveler's appearance, the value, unlike the slave, as we said. Chapter on explaining the divisions of the Sunnah. Know that the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ encompasses command and prohibition, specific and general, and all the divisions which are: the two (shortening and completion) are equal, as proven by building one on the other and their unity in condition and name, so it does not entail choice for ease, rather ease is determined in shortening. So it became, i.e., what we mentioned of the determination of shortening for the traveler. Like the mudabbar when it commits a tort, etc., meaning what we mentioned that ease is determined in the traveler's shortening, so choice does not benefit ease, analogous to the mudabbar issue. For the mudabbar, if it commits a tort by destroying someone's property, the lesser of the value and the blood-money is necessarily incumbent upon the master, due to the unity of type, because the value is of the same type as the blood-money, so ease is determined in the lesser specifically, just as ease is determined in the traveler's shortening, so he does not choose between the value of the mudabbar and the blood-money of the tort, because choice does not entail ease. Performance. As we said: For if it commits a tort, the master chooses between handing over the slave himself to the guardian of the tort and paying the blood-money of the tort, even if the slave's value is less or more than the blood-money. And that is as we said regarding the choice of the authorized slave in Jumu'ah: that choice between two different things benefits ease, and in the slave also there are two different matters: one is handing over the slave himself, and the second is paying the blood-money, for they differ in form and meaning, for one is property and the other is a person. And when there is difference, ease is not determined in the lesser in number, rather each one entails ease, so choice benefits ease, as in the authorized slave in the congregation, choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr, which are different, benefits ease. When he finished from the first principle, which is the Book of Allah, he began the second principle, which is the Sunnah. And since its definition was well-known among the people, he turned away from it and began its division. Sunnah: linguistically, it means the way and habit. In Shari'ah, it is applied to supererogatory acts of worship, the doing of which earns reward and the omission of which does not incur punishment. Also, it is applied to what emanated from the Prophet ﷺ other than the Qur'an. The difference between them (Sunnah and Hadith) is that Sunnah is applied to his statement, action, and tacit approval, and to the statements and actions of the Companions, while Hadith is applied specifically to his statement. Hence the author used the word Sunnah to include all. According to the Muhaddithin, Sunnah, Khabar, and Hadith are synonymous, each applied to his statement, action, and tacit approval, and to the statement and action of the Companion and Tabi'i and their tacit approval. Some restricted Hadith to Marfu' and Mawquf, since Maqtu' is only an Athar according to them. Some distinguished between Hadith and Khabar, saying: what comes from him ﷺ or from the Companion or Tabi'i is Hadith, and what deals with the affairs of rulers and past events is Khabar. Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah: i.e., his statement specifically. His tacit approval: the meaning of tacit approval is that someone did or said something in his presence and he did not object but remained silent and affirmed. The first is called qawli Sunnah, the second fi'li, and the third taqriri and sukuti. Chapter of Sunnah. The second principle: Sunnah. It was mentioned earlier, so the Sunnah is a branch of the Book in explaining those divisions with their rulings, but the chapter is only to explain what is specific to the Sunnahs. i.e., Chapter of Sunnah. Mursal and Musnad. So we say: Sunnah is of two types: Mursal and Musnad. The Mursal from the Companion is attributed to hearing, and from the second century, who are the Tabi'un. The Mursal: Sunnah is a branch, etc., so there is no need to repeat it in the chapter of Sunnah. What is specific to the Sunnahs: it is not found in the Book, such as investigating how a chain is connected or broken, the context of the report, how hearing, accuracy, and transmission occur. All these investigations are not found in the Book, because it is transmitted only by mutawatir reports. If you understand this, we say: Sunnah, in terms of its reaching us, is of two types. Mursal: that the narrator drops the intermediaries between him and the Prophet and says: The Prophet said such and such. It is of four types: either the Companion narrates it as mursal, or the Tabi'i, or those after them of the next generation, or it is mursal from one aspect and not from another. The first is the first, second the second, third the third, fourth the fourth. According to the Muhaddithin, if the drop is from the beginning, i.e., from the author, it is Mu'allaq. Its forms include dropping the entire chain and saying: The Prophet said..., and dropping only the Companion, or dropping both the Tabi'i and Companion together. And also dropping his immediate teacher and attributing to the one above him. If the drop is from the end of the chain after the Tabi'i, it is Mursal, as when the Tabi'i says: The Prophet said such and such. Then either the drop is of two or more consecutively, it is Mu'dal, otherwise, i.e., if not two consecutively, or only one drop, or more than two but not consecutively, it is Munqati'. Musnad: the opposite of Mursal, as when the narrator says: So-and-so narrated to us from so-and-so from the Messenger of Allah. The Mursal from the Companion: he says: The Prophet said such and such, for example, without mentioning his teacher. This is if the Companion is narrating from another Companion; otherwise, Mursal from a Companion is inconceivable, as there is no intermediary between him and the Messenger of Allah. This is the first type. It is attributed to hearing and accepted by consensus, because his drop is of a Companion intermediary between him and... * All of them: a refutation of the misconception that tawatur is not specific to Sunnah because it is also found in the Book. He refutes it by saying 'all of them' and the result is that some investigations are found, but all of them are not found in it. Understand.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the Sunnah, the second source of Islamic law after the Qur'an. The author begins with a ruling: in the case of a traveler shortening prayer, there is no choice; it is determined. He supports this with an analogy (qiyas) involving a mudabbar slave (one whose manumission is deferred until the master's death). Just as a mudabbar committing a tort obligates the master to pay the lesser of its value or the blood-money because both are of the same type (property), so too the traveler's shortening and completing prayer are of the same type (both valid prayers), so the traveler must choose the easier (shortening) because choice between two different things would provide ease only if they were different, but here they are the same genus. He contrasts this with a regular slave, where the master has a genuine choice between handing over the slave or paying blood-money because they are different (person vs. property). This illustrates a usul principle: ease through choice only applies when the options are different in essence. The author then formally defines Sunnah linguistically and technically, distinguishing it from Hadith and Khabar. According to the Hanafi usul tradition, Sunnah includes the Prophet's statements, actions, and tacit approvals, as well as the statements and actions of the Companions (since they are a source of law). Hadith, in contrast, is restricted to the Prophet's statements. The term 'Khabar' is sometimes used for historical reports. The author also explains three types of Sunnah: qawli (verbal), fi'li (action), and taqriri/sukuti (tacit approval). Finally, he discusses the transmission categories: musnad (with a complete chain) and mursal (with a missing link). Mursal from a Companion is accepted by consensus because the missing Companion intermediary does not affect reliability. He details various forms of broken chains according to hadith terminology: mu'allaq, mursal, munqati', and mu'dal. The passage emphasizes that these technical discussions about chains are specific to Sunnah, not the Qur'an, because the Qur'an is transmitted mutawatir.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): Linguistically: way or habit. Technically: what emanated from the Prophet ﷺ other than the Qur'an, including his statements, actions, and tacit approvals, and also the statements and actions of the Companions. In fiqh, it also refers to supererogatory acts.
الحديث (al-hadith): According to the author, hadith is specifically the Prophet's statements (qawl), while sunnah is broader. However, muhaddithin use them interchangeably.
الخبر (al-khabar): In some terminologies, khabar refers to historical accounts and reports about rulers, distinct from hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT included in the Hanafi definition of Sunnah?
A) The Prophet's tacit approval
B) The statements of the Companions
C) The actions of the Tabi'in (Successors)
D) The Prophet's actions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, Sunnah is the second source of law and encompasses the Prophet's words, deeds, approvals, and the statements and actions of the Companions.

Module 12 · Lesson 8

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
Transmission Categories of Sunnah: Musnad, Mursal, and Broken Chains
Divides Sunnah into transmission categories and explains broken chain terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between musnad (continuous chain) and mursal (broken chain), identify the subtypes of mursal (from Companion, Tabi'i, etc.), and state the Hanafi position on accepting mursal from a Companion.

Core Idea
A mursal hadith from a Companion is accepted as sound by Hanafis, while other broken chains require scrutiny.

This lesson focuses on the transmission categories of Sunnah: how a report reaches us with a full chain (musnad) or with a missing link (mursal). The author explains the technical hadith terminology for broken chains and highlights the Hanafi acceptance of mursal from a Companion, which is a key point of debate with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic division: musnad vs. mursal
The passage states that Sunnah, in terms of its reaching us, is of two types: musnad (with a continuous chain up to the Prophet) and mursal (where the narrator drops one or more intermediaries). This is the foundational division.
Musnad is considered stronger in transmission.
2
Define the four subtypes of mursal
The author lists four types based on who drops the chain: (1) a Companion narrates without mentioning his source (if he heard from another Companion), (2) a Tabi'i says 'The Prophet said' without a Companion, (3) a Taba' Tabi'i does the same, (4) a report that is mursal from one perspective and not from another.
The fourth type is a report that has both a mursal and a musnad version.
3
Identify Hanafi rule on mursal from Companions
The author explicitly states: 'The Mursal from the Companion is attributed to hearing and accepted by consensus because his drop is of a Companion intermediary.' Hanafis consider such mursal sound because the missing Companion is trustworthy and the drop is insignificant.
Other broken chains (from Tabi'i or later) are not automatically accepted.
4
Distinguish other broken chain terms
The passage introduces mu'allaq (drop from the beginning of the chain), munqati' (drop of one or more with non-consecutive breaks), and mu'dal (drop of two or more consecutively). These are distinct from mursal.
Hanafis have specific conditions for accepting each type.

باب السنة الأصل الثاني السنة وفي مسألتنا هما سواء، فصار كالمدبّر إذا جنى لزم مولاه الأقل من الأرش ومن أي في مسألة ظهر المسافر القيمة بخلاف العبد لما قلنا . باب في بيان أقسام السنة اعلم أن سنة رسول الله الله جامعة للأمر والنهي والخاص والعام وسائر الأقسام التي هما : أي القصر والإكمال، سواء بدليل بناء أحدهما على الآخر واتحادهما في الشرط والاسم، فلا يتضمن التخير رفقاً بل يتعيّن اليسر في القصر. فصار أي ما ذكرنا من تعين القصر في حق المسافر. كالمدبّر إذا جنى إلخ يعني ما ذكرنا من أن اليسر متعين في قصر المسافر فلايفيد التخير نظير لمسألة المدبر، فإن المدبّر إذا جنى جناية بأن أتلف مال إنسان يلزم على المولى ما هو الأقل من القيمة ومن الأرش عينا لاتحاد الجنس؛ لأن القيمة من جنس الأرش فيتعين الرفق في الأقل خاصةً، كما يتعين الرفق في قصر المسافر، فلا يتخير بين قيمة المدبّر وبين أرش الجناية، لعدم تضمن التخير رفقاً. أداء لما قلنا : فإنه إذا جنى جناية يتخيّر المولى بين دفع العبد بعينه إلى ولي الجناية وبين دفع أرش الجناية وإن كان قيمة العبد أقل أو أكثر من الأرش، وذلك لما قلنا في تخيّر العبد المأذون في الجمعة من أن التخير بين الشيئين المتغايرين يفيد الرفق، وفي العبد أيضا أمران متغايران: أحدهما دفع العبد بعينه، والثاني دفع الأرش، فإنهما مختلفان صورة ومعنى، فإن أحدهما مال والآخر رقبة، وعند التغير لا يتعين الرفق في الأقل عدداً، بل يتضمن كل واحد منهما رفقاً، فيفيد التخيّر رفقاً كما في العبد المأذون في الجماعة يفيد التخير بين الجمعة والظهر المتغايرين رفقاً. ولما فرغ عن الأصل الأول، وهو كتاب الله شرع في الأصل الثاني وهو السنة، ولما كان تعريفها مشهوراً عند الأنام أعرض عنه وشرع في تقسيمها. السنّة: السنة في اللغة الطريقة والعادة، وفي الشرع تطلق على العبادات النافلة التي يتعلّق بفعلها الثواب ولا يتعلق بتركها العقاب، وأيضاً يطلق على ما صدر من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم غير القرآن والفرق بينهما وبين الحديث هو أن السنة تطلق على قوله وفعله وسكوته عليه وعلى أقوال الصحابة وأفعالهم والحديث يطلق على قوله عليها خاصة، فلذا أورد المصنف لفظ السنة ليشمل الجميع، وعند المحدثين: السنّة والخبر والحديث بمعنى واحد، حيث يطلق كل واحد منها على قوله وفعله وسكوته وعلى قول الصحابي والتابعي وفعلهما وسكوتهما، وخص بعضهم الحديث بالمرفوع والموقوف؛ إذ المقطوع أثر عنده، وبعضهم فرّق بين الحديث والخبر فقال: ما جاء منه عليه أو من الصحابي أو التابعي فهو حديث، وما فيه أحوال السلاطين والأخبار الماضية خبر سنة رسول الله: أي قوله (عليه) خاصة. * سكوته: ته والمراد بالسكوت أنه فعل أحد أو قال شيئا في حضرته عليها ولم ينكر عليه بل سكت وقرر، ويقال للأول السنة القولية، وللثاني الفعلية، وللثالث التقريرية والسكوتية. باب السنة الأصل It is of four types: either the Companion narrates it as mursal, or the Tabi'i, or those after them of the next generation, or it is mursal from one aspect and not from another. The first is the first, second the second, third the third, fourth the fourth. According to the Muhaddithin, if the drop is from the beginning, i.e., from the author, it is Mu'allaq. Its forms include dropping the entire chain and saying: The Prophet said..., and dropping only the Companion, or dropping both the Tabi'i and Companion together. And also dropping his immediate teacher and attributing to the one above him. If the drop is from the end of the chain after the Tabi'i, it is Mursal, as when the Tabi'i says: The Prophet said such and such. Then either the drop is of two or more consecutively, it is Mu'dal, otherwise, i.e., if not two consecutively, or only one drop, or more than two but not consecutively, it is Munqati'. Musnad: the opposite of Mursal, as when the narrator says: So-and-so narrated to us from so-and-so from the Messenger of Allah. The Mursal from the Companion: he says: The Prophet said such and such, for example, without mentioning his teacher. This is if the Companion is narrating from another Companion; otherwise, Mursal from a Companion is inconceivable, as there is no intermediary between him and the Messenger of Allah. This is the first type. It is attributed to hearing and accepted by consensus, because his drop is of a Companion intermediary between him and... * All of them: a refutation of the misconception that tawatur is not specific to Sunnah because it is also found in the Book. He refutes it by saying 'all of them' and the result is that some investigations are found, but all of them are not found in it. Understand.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the Sunnah, the second source of Islamic law after the Qur'an. The author begins with a ruling: in the case of a traveler shortening prayer, there is no choice; it is determined. He supports this with an analogy (qiyas) involving a mudabbar slave (one whose manumission is deferred until the master's death). Just as a mudabbar committing a tort obligates the master to pay the lesser of its value or the blood-money because both are of the same type (property), so too the traveler's shortening and completing prayer are of the same type (both valid prayers), so the traveler must choose the easier (shortening) because choice between two different things would provide ease only if they were different, but here they are the same genus. He contrasts this with a regular slave, where the master has a genuine choice between handing over the slave or paying blood-money because they are different (person vs. property). This illustrates a usul principle: ease through choice only applies when the options are different in essence. The author then formally defines Sunnah linguistically and technically, distinguishing it from Hadith and Khabar. According to the Hanafi usul tradition, Sunnah includes the Prophet's statements, actions, and tacit approvals, as well as the statements and actions of the Companions (since they are a source of law). Hadith, in contrast, is restricted to the Prophet's statements. The term 'Khabar' is sometimes used for historical reports. The author also explains three types of Sunnah: qawli (verbal), fi'li (action), and taqriri/sukuti (tacit approval). Finally, he discusses the transmission categories: musnad (with a complete chain) and mursal (with a missing link). Mursal from a Companion is accepted by consensus because the missing Companion intermediary does not affect reliability. He details various forms of broken chains according to hadith terminology: mu'allaq, mursal, munqati', and mu'dal. The passage emphasizes that these technical discussions about chains are specific to Sunnah, not the Qur'an, because the Qur'an is transmitted mutawatir.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where the narrator drops one or more intermediaries between himself and the Prophet, e.g., a Tabi'i saying 'The Prophet said' without mentioning the Companion.
المسند (al-musnad): A hadith with a continuous chain of narrators up to the Prophet.
المعلق (al-mu'allaq): A hadith where the chain is dropped from the beginning (the author's side), e.g., 'The Prophet said...' without any chain.
المعضل (al-mu'dal): A hadith where two or more consecutive narrators are dropped from the chain.
المنقطع (al-munqati'): A hadith where the chain is broken non-consecutively, or only one narrator is dropped at any point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is mursal from a Companion accepted by Hanafis?
A) Because Companions are all trustworthy and the missing link is another Companion.
B) Because the Prophet directly taught all Companions.
C) Because the chain is still continuous if we consider the Companion as the authority.
D) Because the author of the text says so without reason.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mursal from a Companion is accepted as reliable evidence by consensus, while other broken chains require additional scrutiny.

The Principle of Determined Ease: Traveler's Prayer and the Mudabbar Analogy
Establishes the ruling of determined ease for traveler's prayer via mudabbar qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the principle that when two options are of the same genus, ease is determined (not chosen), by applying the Hanafi qiyas of the mudabbar slave to the traveler's shortening prayer.

Core Idea
When options are identical in genus, the easier option is mandatory, not a choice.

This lesson unpacks a complex qiyas (analogical reasoning) from the passage. The author argues that a traveler must shorten prayer (qasr) – it is not a free choice between shortening and completing. He supports this with an analogy to a mudabbar slave who commits a tort: the master must pay the lesser of value or blood-money because both are of the same type (property). Understanding this analogy is key to grasping how Hanafi usul uses qiyas to establish rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the traveler
The passage states: 'فصار أي ما ذكرنا من تعين القصر في حق المسافر' (So what we mentioned becomes determined shortening for the traveler). The ruling is that qasr is determined (تعين), not optional.
This contrasts with the opinion that the traveler may choose.
2
Understand the mudabbar slave analogy
A mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred to master's death) commits a tort. The master must pay the lesser of the slave's value or the blood-money (أرش). The author says this is because value and blood-money are of the same type (جنس واحد), so the easier option (the lesser) is determined.
If the options were different in type, the master would have a genuine choice.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that the two options (shortening and completing prayer) are of the same genus (متفقان في الجنس). Both are valid prayers; their essence does not differ. Thus, choosing between them does not provide additional ease.
In contrast, a regular slave and blood-money are different: one is a person, the other is property.
4
Apply the qiyas to the traveler's case
The analogy: asl (mudabbar case) has ruling that the lesser is determined; far' (traveler's prayer) has the same illa (same genus), so the ruling is that the easier (shortening) is determined. Hence the traveler must shorten, not choose.
This is an example of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).

In Shari'ah, it is applied to supererogatory acts of worship, the doing of which earns reward and the omission of which does not incur punishment. Also, it is applied to what emanated from the Prophet ﷺ other than the Qur'an. The difference between them (Sunnah and Hadith) is that Sunnah is applied to his statement, action, and tacit approval, and to the statements and actions of the Companions, while Hadith is applied specifically to his statement. Hence the author used the word Sunnah to include all. According to the Muhaddithin, Sunnah, Khabar, and Hadith are synonymous, each applied to his statement, action, and tacit approval, and to the statement and action of the Companion and Tabi'i and their tacit approval. Some restricted Hadith to Marfu' and Mawquf, since Maqtu' is only an Athar according to them. Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the Sunnah, the second source of Islamic law after the Qur'an. The author begins with a ruling: in the case of a traveler shortening prayer, there is no choice; it is determined. He supports this with an analogy (qiyas) involving a mudabbar slave (one whose manumission is deferred until the master's death). Just as a mudabbar committing a tort obligates the master to pay the lesser of its value or the blood-money because both are of the same type (property), so too the traveler's shortening and completing prayer are of the same type (both valid prayers), so the traveler must choose the easier (shortening) because choice between two different things would provide ease only if they were different, but here they are the same genus. He contrasts this with a regular slave, where the master has a genuine choice between handing over the slave or paying blood-money because they are different (person vs. property). This illustrates a usul principle: ease through choice only applies when the options are different in essence. The author then formally defines Sunnah linguistically and technically, distinguishing it from Hadith and Khabar. According to the Hanafi usul tradition, Sunnah includes the Prophet's statements, actions, and tacit approvals, as well as the statements and actions of the Companions (since they are a source of law). Hadith, in contrast, is restricted to the Prophet's statements. The term 'Khabar' is sometimes used for historical reports. The author also explains three types of Sunnah: qawli (verbal), fi'li (action), and taqriri/sukuti (tacit approval). Finally, he discusses the transmission categories: musnad (with a complete chain) and mursal (with a missing link). Mursal from a Companion is accepted by consensus because the missing Companion intermediary does not affect reliability. He details various forms of broken chains according to hadith terminology: mu'allaq, mursal, munqati', and mu'dal. The passage emphasizes that these technical discussions about chains are specific to Sunnah, not the Qur'an, because the Qur'an is transmitted mutawatir.

Key Terms
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbir).
القصر (al-qasr): Shortening the prayer from 4 rak'at to 2 rak'at while traveling.
الإتمام (al-itmam): Completing the prayer in full (4 rak'at) while traveling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the mudabbar analogy support the ruling that qasr is determined?
A) Because both the mudabbar and the traveler are in a state of travel.
B) Because in both cases, the options (value & blood-money; qasr & itmam) are identical in genus, so ease is determined in the lesser.
C) Because the mudabbar is an example of mercy, and so is the traveler.
D) Because the master always chooses the easier option.

Key Takeaway
When two permissible options are identical in genus, the easier option becomes wajib (determined) rather than a free choice.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate

Mursal and Musnad in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Defines and classifies Sunnah into Mursal and Musnad with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Mursal and Musnad hadith according to Hanafi usul, and explain the conditions under which Mursal is accepted as a legal proof.

Core Idea
Mursal from a trustworthy narrator is accepted in Hanafi usul and can be stronger than Musnad.

In Hanafi usul, the Sunnah is classified based on the completeness of its chain of transmission. This passage from a classical usul text defines Mursal and Musnad, and explains the unique Hanafi position that the Mursal of a trustworthy narrator is a valid proof and may even be preferred over Musnad. It also addresses internal and cross-madhhab disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Define Mursal and Musnad
Mursal is when the narrator omits the chain and says 'The Prophet said' directly; Musnad is when the full chain is mentioned.
2
Classify Mursal by generation
Identify the four types of Mursal: from a Companion, from a Follower, from a Follower of Followers, and partial Mursal.
3
Understand Hanafi acceptance of early Mursal
The Mursal of a Companion is accepted by consensus; the Mursal of a Follower of Followers is accepted and considered above Musnad.
4
Analyze the dispute on later Mursal
Al-Karkhi accepts Mursal from later generations due to continuing trustworthiness; Isa ibn Aban rejects due to corruption of the age.
If supported by trustworthy narrators, even later Mursal is accepted by consensus.

باب السنة
الأصل الثاني السنة

سبق ذكرها، فكانت السنة فرعاً للكتاب في بيان تلك الأقسام بأحكامها، وإنما هذا الباب لبيان ما يختص به السنن.
أي باب السنة
المرسل والمسند ]
فنقول: السنة نوعان مرسل ومسند، فالمرسل من الصحابي محمول على السماع ومن القرن الثاني وهم التابعون السنة فرعاً إلخ فلا حاجة إلى إيرادها في باب السنة مرةً أخرى يختص به السنن: ولم يوجد في الكتاب، كالبحث عن كيفية الاتصال والانقطاع ومحل الخبر وكيفية السماع والضبط والتبليغ، فهذه الأبحاث كلها لا توجد في الكتاب؛ لأنه مروي بخبر متواتر فقط. وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول : السنة باعتبار وصولها إلينا نوعان. مرسل: بأن يترك الراوي الوسائط التي بينه وبين النبي ويقول : قال النبي كذا، وهو على أربعة أقسام؛ لأنه إما يرسله الصحابي أو التابعي أو من دونهم من تبع التابعين، أو هو مرسل من وجه دون وجه، فالأول هو الأول، والثاني هو الثاني والثالث هو الثالث والرابع هو الرابع. وأما عند المحدثين فسقوط السند إن كان أوّله أي من المصنّف وهو المعلّق، ومن صوره أن يحذف جميع السند ويقول: قال النبي ، ومنها أن يحذف إلا الصحابي، أو إلا التابعي والصحابي معاً.
ومنها أن يحذف شيخه ويضيف إلى من فوقه، وإن كان السقوط من آخر السند بعد التابعي فهو المرسل بأن يقول التابعي: قال النبي كذا. ثم لا يخلو إما إن كان السقوط باثنين فصاعداً مع التوالي فهو المعضل، وإلا أي إن لم يكن السقوط باثنين مع التوالي، أو سقط واحد فقط أو أكثر من اثنين لكن بشرط عدم التوالي فهو المنقطع. ومسند وهو خلاف المرسل بأن يقول الراوي: حدثنا فلان عن فلان عن رسول الله . فالمرسل من الصحابي: بأن يقول: قال النبي كذا مثلا، ولايذكر شيخه. هذا إذا كان رواية الصحابي من صحابي آخر، وإلا فالإرسال عن الصحابي غير متصوّر ؛ إذ لا واسطة بينه وبين رسول الله . وهذا هو القسم الأول. محمول على السماع مقبول بالإجماع؛ لأن إرساله بإسقاط صحابي متوسط بينه وبين= النبي
وذلك الصحابي عدل، فليس هنا جهالة المسقط، فهذا الحديث المرسل مقبول بهذا الوجه، وإذا قال الصحابي: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال كذا أو فعل كذا، فهو مسند والثالث وهو تبع التابعين، وهذا هو القسم الثاني. وضح له الأمر أي ظهر للراوي واستبان له الإسناد فلذا ترك الإسناد.
فوق المسند عندنا، حتى يرجح هو عند التعارض بينه وبين المسند. وهذا القسم كما هو حجة ومقبول عندنا كذلك عند مالك محله وأحمد بن حنبل حاله في إحدي الروايتين عنه، وعند أكثر المتكلمين وعند أهل الظواهر، والشافعي محلله لا يقبل إلا إذا تأيد بحجة قطعية أو قياس صحيح أو تلقته الأمة بالقبول، أو عرف من حال المرسل أنه لا يروي إلا عن ثقة. وبالجملة إذا تأيد باقتران ما يتقوّى به فيُقبل وإلا لا؛ لأنه عند جهالة صفات الراوي لا يقبل حديثه، فعند جهالة صفاته وذاته فبالطريق الأولى. نحن نقول كلامنا في إرسال ثقة لو أسند حديثه إلى شخص يصدق في ذلك فلان يصدق في نسبته إلى النبي أولى.
لم يتضح له الأمر: أي أمر الحديث كمال الوضوح. ما تحمل عنه: أي يجعل حمله على من سمعه ويفرغ ذمته عن ذلك، فأما إذا اتضح عنده طريق الإسناد يقول بلا وسوسة: قال النبي كذا، ولما كان يرد أنه على هذا ينبغي أن يجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب كما يجوز بالمشهور والمتواتر، وذلك لأن المرسل لما كان فوق المسند، والمسند ثلاثة أقسام التواتر والمشهور والآحاد فإن لم يفق المرسل على جميع أقسامه فلا أقل من أن يفوق على أدون الأقسام وهو الآحاد ، فإذا زاد مرتبته على الآحاد فلحق بالمشهور؛ إذ لا واسطة بينهما، والمشهور يجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب دفعه بقوله: لكن هذا إلخ. فلم يجز الزيادة التي هي في معنى النسخ بمثله، فإنه يؤدّي إلى الزيادة على الكتاب بالرأي والاجتهاد وهو غير جائز بخلاف المشهور، فإن مزيَّته وقوته ليست بالاجتهاد بل بالنص. دون هؤلاء أي مراسيل من بعد الصحابة والتابعين وتبعهم، والمراسيل جمع المرسل، والياء للإشباع كما في الدراهيم. وفي "المغرب" أنه اسم جنس كالمناكير. اختلف فيه أي فيما ذكر من مراسيل من دون هؤلاء، وهذا قسم ثالث منه، فعند بعض مشايخنا مثل الكرخي يقبل؛ لأن ما هو علة لقبول مراسيل القرون الثلاثة توجد في من بعدهم، وهي الضبط والعدالة. وقال عيسى بن أبان لايُقبل؛ لأن بعد القرون الثلاثة زمان فسق، ولم يشهد بعد التهم. يروي الثقات مرسله إلخ فحينئذ يقبل مراسيله أيضاً بالاتفاق كمراسيل القرون الثلاثة.
Chapter of Sunnah. The second source: Sunnah. It was previously mentioned that the Sunnah is a branch of the Book in explaining those categories with their rulings, and this chapter is only for clarifying what is specific to the Sunnah. That is: 'Chapter of Sunnah' [meaning the commentary on the chapter]. 'Mursal and Musnad'. So we say: Sunnah is of two types: Mursal and Musnad. The Mursal from a companion is considered to be heard, and from the second century (i.e., the Followers) ... the Sunnah is a branch etc., so there is no need to mention it again in the chapter of Sunnah. What is specific to the Sunnah: and it is not found in the Book, like research on the manner of connection and disconnection, the locus of the report, the manner of hearing, accuracy, and conveying. All these investigations are not found in the Book because it is only transmitted by mutawatir reports. When you know this, we say: Sunnah, in terms of its transmission to us, is of two types: Mursal: by the narrator omitting the intermediaries between himself and the Prophet, saying 'The Prophet said such and such.' It is of four divisions: because either the Companion omits it, or the Follower, or those below them from the Followers of the Followers, or it is Mursal from one perspective and not another. The first is the first, the second is the second, the third is the third, and the fourth is the fourth. According to the hadith scholars, if the chain is dropped at its beginning (i.e., by the compiler), it is called Mu'allaq. Forms include: deleting the entire chain and saying 'The Prophet said', or deleting except the Companion, or deleting except the Follower and the Companion together. Also, deleting his shaykh and attributing to those above him. If the omission is from the end of the chain after the Follower, it is Mursal, such as when a Follower says 'The Prophet said such and such.' Then either the omission is of two or more consecutively, which is Mu'dal, or else (i.e., if it is not a consecutive omission of two, or a single omission, or more than two but not consecutive) it is Munqati'. Musnad is the opposite of Mursal, where the narrator says 'So-and-so narrated to us from so-and-so from the Messenger of Allah.' Thus, the Mursal from a Companion: when he says 'The Prophet said such and such' and does not mention his shaykh. This is if the Companion is transmitting from another Companion; otherwise, Mursal from a Companion is inconceivable because there is no intermediary between him and the Messenger of Allah. This is the first category. It is considered as heard and accepted by consensus, because his omission is dropping an intermediary Companion between him and the Prophet, and that Companion is trustworthy, so there is no unknown person omitted. So this Mursal hadith is accepted in this respect. If the Companion says 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say such and such' or 'do such and such', it is Musnad. The third (category) is the Follower of the Followers. This is the second category. The matter became clear to him, i.e., the chain became apparent and clear to the narrator, so he omitted the chain. It is above Musnad in our view, so that it is given preference when it conflicts with Musnad. This category, as it is a proof and accepted by us, is also accepted by Malik, Ahmad ibn Hanbal in one of the two narrations from him, and by most theologians and the literalists. As for al-Shafi'i, he does not accept it unless it is supported by a decisive proof, a valid analogy, or the ummah has received it with acceptance, or it is known from the Mursil that he only narrates from trustworthy sources. In short, if it is supported by something that strengthens it, it is accepted; otherwise, it is not, because when the qualities of the narrator are unknown, his hadith is not accepted. So when both his qualities and identity are unknown, it is even more so. We say: our discussion is about the Mursal of a trustworthy narrator; if he attributes his hadith to a person he is truthful about, then he is even more truthful in attributing it to the Prophet. 'The matter did not become clear to him': i.e., the matter of the hadith was not fully clear. 'What he transmitted' means he makes it a burden on the one he heard from and discharges his responsibility. When the chain becomes clear to him, he says without hesitation: 'The Prophet said such and such.' Since it might be objected that according to this, it should be permissible to add to the Book through it, just as it is permissible through the well-known (mashhur) and mutawatir, because the Mursal is above the Musnad, and the Musnad has three categories: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. If the Mursal does not surpass all its categories, at least it surpasses the lowest category, which is ahad. So if its rank is above ahad, it joins the mashhur, as there is no intermediary between them, and the mashhur permits addition to the Book. He refuted this by saying: 'But this...' so addition that is in the sense of abrogation is not permitted through it, because it would lead to addition to the Book by opinion and ijtihad, which is not permissible, unlike the mashhur, whose strength is not due to ijtihad but due to text. 'Other than these': i.e., the Mursal of those after the Companions, Followers, and their followers. 'Al-Marasil' is the plural of Mursal, and the ya is for prolongation as in 'al-darahim'. In 'al-Mughrib', it is a generic noun like 'al-manakir'. 'There is disagreement about it': i.e., about the Mursal of those after these generations. This is a third category. According to some of our shaykhs like al-Karkhi, it is accepted because the reason for accepting the Mursal of the first three generations (i.e., accuracy and trustworthiness) also exists in those after them. Isa ibn Aban said it is not accepted because after the first three generations is an age of corruption, and there is no safeguard against suspicion. 'If trustworthy narrators report his Mursal as they report his Musnad': then his Mursal is also accepted by consensus, like the Mursal of the first three generations.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the 'Chapter of Sunnah' from a usul al-fiqh work, explaining the classification of Sunnah into Mursal and Musnad. The author first clarifies that this chapter discusses what is specific to the Sunnah, distinct from the Qur'an, since the Sunnah is a branch of the Book. The Sunnah is divided into two types based on how it reaches us: Mursal (where the chain is omitted at some point) and Musnad (where the chain is complete). The Mursal is further divided into four categories depending on who omits the chain: a Companion, a Follower, a Follower of the Followers, or a Mursal from one perspective but not another. The author then distinguishes between the terminology of usul scholars and hadith scholars: the latter use terms like Mu'allaq, Mursal, Munqati', and Mu'dal with specific definitions. The text emphasizes that the Mursal of a Companion is accepted by consensus because the omitted narrator is known to be trustworthy. For the Mursal of a Follower of the Followers (third generation), the Hanafi school considers it above Musnad in strength, even to the point of preference in case of conflict. This view is shared by Malik and Ahmad but not by al-Shafi'i, who requires external support. The author then refutes a potential objection that if Mursal is stronger than Musnad, it could be used to abrogate the Qur'an; the response is that such addition is not allowed because it would be based on opinion and ijtihad, whereas the strength of mashhur and mutawatir is based on textual transmission. Finally, the passage addresses disagreement among Hanafi scholars about accepting Mursal from generations after the first three: al-Karkhi accepts it, while Isa ibn Aban rejects it. However, if the Mursal is reported by trustworthy narrators alongside the Musnad, it is accepted by consensus.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits some intermediaries between himself and the Prophet, saying 'The Prophet said' without giving a complete chain.
المسند (al-musnad): A hadith where the narrator states the full chain of transmission from himself back to the Prophet.
التابعي (al-tabi'i): A Follower: a person who met a Companion of the Prophet and died as a Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling on the Mursal of a Companion?
A) It is not accepted because of the missing link.
B) It is accepted by consensus because the omitted person is a trustworthy Companion.
C) It is accepted only if supported by a decisive proof.
D) It is accepted only from the first three generations.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts Mursal from trustworthy narrators and may prefer it over Musnad, but disagreement exists for later generations.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Acceptance of Mursal Hadith: Superiority Over Musnad and Conditions
Explaining the third type of Mursal hadith and its acceptance conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on mursal hadith, identify when it is accepted, and evaluate the objection regarding abrogation.

Core Idea
A reliable mursal is above musnad in strength but cannot abrogate the Quran.

In this passage, the author clarifies the Hanafi stance on mursal hadith, a narration with an omitted link. The text establishes that when the narrator is reliable, mursal is not only accepted but considered stronger than musnad. However, its strength derives from ijtihad, not textual certainty, so it cannot be used for abrogation. This lesson breaks down the reasoning and the inter-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of mursal mentioned
The text distinguishes mursal by the level of the omitted narrator: (1) when the chain is clear but omitted, (2) when the chain is unclear, (3) mursal from after the first three generations. Note which type is subject to disagreement.
2
State the Hanafi hierarchy: mursal above musnad
Understand why the Hanafis consider mursal stronger when the mursil is reliable. The text says it is 'above musnad' and given preference when conflicting.
This is a key difference from other schools.
3
Analyze the objection about abrogation
The text anticipates the objection: if mursal is above musnad, could it be used to add to the Quran? The answer is no, because its superiority comes from ijtihad, not from textual certainty.
The author refutes by distinguishing between text-based and ijtihad-based strength.
4
Compare the Shafi'i position and the Hanafi response
Shafi'i requires mursal to be supported by a categorical proof, sound analogy, or community acceptance. The Hanafi response argues that if the mursil is reliable, his omission of the chain does not weaken the hadith; his truthfulness in attributing to a person implies truthfulness in attributing to the Prophet a fortiori.
5
Examine the third category: mursal after the first three generations
There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: al-Karkhi accepts it, Isa ibn Aban rejects it. However, if reliable narrators transmit both the mursal and musnad versions, acceptance is by consensus.
This shows the nuanced conditions for acceptance.

باب السنة الأصل الثاني السنة والثالث على أنه وضح له الأمر واستبان له الإسناد وهو فوق المسند. فإن من أي هذا القسم من المرسل لم يتضح له الأمر نسبه إلى من سمعه منه؛ ليحمله ما تحمّل عنه، لكن هذا ضرب أي ذلك الحديث نوع مزية يثبت بالاجتهاد، فلم يجز النسخ بمثله، وأما مراسيل من دون هؤلاء فقد زيادة والرأي اختلف فيه، إلا أن يروي الثقات مرسله كما رووا مسنده، = النبي وذلك الصحابي عدل، فليس هنا جهالة المسقط، يتضح له الأمر: أي أمر الحديث كمال الوضوح. ما تحمل عنه: أي يجعل حمله على من سمعه ويفرغ ذمته عن ذلك، فأما إذا اتضح عنده طريق الإسناد يقول بلا وسوسة: قال النبي كذا، ولما كان يرد أنه على هذا ينبغي أن يجوز الأقسام وهو الآحاد ، فإذا زاد مرتبته على الآحاد فلحق بالمشهور؛ إذ لا واسطة بينهما، والمشهور يجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب دفعه بقوله: لكن هذا إلخ. فلم يجز الزيادة التي هي في معنى النسخ بمثله، فإنه يؤدّي مثل إرسال محمد بن الحسن وأمثاله وقال الشافعي له: لا أقبل إلا مراسيل سعيد المسيب له، فإني تتبعتها فوجدتها مسانيد. بن
Chapter of Sunnah, the second foundation. And the third: that it became clear to him and the chain became evident to him, and it is above the musnad. For whoever from this category of mursal does not have the matter clear to him, he attributes it to the one he heard it from, so that he may carry what he received. But this is a type of advantage established by ijtihad, so abrogation by its like is not permissible. As for the mursal of those after these, there is difference of opinion, except if the reliable narrators narrate its mursal as they narrate its musnad. And that companion is just, so there is no ignorance of the one who omitted, so this mursal hadith is accepted in this respect. If a companion says: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say such or do such, it is musnad. And the third is the follower of the followers, and this is the second category. 'It became clear to him' means it appeared to the narrator and the chain became evident, so he left the chain. It is above the musnad with us, such that it is given preference when conflicting with musnad. This category is accepted and is proof with us, similarly with Malik and Ahmad in one narration, and with most of the mutakallimun and the zahiris. As for al-Shafi'i, he does not accept it unless supported by a categorical proof, sound analogy, or acceptance by the ummah, or it is known that the mursil only narrates from reliable sources. In summary, if supported by what strengthens it, it is accepted; otherwise not. Because if the character of the narrator is unknown, his hadith is not accepted, so if both his character and identity are unknown, it is even more so. We say our discussion is about the mursal of a reliable person; if he attributes his hadith to someone he trusts, then he is truthful in attribution to the Prophet a fortiori. 'It did not become clear to him' means the matter of the hadith is not perfectly clear. 'What he received' means he makes it a burden from the one he heard and absolves himself. If the chain is clear to him, he says without hesitation: The Prophet said such. And because it might be objected that then it should be permissible to add to the Quran through it as through mashhur and mutawatir, because mursal is above musnad, and musnad has three divisions: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad; if not all, then at least it outweighs the lowest which is ahad, so it becomes like mashhur, and mashhur allows addition to the Quran. He refutes this by saying: but this is a type of advantage established by ijtihad, so abrogation by its like is not permissible, for it would lead to addition to the Quran by opinion and ijtihad, which is not permissible, unlike mashhur whose strength is from text not ijtihad. 'After these' means mursal of those after the companions, followers, and their followers. 'Difference of opinion' regarding what is mentioned of these mursals, which is a third category. According to some of our scholars like al-Karkhi, it is accepted because the cause for acceptance of mursal of the first three generations exists in those after them, namely precision and justice. Isa ibn Aban said it is not accepted because after the third generation is a time of transgression and accusations of lying. 'If reliable narrators narrate its mursal as they narrate its musnad, then it is accepted by consensus like the mursal of the first three generations.' The Prophet like the mursal of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and his peers. Al-Shafi'i said: I accept only the mursal of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, for I traced them and found them to be musnad. Ibn.

Commentary
This passage from the usul work discusses the third type of mursal hadith and its acceptance conditions. The author begins by stating that the third type of mursal is when the chain is unclear to the narrator, so he attributes it to the one he heard it from, but this is a type of advantage (maziyya) established by ijtihad, not by text, so abrogation by it is not permissible. Then he discusses the mursal of those after the first three generations, noting that there is disagreement. The Hanafi position is that if reliable narrators transmit both the mursal and the musnad versions, then acceptance is by consensus. The passage then explains that a companion's statement 'I heard the Prophet' is musnad, and the third type is from the followers of followers. The commentator elaborates that 'it became clear to him' means the narrator understood the chain, so he omitted it. This type is above musnad in the Hanafi school, so it is given preference when conflicting. Al-Shafi'i only accepts mursal if supported by evidence or if the mursil is known to only narrate from reliable sources. The Hanafi response is that we are discussing a reliable mursil; if he is trustworthy in attributing to a person, he is more so in attributing to the Prophet. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if mursal is above musnad, then it should allow addition to the Quran like mashhur. The answer is that mursal's strength comes from ijtihad, not text, so it cannot be used for abrogation. Finally, the passage covers the third category of mursal from those after the first three generations, where there is disagreement between al-Karkhi (acceptance) and Isa ibn Aban (rejection), but if reliable narrators confirm it, it is accepted by consensus. The example of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan's mursal is given, and al-Shafi'i's statement that he only accepts the mursal of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits one or more links in the chain, typically the companion or the follower, and directly attributes to the Prophet.
المسند (al-musnad): A hadith with a complete connected chain going back to a companion or the Prophet.
الاجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning using the tools of usul to derive rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a mursal hadith from a reliable narrator compared to a musnad hadith?
A) It is weaker than musnad.
B) It is equal to musnad.
C) It is stronger than musnad and can be used for abrogation.
D) It is stronger than musnad but cannot be used for abrogation.

Key Takeaway
A reliable mursal is stronger than musnad but cannot abrogate because its strength is ijtihadi, not textual.

Mutawatir Hadith: Definition and Conditions
Defining mutawatir and clarifying its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir hadith and identify its key conditions according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mutawatir hadith provides certain knowledge through a narrating group so large that collusion is impossible.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the authority of the Sunnah depends on the type of transmission. Mutawatir hadith yields certainty (qat'i), obligating both belief and action. Understanding its definition and conditions is foundational for distinguishing it from other categories like mashhur and ahad, which have different epistemological weight.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core definition
Identify that mutawatir is defined as a report by a group so numerous that collusion to lie is impossible, across all generations from the Prophet to the narrator.
Linguistically, tawatur means succession; technically, it refers to the quality of transmission.
2
Recognize the key condition: impossibility of collusion
The essence is not a specific number but that the group is large enough that collusion is rationally impossible. The Hanafi school does not fix a minimum number.
Some scholars suggested numbers (5, 40, etc.), but the majority view is that the criterion is the resulting necessary knowledge.
3
Note the additional conditions mentioned and their status
Justice ('adalah) and diversity of locations are mentioned but are not strict conditions for tawatur according to the majority. They are mentioned because they enhance certainty, not as prerequisites.
The condition that the large number persists in every generation (istimrar) is essential for the hadith to be mutawatir from beginning to end.

Source Text

عند العامة في التواتر، وإنما هي شرط في أخبار الآحاد وتباين أماكنهم أي تباعدها وهذا يشير إلى اشتراطه، وهو ليس بشرط عند الجمهور لحصول العلم بأخبار ساكني بلدة واحدة، وإنما ذكر المصنف هذه القيود؛ لأنها Mutawatir hadith and its ruling. And the musnad is divided into categories: mutawatir, which is reported by a group whose number cannot be counted and it is not imagined they collude in lying due to their large number, justice, and diversity of locations, and this condition continues until it reaches... The cause for absence of collusion mentioned earlier. And his examples, so the mursal of Muhammad and his musnad are accepted by reliable narrators. I say: mentioning Muhammad in the example is lenient, because he is in the third century, i.e., follower of followers by consensus. I do not accept the mursal of the followers and those after them. A note: The author did not mention the fourth type of mursal, which is mursal from one aspect and musnad from another. I say: it is accepted by the general scholars, because the mursal is silent about the state of the narrator while the musnad speaks, and silence does not oppose speech, so the aspect of isnad outweighs the aspect of irsal, like the hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian' narrated as musnad by Isra'il ibn Yunus and as mursal by Shu'bah. Abu Dawud no. 2085. When he finished with mursal and its rulings, he began on musnad. Three divisions: either it is transmitted by a group that cannot collude in lying, or not. In the first case, either all times are equal from the beginning of the report to the end, or it becomes so after the first century. The first is mutawatir, the second is mashhur. In the second case, it is khabar al-wahid. Linguistically, tawatur is succession one after another from watar. From it, the verse: 'Then We sent Our messengers in succession' (23:44), i.e., one after another. In terminology, it is a report of a group that gives by itself knowledge of its truthfulness. The author explained it by saying: it is what is reported by... not limiting the number is not a condition according to the majority, contrary to some who stipulated a number: five, seven, twelve, twenty, forty, seventy. Rather, whatever brings necessary knowledge is a sign of tawatur. And do not think to make this sentence an interpretation of his saying 'their number cannot be counted' so it agrees with the majority. 'And their justice' indicates stipulating justice, but it is not a condition for the general scholars in tawatur, rather it is a condition in ahad reports. 'And diversity of their locations' indicates stipulating it, but it is not a condition according to the majority because knowledge can be obtained from reports of residents of one town. The author only mentioned these restrictions because they are more conclusive of probability, not because they are real conditions. Since the purpose here is to explain the mutawatir from the Sunnah, not absolute mutawatir, he added another condition: 'that it continues to be connected', i.e., reported by a group whose number cannot be counted in each generation, such that all times are equal from the transmitter to the Prophet, even if that number is cut off in one generation... their number.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage begins by defining mutawatir hadith and then discusses its conditions. The author states that mutawatir is a type of musnad hadith. It is reported by a group so large that it is impossible for them to collude in lying, due to their large number, justice, and diverse locations, and this condition persists through all generations. The text then digresses into a note about an example, then returns to the definition. The commentator explains that the exact number is not a condition; what matters is that it produces necessary knowledge. The conditions of justice and diverse locations are not strictly necessary for tawatur according to the majority; they are mentioned because they strengthen certainty. The passage ends by adding that tawatur requires continuity of the large number in every generation up to the Prophet.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir): A hadith reported by a large number in every generation such that collusion is impossible, providing certain knowledge.
مشهور (mashhur): A hadith that becomes widely known after the first generation, but does not meet the mutawatir condition in the first generation.
خبر واحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith that does not meet the conditions of mutawatir or mashhur; it is reported by one or a few narrators and yields probability (zann).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The narrators must be just and from different locations.
C) The number of narrators must be such that collusion to lie is impossible.
D) It must be continuous until the Prophet's time, even if only one narrator remains.

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith is defined by the impossibility of collusion due to the sheer number of narrators in every generation, producing certain knowledge; specific numbers and conditions like justice are not strict requirements.

Acceptance of Mursal Hadith in Hanafi School
Discussion on acceptance of mursal hadith and its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mursal hadith, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the rule for conflicting mursal and musnad chains.

Core Idea
Hanafis accept mursal from trustworthy tabi'un; the musnad chain overrides when both exist.

The Hanafi school accepts mursal hadith from trustworthy tabi'un, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts acceptance to only Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. This passage clarifies the Hanafi position and introduces a fourth type of mursal — where one chain is mursal and another is musnad — and the rule that the musnad aspect prevails. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to evaluate hadith evidence in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage and pinpoint the Hanafi view (accept mursal from trustworthy tabi'un) and the Shafi'i view (only accept mursal of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab).
Note that the Hanafi position is attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand why Hanafis reject the Shafi'i restriction: they focus on the transmitter's reliability, not the generation.
The text also notes that Imam Muhammad's example was 'lenient' because he was from a later generation.
3
Apply the fourth type rule
Consider the case where a hadith is transmitted with both mursal and musnad chains. The rule is that the musnad chain overrides the mursal because it is 'speaking' (natiq) while the mursal is 'silent' (sakit).
Example: 'No marriage except with a guardian' — narrated as musnad by Isra'il and mursal by Shu'bah, with preference given to the musnad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السنة الأصل الثاني السنة مثل إرسال محمد بن الحسن وأمثاله وقال الشافعي له: لا أقبل إلا مراسيل سعيد المسيب له، فإني تتبعتها فوجدتها مسانيد. وأمثاله فمراسيل محمد ومسانيده عند الثقات مقبولة. أقول: ذكر محمد في المثال تسامح؛ لأنه في القرن الثالث أي تبع التابعين بالاتفاق. لا أقبل مراسيل التابعين ومن بعدهم. تنبيه: و لم يذكر المصنف القسم الرابع من المرسل، وهو مرسل من وجه ومسند من وجه آخر، فأقول: هو مقبول عند العامة؛ لأن المرسل ساكت عن حال الراوي والمسند ناطق والساكت لا يعارض الناطق، فيغلب وجه الإسناد على وجه الإرسال كحديث لا نكاح إلا بولي. أسنده إسرائيل بن يونس وأرسله شعبة. ابوداود رقم: ۲۰۸۵] ولما فرغ من المرسل وأحكامه شرع في المسند.
Chapter of Sunnah. The second source: the Sunnah. Like the mursal transmissions of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and similar ones. Al-Shafi'i said to him: I do not accept except the mursal of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, for I followed them and found them to be musnad. And the like: the mursal of Muhammad and his musnad are acceptable among trustworthy people. I say: Muhammad's mention is lenient, for he is in the third century, i.e., a follower of the tabi'un by consensus. I do not accept the mursal of tabi'un and those after them. Note: The author did not mention the fourth type of mursal, which is mursal from one aspect and musnad from another. I say: It is acceptable with the general public because the mursal is silent about the condition of the narrator, while the musnad speaks, and one who is silent does not contradict one who speaks, so the aspect of isnad overrides the aspect of irsal, such as the hadith 'No marriage except with a guardian'. Isra'il ibn Yunus narrated it as musnad, and Shu'bah narrated it as mursal. Abu Dawud no. 2085. When he finished with mursal and its rulings, he began with musnad.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the acceptance of mursal hadith (a hadith where the link from the tabi'i to the Prophet is missing). The Hanafi position, exemplified by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, accepts mursal hadith from trustworthy tabi'un and those after them, as long as the transmitter is reliable. Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, only accepts mursal from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, claiming he verified that his mursal reports were actually musnad. The commentator clarifies that Imam Muhammad's example was lenient because he was from the third generation. Then a note discusses a fourth type of mursal where one chain is irsal and another is isnad; in such cases, the musnad aspect prevails, as in the marriage guardian hadith.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the tabi'i (follower) narrates directly from the Prophet, omitting the companion link.
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete chain of transmission, with every link named.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hanafis accept mursal hadith from trustworthy tabi'un, and when chains conflict, the musnad overrides the mursal.

Definition and Conditions of Mutawatir Hadith
Defining mutawatir and its epistemological implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir hadith, state its three conditions, and distinguish the Hanafi view that it yields necessary knowledge from the view that it yields inferential knowledge.

Core Idea
Mutawatir hadith gives certainty like seeing—no calculation, just irresistible knowledge.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of mutawatir as a report transmitted by a group whose collusion on a lie is impossible, yielding necessary (daruri) knowledge. We will examine the conditions, the epistemological debate, and why the Hanafi school holds that such knowledge is immediate, not inferential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-fold division of khabar
In the source text, the author divides reports into three types based on tawatur. Recognize mutawatir, mashhur, and khabar wahid.
The division hinges on whether collusion is impossible and whether the tawatur is continuous from the start.
2
Locate the linguistic and technical definitions
Find the linguistic root 'w-t-r' and the Quranic usage. Then identify the technical definition: 'a report of a group that by itself yields knowledge of its truthfulness'.
The Quranic verse is used to show the meaning of succession.
3
Analyze the conditions: strict or probabilistic?
The text mentions number, integrity (adalah), and geographical diversity. Note that these are not strict conditions for the majority; they are means to exclude possibility of collusion.
The true conditions are three: numbers preventing collusion, basis in sense, and continuity across layers.
4
Determine the epistemological claim
The central debate: does mutawatir yield necessary (daruri) knowledge or inferential (nazari)? The Hanafi position is necessary, proven by universal human experience.
The proof from common experience: we have certainty about distant lands through reports without reasoning.
5
Trace the Hanafi proof and three correct conditions
The author gives three conditions for tawatur, all relating to the informants. Use the rational proof from the text to support the Hanafi view.
Condition 1: numbers preventing collusion; 2: reliance on sense; 3: equality in all layers.

It has three divisions; because it is either transmitted by a group whose collusion upon lying is impossible, or not. On the first, either all times are equal from the beginning of that report to the end of the transmitter, or not, but becomes so after the first century. On the first branch it is mutawatir, on the second it is mashhur, and on the second branch it is khabar wahid. Tawatur linguistically is the succession of things one after another from watar, from His saying: 'Then We sent Our messengers consecutively' (23:44), i.e., one after another. Technically, it is a report of a group that by itself yields knowledge of its truthfulness. The author explains it by saying: 'it is what is transmitted by...' etc. Their number is not countable, and uncountability is not a condition according to the majority, contrary to some who stipulated a number, some said five, some seven, some twelve, some twenty, some forty, some seventy, but whatever yields necessary knowledge is a sign of tawatur. Do not think that this sentence is an interpretation of 'their number is not countable', thus agreeing with the majority. 'And their integrity' refers to stipulating integrity, but it is not a condition according to the general public in tawatur; it is rather a condition in khabar al-ahad. 'And the diversity of their places' i.e., their separation, and this refers to stipulating it, but it is not a condition for the majority because knowledge can be obtained from reports of residents of one town. Rather, the author mentioned these restrictions because they cut off probability, not because they are real conditions. Since the purpose here is to explain mutawatir from the Sunnah, not absolute mutawatir, he added another restriction: 'until it reaches' etc., i.e., it is transmitted by a group whose number is not countable layer by layer, such that all times are equal from the transmitter to the Prophet, even if that number is cut off in a century. And that is like the transmission of the Qur'an, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of zakat, and similar things. And it (mutawatir) yields certain knowledge like eyewitness, necessary knowledge. That is, certain knowledge is obtained from mutawatir without acquisition and consideration, just as it is obtained from witnessing, because it is obtained for those who are unable to consider, like children. The detailed position: the Brahmins and Samaniyyah said that mutawatir does not yield certainty at all but yields only conjecture, while the majority holds that it yields certainty. Then they differed: is it necessary or theoretical? The majority say it is necessary. Abu al-Qasim al-Ka'bi, Abu al-Husayn al-Basri of the Mu'tazila, and Abu Bakr al-Daqqaq of the Shafi'is said it is inferential, i.e., theoretical. Al-Ghazali said it is a third type. Al-Murtada and al-Amidi withheld. Our proof: we find in ourselves necessary knowledge of distant lands and Egypt just as we find knowledge of physical things, with no difference between them, and that is only through reports. And because if it were theoretical, it would need arrangement of premises, but the necessary is lacking since it is obtained by those who are not able to do that, as we said. Know that the correct conditions of tawatur are three, all relating to the informants: first, their number reaches such density that prevents agreement and collusion upon lying habitually; second, they are based on sense-experience, because in the case of the origination of the world it does not give certainty; third, that such tawatur is equal in all layers.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage defines mutawatir hadith as a transmission by a large group that cannot collude on a lie, and it yields necessary knowledge. The commentary elaborates on the conditions: uncountability is not a strict condition but a means; integrity and geographical diversity are not essential but help exclude possibility. The epistemological debate is covered: most scholars say mutawatir gives necessary knowledge (like seeing), while some say it is inferential. The Hanafi position is that it is necessary, proven by common human experience. Three conditions are listed: massive numbers preventing collusion, reliance on sense, and continuity across generations.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir): A hadith reported by a group whose collusion on a lie is impossible at every level, yielding necessary knowledge.
علم ضروري (ilm daruri): Knowledge that is immediate and unavoidable, like sense-perception.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A report that does not reach the level of tawatur and yields only probable knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, which of the following is NOT a true condition for tawatur?
A) The narrators must be numerous enough to prevent collusion
B) The narrators must be from different geographical regions
C) The narrators must be upright (adl)
D) The transmission must be continuous across all layers

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith yields necessary certainty, and its three conditions (numerousness preventing collusion, sense-based reporting, and continuity across layers) make it a cornerstone of Islamic epistemological certainty.

Definition and Ruling of Mashhur Hadith
Defining mashhur and proving its authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mashhur hadith and distinguish it from mutawatir and ahad by applying the Hanafi time-and-transmitter criteria.

Core Idea
A mashhur hadith is a single-chain report that earned early fame in the first two centuries, giving it near-certain authority.

In Hanafi usul, the authority of a hadith depends on its transmission history. This lesson defines the mashhur category, which sits between mutawatir and ahad. You will learn why early fame up to the second century matters and how the Prophet's praise of the early generations elevates mashhur reports above ordinary ahad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first line: mashhur is originally ahad (single-chain) but later spread so that it is narrated by a group impossible to collude on lying. Note the key elements: original ahad, later wide transmission by trustworthy narrators.
The phrase 'لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب' is similar to tawatur conditions but specific to the second and third generations.
2
Understand the time restriction
The text explicitly restricts mashhur to reports that became famous in the first or second century. If fame occurs later, even if widespread, it is not called mashhur. Example: many reports became known due to later writing but do not qualify.
Why first two centuries? Because those generations are praised by the Prophet.
3
Recognize the objection
An imagined objection: if mashhur was ahad in the first century, how can it be preferred over a regular ahad? Both were unknown in the first century.
This objection tests understanding of why mashhur gets special status.
4
Analyze the response
The author rebuts by pointing to the transmitters of the second and third centuries: they are from the best generations, trustworthy imams not accused of falsehood. Their collective acceptance gives the hadith added weight.
The hadith 'Khair al-qurun' is cited as proof for reliability of those generations.
5
Apply the distinction
Now classify a given hadith: Is it ahad? Did it become famous in the first two centuries? If yes, it is mashhur; if only later famous, it remains ahad.
Practice with a hadith like 'Innama al-a'mal bi-nniyat' which is mashhur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشهور وهو ما كان من الآحاد في الأصل ثم انتشر، فصار ينقله قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب، وهم القرن الثاني ومن بعدهم، وأولئك قوم ثقات أئمةٌ لا يتهمون. إنما قيّد باشتهاره في القرن الأول والثاني؛ لأنه لو لم يشتهر في هذين القرنين بل في القرون التي بعدهما لا يسمّى مشهوراً. ألا ترى أن عامة الأخبار اشتهرت في هذا الزمان لكثرة التدوين، ولكن لا يقال لها مشهور. ولما كان يتوهّم أن الخبر المشهور على ما قلتم إنما اشتهر بعد القرن الأول فما وجه ترجيحه على الآحاد؛ لأنه أيضا كان غير مشهور في القرن الأول، وإنما العبرة بهذا القرن؛ إذ هو منشأ ذلك دفعه بقوله: وأولئك إلخ. وأولئك أهل القرن الثاني والثالث الذين نقلوه لايتهمون بالافتراء والكذب؛ لأنه عليه قال: 'خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم' [البخاري، رقم: ٦٦٥٨].
And the mashhur: it is what was originally ahad, then spread, so that it is transmitted by a group concerning whom collusion on lying is not imagined, and they are the second century and after them, and those are trustworthy people, imams, not accused. He restricted it to its fame in the first and second centuries because if it did not become famous in these two centuries but in later centuries, it would not be called mashhur. Do you not see that most reports became famous in this time due to much writing, but they are not called mashhur? And when it is imagined that the mashhur report according to your statement became famous only after the first century, what is the basis for preferring it over ahad? Because it too was not famous in the first century. But the criterion is this century, for it is its origin. He refuted this by saying: 'And those are the people of the second and third centuries who transmitted it, not accused of falsehood and lying', because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' [Bukhari no. 6658]
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage defines mashhur hadith as one that was originally a single-chain report but later spread to be transmitted by many in later generations, specifically the second century onwards. The key is that it must have become well-known in the first and second centuries; fame after that does not confer the status of mashhur. The commentary addresses a potential objection: why prefer mashhur over ahad since both were not famous in the first century? The answer is that the transmitters of the second and third centuries are the best generations, as per the hadith, and thus not accused of lying. This gives mashhur higher authority than a regular ahad hadith.

Key Terms
مشهور (mashhur): A hadith that was originally ahad but became widely transmitted in the first and second centuries.
آحاد (ahad): A hadith that does not meet the conditions of tawatur or mashhur; single-chain report.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require that a mashhur hadith must have become famous in the first or second century?
A) Because later fame is unreliable.
B) Because the transmitters of those centuries are from the best generations not accused of lying.
C) Because hadiths were not written down later.
D) Because the Prophet himself commanded it.

Key Takeaway
A mashhur hadith is an ahad report that achieved early fame in the first two centuries, making it authoritative due to the reliability of the early generations.

Mashhur Hadith: Definition and Epistemological Status
Defines mashhur hadith and its epistemological category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a mashhur hadith by its definitional criteria and explain its epistemological status (ilm tuma'niyyah) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mashhur gives tranquil knowledge (ilm tuma'niyyah) – between certainty and mere probability.

In Hanafi usul, hadith is classified into three categories: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. The mashhur holds a unique intermediate position. This lesson unpacks its precise definition and the kind of knowledge it provides, which is not full certainty (like mutawatir) but stronger than a solitary report.

Guided Path
1
State the three hadith categories in Hanafi usul
Identify mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad with key features. This provides the framework.
Focus on the Hanafi tripartite division, not the Shafi'i (which only has mutawatir and ahad).
2
Define mashhur technically
State that it was originally ahad but became widespread through reliable transmitters in the second and third centuries.
The definition hinges on the timing of its spread (early centuries) and the character of transmitters.
3
Analyze the epistemological claim
Explain that mashhur yields ilm tuma'niyyah (tranquil knowledge) – a degree of certainty that is below necessary knowledge but above mere probability. Contrast with mutawatir (certainty) and ahad (speculative).
The Hanafi view is that the denier of a mashhur is misguided but not a disbeliever, unlike the denier of mutawatir.
4
Recall the proof for this status
The text cites the Prophet's praise of the early generations (the best of centuries) as the basis for trusting the transmitters of mashhur.
This is not a chain-based proof but a general trust in the community.
