[رقم: ٦٣٩] قال أحمد: ليس في قلبي من المسح شيء فيه أربعون حديثا عن أصحاب رسول الله ، ما رفعوا وما وقفوا. وروى ابن المنذر في آخرين عن الحسن البصري، قال حدثني سبعون رجلا من أصحاب رسول الله الله أنه عليها مسح على الخفين كذا في فتح القدير ". أقول: على هذا حديث المسح متواتر المعنى، وليس بمشهور؛ =
* قيل: القائل مولانا عبد العلي بحر العلوم في شرح "المسلم".
Chapter of the Sunnah. The second source: the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, such as the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of zakat, and the like. [Section: The Famous Hadith and its Ruling] And indeed it necessitates knowledge of certainty similar to direct observation, as necessary knowledge. The mashhur (famous) is that which was originally ahad (solitary) then spread, so that it is transmitted by a group about whom it is not imagined that they conspired to lie, and they are the people of the second century and after them, and those are trustworthy leaders who are not accused. ... (continues) ... So by their testimony and affirmation it becomes like mutawatir, until al-Jassas said: it is one of the two divisions of mutawatir. And Isa ibn Aban said: its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever, and that is the correct position with us; because that mashhur report by the testimony of the predecessors becomes a proof for acting upon it like mutawatir, so addition to the Book of Allah is valid through it, and that is abrogation according to us, such as the addition of stoning and wiping over the khuffs. ...
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the classification of hadith into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad, focusing on the definition and authority of the mashhur (famous) hadith. The author begins by stating that the second source (after the Quran) is the Sunnah, and then delves into the types. The mashhur hadith is defined as that which was originally reported by a few (ahad) but later became widespread, transmitted by a group whose collusion on lying is inconceivable. Importantly, this group includes the trustworthy, upright scholars of the second and third centuries. The text then explains the conditions for tawatur (mass transmission): numbers that preclude collusion, reliance on sense perception, and equality in all generations. There is a discussion on whether mutawatir gives necessary knowledge (daruri) or acquired (nadari). The majority hold it is necessary, but some like Abu al-Qasim al-Ka'bi consider it inferential. The author argues for necessary knowledge by pointing out that we find in ourselves necessary knowledge of distant lands just as of physical objects, even without reasoning, and if it were theoretical, it would require premises not available to all. Moving to the mashhur, the text clarifies that it does not reach the level of mutawatir in the first generation, but due to the unimpeachable character of later transmitters (second and third generations, praised by the Prophet as 'the best of generations'), it attains a status close to mutawatir. This leads to a key dispute: can the mashhur hadith add to or abrogate the Quran? The author presents multiple views. Al-Jassas considers mashhur one of two types of mutawatir, thus giving certain knowledge. Isa ibn Aban holds it is below mutawatir but above ahad, giving tranquil knowledge (ilm tuma'niyyah) such that its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever; it allows addition to the Quran but not abrogation. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that of Isa ibn Aban. The passage then explains that addition via mashhur is permissible because it is partly mutawatir and partly ahad: from one perspective it is like tawatur (due to its widespread acceptance), from another like ahad (since its origin was solitary). Two examples are given: (1) the addition of stoning (rajm) for the married adulterer to the Quranic verse prescribing one hundred lashes for both single and married, and (2) the addition of wiping over leather socks (masah ala al-khuffayn) instead of washing the feet in a state of wudu while wearing them. The text notes a potential objection: both examples are actually mutawatir in meaning, not merely mashhur, according to some authorities like Fath al-Qadir. The author concludes with a remark that the hadith of wiping is mutawatir in meaning, not just mashhur. This nuanced discussion highlights the Hanafi methodology in dealing with the authority of hadith and its relationship with the Quran.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): Report transmitted by an overwhelming number in every generation, giving necessary knowledge.
المشهور (al-mashhur): Report originally ahad but became widespread in early centuries via trustworthy transmitters, giving tranquil knowledge.
الآحاد (al-ahad): Report that does not reach the level of tawatur or shuhrah, narrated by one or a few.
علم الطمأنينة (ilm al-tuma'niyyah): Tranquil knowledge: a degree of certainty sufficient for action but not absolute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence for rejecting a mashhur hadith according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) The person becomes a disbeliever (kafir).
B) The person is misguided (dall) but not a disbeliever.
C) The person is a sinner (fasiq) but remains a believer.
D) The person is excused as ignorant.

Key Takeaway
The mashhur hadith in Hanafi usul is an independent category between mutawatir and ahad, providing tranquil knowledge (ilm tuma'niyyah) such that its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever.

Legal Authority of Mashhur: Addition and Abrogation
Explains the legal authority of mashhur hadith to add to the Quran, with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a mashhur hadith can add to (ziyadah) the Quran but cannot abrogate (naskh) it, and illustrate with the examples of stoning and wiping over socks.

Core Idea
Mashhur hadith adds to the Quran but never abrogates it.

A crucial controversy in usul is whether a hadith can add an extra ruling to the Quranic text. Hanafis distinguish between addition (ziyadah) and abrogation (naskh). The mashhur hadith, due to its intermediate status, can supplement the Quran but cannot repeal its rulings. This lesson examines the reasoning and the classic examples of stoning for the married adulterer and wiping over socks.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi rule on ziyadah via mashhur
The rule: A mashhur hadith can add an additional legal element to the Quranic text, such as specifying a condition or adding a penalty. This is allowed because mashhur has a level of certainty above ahad.
The addition must be a 'statement from one aspect' – like specifying a general or restricting a mutlaq.
2
Distinguish ziyadah from naskh
Naskh (abrogation) replaces a Quranic ruling. Only mutawatir can abrogate the Quran. Ziyadah is not naskh; it is an addition that clarifies or supplements without contradicting the Quran's core.
The text says: 'ziyadah bayan min wajh' – addition from one aspect, not pure naskh.
3
Apply to the example of stoning (rajm)
The Quran says: 'The fornicator and fornicatress, flog each one of them a hundred lashes.' (24:2) This applies absolutely. The mashhur hadith adds stoning for the married (muhsan) offender. This is ziyadah because it does not negate the lashing but adds a punishment for a specific category.
Some scholars argued this hadith is actually mutawatir in meaning, but the example illustrates the principle.
4
Apply to the example of wiping over socks (masah ala al-khuffayn)
The Quran commands washing the feet to the ankles (5:6). The mashhur hadith permits wiping over leather socks when wearing them in a state of wudu. This restricts the general command to wash, thus adding a concession.
This is also considered ziyadah: an addition to the general ruling.

ومثل زيادة
بمنزلة المتواتر: بخلاف الأحاد حيث لم يحصل له هذه المرتبة. أحد قسمي المتواتر : فيبثت به علم اليقين لكن بطريق الاستدلال، وإليه ذهب جماعة من أصحابنا. وقال عيسى بن أبان من أصحابنا: إنه دون المتواتر وفوق خبر الواحد، يوجب علم طمانية لا علم يقين حتى يضلّل جاحده ولا يكفر، ويجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب، ولا يجوز به النسخ مطلقاً، وإليه ذهب كثير من المحققين، وقال بعض أصحاب الشافعي له: إنه ملحق بخبر الواحد فلا يفيد إلا الظن وهو: أي الزيادة، وتذكير الضمير باعتبار الخبر. عندنا أعلم أن الزيادة لو كانت بياناً محضا كبيان التفسير لجازت بالمتواتر والمشهور والأحاد، ولو كانت نسخاً محضا لم يجز إلا بالمتواتر لاشتراط المساواة فيه، ولو كانت بياناً من وجه من حيث ترفع الإطلاق وتبدله بالتقييد جازت بالمشهور؛ لأنه متواتر من وجه وآحاد من وجه نظراً إلى الجهتين. وذلك: أي الزيادة على الكتاب بالخبر المشهور. زيادة الرجم في حق المحصن على الكتاب، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿والزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ (النور: ۲)، فإن في هذه الأمة حد الزنا مائة جلدة مطلقاً، أي سواء كان الزاني محصناً أو لا، ولكن زيد عليه الرجم في حق المحصن بالخبر المشهور، وهو قوله : " والثيب بالثيب جلدة مائة والرجم". رواه مسلم عن عبادة بن الصامت [رقم: ٤٤١٤] وروى غيره من غير واحد من أصحاب النبي الرحم في حق المحصن. ولذا قيل : في هذا التمثيل نظر، فإن ثبوت الرحم متواتر المعنى كما صرّح به في "فتح القدير". والمسح على الخفين لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَيْنِ ﴾ (المائدة: (٦) ، يوجب الغسل عموماً، سواء كان حالة التخفف أو غيرها ولكن زيد عليه المسح في حالة التخفّف، وخص هذه الحالة عن الغسل بالخبر المشهور وهو ما روى على أنه جعل رسول الله له ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن للمسافر، ويوماً وليلة للمقيم. رواه مسلم. [رقم: ٦٣٩] قال أحمد: ليس في قلبي من المسح شيء فيه أربعون حديثا عن أصحاب رسول الله ، ما رفعوا وما وقفوا. وروى ابن المنذر في آخرين عن الحسن البصري، قال حدثني سبعون رجلا من أصحاب رسول الله الله أنه عليها مسح على الخفين كذا في فتح القدير ". أقول: على هذا حديث المسح متواتر المعنى، وليس بمشهور؛ =
* قيل: القائل مولانا عبد العلي بحر العلوم في شرح "المسلم".
Chapter of the Sunnah. The second source: the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, such as the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of zakat, and the like. [Section: The Famous Hadith and its Ruling] And indeed it necessitates knowledge of certainty similar to direct observation, as necessary knowledge. The mashhur (famous) is that which was originally ahad (solitary) then spread, so that it is transmitted by a group about whom it is not imagined that they conspired to lie, and they are the people of the second century and after them, and those are trustworthy leaders who are not accused. ... (continues) ... So by their testimony and affirmation it becomes like mutawatir, until al-Jassas said: it is one of the two divisions of mutawatir. And Isa ibn Aban said: its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever, and that is the correct position with us; because that mashhur report by the testimony of the predecessors becomes a proof for acting upon it like mutawatir, so addition to the Book of Allah is valid through it, and that is abrogation according to us, such as the addition of stoning and wiping over the khuffs. ...
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the classification of hadith into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad, focusing on the definition and authority of the mashhur (famous) hadith. The author begins by stating that the second source (after the Quran) is the Sunnah, and then delves into the types. The mashhur hadith is defined as that which was originally reported by a few (ahad) but later became widespread, transmitted by a group whose collusion on lying is inconceivable. Importantly, this group includes the trustworthy, upright scholars of the second and third centuries. The text then explains the conditions for tawatur (mass transmission): numbers that preclude collusion, reliance on sense perception, and equality in all generations. There is a discussion on whether mutawatir gives necessary knowledge (daruri) or acquired (nadari). The majority hold it is necessary, but some like Abu al-Qasim al-Ka'bi consider it inferential. The author argues for necessary knowledge by pointing out that we find in ourselves necessary knowledge of distant lands just as of physical objects, even without reasoning, and if it were theoretical, it would require premises not available to all. Moving to the mashhur, the text clarifies that it does not reach the level of mutawatir in the first generation, but due to the unimpeachable character of later transmitters (second and third generations, praised by the Prophet as 'the best of generations'), it attains a status close to mutawatir. This leads to a key dispute: can the mashhur hadith add to or abrogate the Quran? The author presents multiple views. Al-Jassas considers mashhur one of two types of mutawatir, thus giving certain knowledge. Isa ibn Aban holds it is below mutawatir but above ahad, giving tranquil knowledge (ilm tuma'niyyah) such that its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever; it allows addition to the Quran but not abrogation. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that of Isa ibn Aban. The passage then explains that addition via mashhur is permissible because it is partly mutawatir and partly ahad: from one perspective it is like tawatur (due to its widespread acceptance), from another like ahad (since its origin was solitary). Two examples are given: (1) the addition of stoning (rajm) for the married adulterer to the Quranic verse prescribing one hundred lashes for both single and married, and (2) the addition of wiping over leather socks (masah ala al-khuffayn) instead of washing the feet in a state of wudu while wearing them. The text notes a potential objection: both examples are actually mutawatir in meaning, not merely mashhur, according to some authorities like Fath al-Qadir. The author concludes with a remark that the hadith of wiping is mutawatir in meaning, not just mashhur. This nuanced discussion highlights the Hanafi methodology in dealing with the authority of hadith and its relationship with the Quran.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): Adding a legal ruling to the Quranic text via mashhur hadith, e.g., stoning as an additional penalty.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation: the replacement of a Quranic ruling by another revealed text. Hanafis require mutawatir for naskh of the Quran.
المحصن (al-muhsan): A person who is married and has had lawful sexual relations (so the stoning penalty applies).
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock worn to protect the feet; wiping over it is permitted during wudu according to the mashhur hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi classification of the addition of stoning for a married adulterer via the mashhur hadith?
A) It is an abrogation (naskh) of the Quranic verse.
B) It is an addition (ziyadah) that specifies the general Quranic ruling.
C) It is a rejection of the Quranic punishment.
D) It is a separate ruling with no relation to the Quran.

Key Takeaway
A mashhur hadith can add an extra ruling (ziyadah) to the Quranic text, exemplified by stoning for the married adulterer and wiping over socks, but it cannot abrogate (naskh) the Quran.

The Epistemological Status of Mashhur Hadith
Defining mashhur hadith and the dispute over its certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three epistemological positions on mashhur hadith and apply the Hanafi view that it yields 'ilm al-tuma'nina.

Core Idea
Mashhur hadith gives satisfactory knowledge (tuma'nina), not certainty; its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever.

This passage explores the debated epistemological weight of mashhur hadith within Hanafi usul, contrasting it with mutawatir and ahad. It presents two Hanafi views—al-Jassas equating it with mutawatir via inference, and Isa ibn Aban placing it between mutawatir and ahad—and the Shafi'i view equating it with ahad. Understanding this helps grasp how Hanafis justify actions like stoning as addition to the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions on mashhur
Determine what al-Jassas, Isa ibn Aban, and some Shafi'is say about the epistemological status of mashhur hadith.
Al-Jassas: 'ilm al-yaqin bi al-istidlal; Isa ibn Aban: 'ilm al-tuma'nina; Shafi'i: zann.
2
Analyze the basis for each position
Note the dalil: al-Jassas relies on the witness of the salaf to equate with mutawatir; Isa ibn Aban differentiates because transmission is not tawatur; Shafi'is consider it ahad.
The Hanafi concept of 'witness of the salaf' (shahadat al-salaf) is central.
3
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why Isa ibn Aban's view is considered sahih by the muhaqqiqun, and what practical implications follow (no takfir, ziyadah allowed, naskh not allowed).
The text says 'wa huwa al-sahih 'indana'.
4
Apply the distinction to a furu' example
Consider the addition of stoning (rajm) as a ruling derived from mashhur hadith. How does the classification affect its binding force?
Hanafis accept rajm as a hadd punishment because it is based on mashhur, not ahad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصار بشهادتهم وتصديقهم بمنزلة المتواتر، حتى قال الجصاص: إنه أحد قسمي المتواتر، وقال عيسى بن أبان يضلّل جاحده ولا يكفر، وهو الصحيح عندنا؛ لأن ذلك الخبر المشهور بشهادة السلف صار حجة للعمل به بمنزلة المتواتر، فصحت الزيادة به وهم التابعون وتبعهم على كتاب الله تعالى، وهو نسخ عندنا، وذلك مثل زيادة الرجم والمسح على الخفين. معنى بمنزلة المتواتر: بخلاف الأحاد حيث لم يحصل له هذه المرتبة. أحد قسمي المتواتر: فيثبت به علم اليقين لكن بطريق الاستدلال، وإليه ذهب جماعة من أصحابنا. وقال عيسى بن أبان من أصحابنا: إنه دون المتواتر وفوق خبر الواحد، يوجب علم طمأنينة لا علم يقين حتى يضلّل جاحده ولا يكفر، ويجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب، ولا يجوز به النسخ مطلقاً، وإليه ذهب كثير من المحققين، وقال بعض أصحاب الشافعي له: إنه ملحق بخبر الواحد فلا يفيد إلا الظن
It became, through their witness and affirmation, like mutawatir, until al-Jassas said: it is one of the two types of mutawatir. And Isa ibn Aban said: its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever, and that is the correct view with us. Because that mashhur report, by the witness of the predecessors, became a proof for acting upon it, like mutawatir, so addition (ziyadah) is valid through it. And the followers and their followers acted upon it from the Book of Allah, and it is abrogation (naskh) with us, such as the addition of stoning and wiping over khuffs. Meaning 'like mutawatir': unlike ahad reports which have not attained this rank. 'One of the two types of mutawatir': it establishes knowledge of certainty, but through inference (istidlal), and a group of our companions went to that. And Isa ibn Aban, from our companions, said: it is below mutawatir and above khabar al-wahid; it necessitates knowledge of tranquility (tuma'nina), not knowledge of certainty, so its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever. Addition to the Book is permissible through it, but abrogation is absolutely not permissible through it, and many of the investigators went to that. And some of al-Shafi'i's companions said: it is attached to khabar al-wahid, so it only yields conjecture (zann).
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage defines mashhur hadith and discusses its epistemological weight. The commentator explains that because the mashhur report was witnessed and affirmed by the early generations (the Companions and Followers), it attains the status of mutawatir in terms of being a proof for action, but not necessarily in certainty. Two main Hanafi positions are presented: al-Jassas considers it a type of mutawatir that gives certainty through reasoning (istidlal), while Isa ibn Aban holds it gives only 'ilm al-tuma'nina (satisfactory knowledge) not 'ilm al-yaqin (certainty). The latter view is deemed correct (sahih) in the madhhab. Consequently, a denier of mashhur is misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever (la yukaffar). The passage also notes that ziyadah (addition) to the Quran is permissible via mashhur, but naskh (abrogation) is not. The Shafi'i view equates mashhur with ahad, giving only zann.

Key Terms
المشهور (al-mashhur): A hadith transmitted by more than two in every generation but does not reach the level of tawatur.
علم الطمأنينة ('ilm al-tuma'nina): Satisfactory knowledge that is less than absolute certainty but sufficient for action.
الزيادة على الكتاب (al-ziyadah 'ala al-kitab): Adding a ruling to the Quran via mashhur hadith, e.g., stoning as an addition to the lashing verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the Hanafi madhhab, what is the status of a person who denies a mashhur hadith?
A) He becomes a disbeliever (kafir).
B) He is misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever.
C) He is considered a sinner but not misguided.
D) He is not subject to any blame.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes mashhur from mutawatir and ahad, attributing to it 'ilm al-tuma'nina, making its denier misguided but not a disbeliever.

Khabar al-Wahid: Definition and First Two Conditions
Defining khabar al-wahid and its first two conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar al-wahid and apply the Hanafi rule that a khabar al-wahid cannot contradict the Quran or the mashhur sunna, distinguishing the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i regarding takhsis of general Quranic texts.

Core Idea
A khabar al-wahid cannot override a general Quranic text or a mashhur sunna; if it does, it is rejected.

In this passage, the author defines khabar al-wahid (the isolated report) and outlines the conditions for its acceptance. The focus is on the first two of eight conditions: that the report must not contradict the Quran (even its general or apparent meanings) and must not contradict the mashhur sunna. The Hanafi school maintains that a khabar al-wahid cannot specify a general Quranic text, a position that contrasts with the Shafi'i school. Understanding these conditions is crucial for properly evaluating the strength of hadith in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Define khabar al-wahid
Identify the key elements: narrated by one or more, but not reaching mashhur or mutawatir in number. Note that it can be narrated by two, three, or more as long as it stays below the threshold of mashhur.
Hanafi definition emphasizes relative strength based on number of narrators.
2
Extract the first two conditions for acceptance
The passage states four conditions in the report itself; only two are detailed here: (a) not contradicting the Quran, (b) not contradicting the mashhur sunna. Understand the rationale: the Quran and mashhur sunna are stronger evidence.
These conditions are about the content of the report, not its transmission.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument on non-contradiction with the Quran
If the khabar al-wahid contradicts a clear Quranic text without possible reasonable interpretation, it is unanimously rejected. If it contradicts a general (amm) or apparent (zahir) text, Hanafis reject it, while Shafi'is allow takhsis (specification).
The difference stems from the status of 'amm: Hanafis consider it qat'i in its generality unless specified by stronger evidence; Shafi'is consider it zanni.
4
Examine the example of wudu from touching the penis
The hadith 'Man massa dhakarah falyatawadda'' is presented as allegedly contradicting the Quranic verse about those who love to purify themselves (9:108). The argument is that the verse praises purification through istinja', which necessarily involves touching the private part, so if touching were a nullifier of wudu, that purification would be negated.
This is a distinctive Hanafi argument; note the subtlety of the dalala.
5
Contrast with the second condition: non-contradiction with mashhur sunna
The mashhur sunna is stronger than a khabar al-wahid, so the latter cannot oppose it. An example is given but not completed in the text. Understand the hierarchy: mutawatir > mashhur > ahad.
The concept of mashhur is important in Hanafi usul for weighing conflicting reports.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خبر الواحد وهو الذي يرويه الواحد أو اثنان فصاعداً أن يكون دون المشهور والمتواتر، وحكمه إذا ورد غير مخالف للكتاب والسنة المشهورة، لأن في الطبقة الأولى وكذا في سائر الطبقات عدد التواتر، فالمثال ليس على ما ينبغي. خبر الواحد وهو الذي يرويه الواحد أو اثنان فصاعداً، دون المشهور والمتواتر في كثرة الرواة، فإن رواه اثنان أو الثلاثة أو أكثر يسمى خبر الواحد بشرط أن لا يبلغ كثرته كثرة المشهور والمتواتر، فلا يتوهم أن خبر الواحد ما رواه واحد. وحكمه: وجوب العمل به بثمانية شروط أربعة في نفس الخبر وأربعة في المخبر. أما الأربعة في نفس الخبر فالاثنان منها ما بينه في قوله: إذا ورد إلخ. إذا ورد ذلك الخبر حال كونه غير مخالف للكتاب والسنة المشهورة فالأوّل أن لا يكون ذلك الخبر مخالفاً للكتاب، فإنه لو كان مخالفاً لنص الكتاب ولا يمكن تأويله بغير تعسف لا يقبل ذلك الخبر اتفاقاً، وكذلك إذا خالف عموم الكتاب أو ظاهره لا يجوز تخصيص العموم، وحمل الظاهر على المجاز عندنا خلافاً للشافعي وعامة الأصوليين، ومثاله ما روى أنه قال: 'من مس ذكره فليتوضأ'، فإنه مخالف للكتاب وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا﴾ (التوبة:108)، فإنها نزلت في الاستنجاء بالماء، وهو لا يمكن إلا بمس الفرج، فلو كان مس الذكر من الحدث لما ثبت التطهير بالاستنجاء، فتأمل. وكذا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب'، فإنه يخالف عموم قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَأُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ﴾ (المزمل:20)، فلا يترك العمل بالكتاب بمثل هذه الأحاديث، والثاني لا يكون مخالفاً للسنة المشهورة؛ لأن الخبر المشهور أقوى منه، فلا يصلح المعارضة به فيترك في مقابلته ومثاله ما روي أنه قضى =
Khabar al-wahid is that which is narrated by one or two individuals and above, and it is below mashhur and mutawatir in the number of narrators. Its ruling: if it comes without contradicting the Book and the mashhur sunna, it is obligatory to act upon it, with eight conditions: four pertaining to the report itself and four to the reporter. As for the four pertaining to the report, two of them are indicated in his statement: 'when it comes without contradicting the Book and the mashhur sunna.' The first is that the report should not be contrary to the Book. If it contradicts a clear text of the Book and cannot be interpreted without unreasonable strain, the report is unanimously rejected. Similarly, if it contradicts a general (amm) text of the Book or its apparent meaning, it is not permissible to specify the general or interpret the apparent metaphorically according to our school, contrary to al-Shafi'i and most usul scholars. An example is the report: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' It is contrary to the Book: His statement, 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' (al-Tawba 9:108), which was revealed about cleaning with water after relieving oneself, which is only possible by touching the private area. So if touching the penis were a cause of hadath, then purification by cleaning with water would not be established. Similarly, his statement: 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' contradicts the generality of His statement, 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (al-Muzzammil 73:20). So one does not abandon acting upon the Book on account of such hadiths. The second condition is that it should not be contrary to the mashhur sunna, because the mashhur report is stronger than it, so it cannot be used as a valid objection against it.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage defines khabar al-wahid (isolated report) and outlines the conditions for its acceptance. It explains that khabar al-wahid is transmitted by one, two, or a few narrators but does not reach the level of mashhur or mutawatir. The first two conditions (from the four related to the report itself) are: (1) It must not contradict the Quran. The Hanafi position holds that even if it contradicts a general or apparent meaning of the Quran, it cannot override the Quran. The Shafi'i view, mentioned in contrast, allows specification (takhsis) of a general Quranic text by a khabar al-wahid. Examples are given: the hadith about wudu from touching the penis is argued to be contrary to the Quranic verse praising those who purify themselves by washing with water, which necessarily involves touching. Similarly, the hadith that prayer requires Fatiha contradicts the general command to recite what is easy. (2) It must not contradict the mashhur sunna, because the mashhur is stronger.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith reported by one, two, or more narrators but not reaching the level of mashhur or mutawatir.
العموم (al-umum): A general term that applies to all individuals of its category.
السنة المشهورة (al-sunnah al-mashhurah): A hadith that is known widely among the early generations but not reaching mutawatir; it is stronger than ahad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what happens if a khabar al-wahid contradicts a general (amm) text of the Quran?
A) The general text is specified (takhsis) by the hadith.
B) The hadith is rejected because the Quran is stronger.
C) Both are reconciled through metaphorical interpretation.
D) The hadith takes precedence because it is specific.

Key Takeaway
A khabar al-wahid must not contradict the Quran (including its general meanings) or the mashhur sunna; otherwise, it is not accepted as a valid proof in the Hanafi school.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
15 min
Khabar al-Wahid: Definition and Conditions for Acceptance
Defining khabar al-wahid and its eight conditions for acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar al-wahid according to Hanafi usul and list its eight conditions for acceptance, distinguishing between conditions in the report and in the narrator.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid gives probable knowledge (zann) and is accepted only under strict conditions to protect stronger proofs.

The Hanafi school places great emphasis on the epistemological hierarchy of transmitted reports. Khabar al-wahid, the solitary report, occupies a middle ground: it is not as strong as mutawatir or mashhur, yet it is not rejected outright. This lesson unpacks the precise definition and the rigorous conditions that must be met for such a report to be legally binding. You will see how these conditions safeguard the primacy of the Quran and well-established sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Hanafi definition of khabar al-wahid
Understand that khabar al-wahid is any report below the frequency of mashhur and mutawatir, regardless of the number of narrators (one, two, or more). This definition explicitly rejects the conditions of specific numbers held by the Mu'tazila and others.
Key: the threshold is not a fixed number but a comparison to mashhur/mutawatir.
2
Identify the two sets of conditions
There are eight conditions total: four related to the content of the report (fi nafs al-khabar) and four related to the narrator (fi al-mukhbir). The text first explains the conditions in the report.
3
Learn the four conditions in the report
The report must not contradict the Quran (either its nass, 'amm, or zahir); it must not contradict a mashhur sunnah; it must not concern a matter of general necessity (la ta'umm biha al-balwa); and it must not have been abandoned (tark al-muhajja) by the Sahaba when they differed on the issue. Examples illustrate each condition.
The condition about general necessity is particularly Hanafi; al-Shafi'i accepts such reports if authentic.
4
Learn the four conditions in the narrator
The narrator must be Muslim, of integrity ('adalah), of complete intellect (after puberty), and possess dabt (precision in hearing, understanding, memorizing, and maintaining). Each condition is justified: e.g., disbelief creates suspicion, the sinful do not care about lying, etc.
Dabt is more than memory; it includes accurate transmission and preservation.
5
Recognize the epistemological weight
Khabar al-wahid yields zann (probable knowledge), not certainty. This is contrasted with Ahmad and most hadith scholars who held it gives certain knowledge. The Hanafi position is that it provides 'ilm al-tuma'nina (tranquillity) but not absolute knowledge, unlike mutawatir.
This epistemological stance affects how reports are used in legal reasoning, especially when conflicting with stronger sources.

متواتراً لحاجة الخلق إليه، ولذا تواتر القرآن، واشتهر أخبار البيع والنكاح والطلاق ولما لم يشتهر عَلِمنا أنه سهو أو منسوخ كما هو مذهب أبي الحسن الكرخى وجميع المتأخرين منا، وقال الشافعي لله وعامة الأصوليين: يقبل إذا ثبت سنده، وإليه ذهب أهل الحديث، وذلك مثل حديث الجهر بالبسملة فإنه مع عموم البلوى لم يبلغ حد الشهرة فضلاً عن التواتر. وترك المحاجة به: أي بخبر الواحد. حاصله لايكون الحديث متروكاً يكون هذا الحديث حجة عند بعض المتقدمين أصحابنا وعامة المتأخرين وقال أهل الحديث وغيرهم من الأصوليين هو حجة، مثاله ماروي عن زيد بن ثابت عن النبي له الا الله أنه قال: "الطلاق بالرجال". فالصحابة اختلفوا في ألبتة، فحكم هذا الخبر المشروط بشروط أربعة. العمل: لا العلم والطمانية بل الظن، وذهب أحمد وأكثر المحدثين إلى أنه يوجب علم اليقين، وهذا خلاف ما نجد في أنفسنا من أخبار الآحاذ، ووجوب العمل إنما يثبت بشروط أخرى غير الأربعة السابقة. والعقل الكامل : الذي يحصل بعد البلوغ والضبط وهو سماع الكلام كما هو حقه، ثم فهم معناه، ثم حفظه ثم الثبات عليه، أما الإسلام فلأن الكفر يورث تهمة في الخبر لعداوتهم وسعيهم في تخريب الدين بإدخال ما ليس منه فيه، وأما العدالة وهي الاستقامة في الدين فلأن الفاسق لايبالي بالكذب، فإذا كان عدلا يترجح الصدق منه، وأما كمال العقل فلأن الخبر خصوصاً في الدين لا يتأدّى كما هو حقه بغيره، وأما الضبط فلأن الصدق لا يحصل إلا به.
Chapter of Sunnah. The second source: Sunnah. [Khabar al-Wahid and its ruling] And continuity in fasting the expiation of the oath, but since it was originally from ahad [reports], a doubt arose from it, and like an addition after which certainty disappeared. Khabar al-Wahid is that which is narrated by one or two or more, provided it is below the level of mashhur and mutawatir. Its ruling: when it is not contradictory to the Book and the mashhur Sunnah... because in the first generation and likewise in all generations there is the number of tawatur, so the example is not as it should be. Continuity in fasting etc. because in the reading of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'then fasting three consecutive days' [Muslim, no. 639], so the word 'consecutive' was added to the Book, but his reading is mashhur, so addition to the Book by it is permissible. And since it might be thought that since addition to the Book by mashhur khabar is permissible, and addition is abrogation, and abrogation is only by mutawatir, so mashhur should give certain knowledge like mutawatir, he refuted it by saying: 'but it' i.e. the mashhur khabar, 'by it' i.e. by being from ahad, certain knowledge is lost unlike mutawatir, so mashhur gives only tranquillity. It is narrated by one or two, and in this is a refutation of al-Jubba'i and other Mu'tazila who required a number in it, and also a refutation of those who required the number four. For us, number is not considered; whether narrated by one or two. Below mashhur and mutawatir in abundance of narrators. If narrated by two or three or more, it is called khabar al-wahid on condition that its abundance does not reach that of mashhur and mutawatir, so do not think that khabar al-wahid is what is narrated by one. Its ruling: acting upon it is obligatory with eight conditions: four in the report itself and four in the reporter. As for the four in the report, two are explained in his statement: 'when it occurs...' i.e. when that report occurs while it is not contradictory to the Book and the mashhur Sunnah. First, that report should not be contrary to the Book, for if it is contrary to a nass of the Book and cannot be interpreted without extreme difficulty, that report is not accepted by consensus. Likewise, if it contradicts the general ('amm) of the Book or its apparent meaning (zahir), it is not permissible to specify the general or interpret the apparent metaphorically according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i and most usulis. Example: the narration: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu' [Abu Dawud, no. 181], for it contradicts the Book: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' (9:108), which was revealed about cleaning with water after defecation, which is only possible by touching the private part; if touching the penis were a hadath, purification with istinja would not be established, so ponder. Similarly, his statement: 'No prayer except with Fatiha', contradicts the general of His saying: 'So recite whatever is easy from the Qur'an' (73:20), so action on the Book is not abandoned for such hadiths. Second, it should not be contrary to the mashhur Sunnah, because mashhur khabar is stronger than it, so it cannot validly oppose it, so it is left in its presence. Example: the narration that he judged with one witness and an oath, for it contradicts the mashhur khabar: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the denier' [Tirmidhi, no. 1341]. And if its contradiction to mashhur khabar is considered, then its contradiction to mutawatir is even more worthy of consideration. Third, it should be in an event that is not of general necessity... because if it is in a matter of general necessity, it must be mashhur or mutawatir due to the people's need. Thus the Qur'an is mutawatir, and reports of sale, marriage, and divorce are mashhur, and if not famous, we know it is forgetfulness or abrogated, as is the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and all our later scholars. Al-Shafi'i and most usulis said: it is accepted if its chain is authentic; and the people of hadith went to that. Example: the hadith of reciting basmala aloud, which despite widespread need did not reach the level of mashhur, let alone tawatur. 'And leaving out argument with it' i.e. with khabar al-wahid. Summary: the hadith is not abandoned when there is disagreement among the Sahaba in that incident in which the hadith occurs. Because when disagreement appears in the incident, if none of them argued with this hadith, it is known that it was not established with them, otherwise why would they abandon argument with it when needed? So this hadith is not proof according to some of our early scholars and most later ones. The people of hadith and other usulis said it is proof. Example: the narration from Zayd ibn Thabit from the Prophet that he said: 'Divorce is with the husband.' The Sahaba differed on this issue: Zayd ibn Thabit, Umar, Uthman, and Aisha went to this, as is the view of al-Shafi'i; Ali and Ibn Mas'ud went to the view that it is considered according to the condition of the woman, as is our madhhab. If that hadith were established with them, some of them would definitely have argued with it. So the ruling of this khabar with the four conditions is action: not knowledge and tranquillity but zann. Ahmad and most hadith scholars went to the view that it gives certain knowledge, but this contradicts what we find in ourselves regarding ahad reports. The obligation to act is established by other conditions besides the previous four. 'Complete intellect' which is attained after puberty, and 'dabt' which is hearing the speech as it should be, then understanding its meaning, then memorizing it, then maintaining it. As for Islam, because disbelief creates suspicion in the report due to their enmity and efforts to destroy religion by introducing what is not part of it. As for 'adalah (integrity), which is uprightness in religion, because a sinner does not care about lying; if he is upright, truthfulness is more likely from him. As for complete intellect, because the report especially in religion is not conveyed properly without it. As for dabt, because truthfulness is not attained except through it.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work defines khabar al-wahid (solitary report) and outlines the conditions for its acceptance as a proof in Islamic law. The author begins by clarifying the definition: khabar al-wahid is a report narrated by one, two, or more individuals but remains below the level of mashhur (well-known) and mutawatir (mass transmitted). The number of narrators does not matter; what matters is that it does not reach the abundance of mashhur or mutawatir. The ruling (hukm) is that acting upon it is obligatory, but only under eight conditions: four related to the content of the report and four related to the narrator.

The first condition is that the report must not contradict the Quran. If it contradicts a clear text (nass) of the Quran, it is rejected by consensus. If it contradicts the general meaning (amm) or apparent meaning (zahir) of the Quran, the Hanafi school does not allow specifying the general or interpreting the apparent figuratively (majaz) based on such a report, contrary to al-Shafi'i and most usulis. Examples given are the hadith about wudu from touching the penis and the hadith that prayer requires Fatiha, which are seen as conflicting with Quranic verses.

The second condition is that the report must not contradict a mashhur sunnah (well-known hadith). If it does, the mashhur takes precedence because it is stronger. Example: the hadith of judgment with one witness and an oath contradicts the mashhur principle of 'burden of proof on claimant, oath on denier.'

The third condition is that the report must concern an event that is not of general necessity (la ta'umm biha al-balwa). If the issue is widespread, the report must have achieved mashhur or mutawatir status; otherwise, it indicates forgetfulness or abrogation. The Hanafis differ from al-Shafi'i here: al-Shafi'i would accept such a report if its chain is authentic.

The fourth condition is that the report must not have been abandoned (tark al-muhajja) by the Sahaba when they differed on the matter. If the Sahaba disagreed and none used the report, it is not considered proof. Example: the hadith 'Divorce is with the husband' was not used by Ali and Ibn Mas'ud, so it is not strong in the Hanafi view.

The four conditions in the narrator are: Islam, 'adalah (integrity), complete intellect (after puberty), and dabt (precision). Islam is required because disbelief breeds suspicion. 'Adalah ensures truthfulness. Complete intellect is essential for properly conveying religious reports. Dabt involves hearing correctly, understanding, memorizing, and maintaining accuracy. Without dabt, truthfulness cannot be assured.

The passage also discusses epistemological weight: khabar al-wahid gives only zann (probability), not certainty, contrary to Ahmad and most hadith scholars who deemed it productive of certainty. The Hanafi position is that it yields 'ilm al-tuma'nina (tranquillity) but not absolute knowledge, unlike mutawatir.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report narrated by one, two, or more individuals that does not reach the level of mashhur or mutawatir in number of narrators
المشهور (al-mashhur): A hadith that has been narrated by multiple chains in every generation but does not reach tawatur; it gives tranquillity but not certainty
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report narrated by such a large number in every generation that it is impossible for them to have colluded on a lie; it gives certain knowledge
العدالة (al-'adalah): Integrity; uprightness in religion, ensuring the narrator does not lie
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision in narration: hearing correctly, understanding, memorizing, and maintaining the report

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a khabar al-wahid contradicts the general meaning ('amm) of the Quran?
A) The Quran's general meaning is specified by the hadith
B) The hadith is accepted and the Quran's general meaning is interpreted figuratively
C) The hadith is rejected because the Quran takes precedence
D) Both are reconciled if possible

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-wahid is a report below mashhur/mutawatir; its acceptance requires eight strict conditions to ensure it does not undermine stronger sources like the Quran and mashhur sunnah, and it yields only probable knowledge (zann).

The Four Narrator Conditions for Khabar al-Wahid
Explains the four narrator conditions for khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four narrator conditions required by the Hanafi school for accepting a khabar al-wahid and explain the rationale for each.

Core Idea
A khabar al-wahid is only accepted if the narrator is Muslim, just, sane, and precise.

In this lesson, we examine the first part of the passage from Al-Husami, which lays down the four conditions that a narrator of a solitary report must satisfy: Islam, 'adalah (integrity), complete intellect, and dabt (precision). Each condition serves to filter out potential sources of error or bias. Understanding these conditions is essential for evaluating hadith and for grasping the Hanafi approach to the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
From the text, extract the four conditions: الإسلام, العدالة, العقل الكامل, الضبط.
2
Explain why Islam is required
The author states disbelief casts suspicion due to enmity; a non-Muslim may deliberately corrupt the religion.
3
Explain why 'adalah is required
A sinner does not care about lying; a just person is presumed truthful.
4
Explain why complete intellect is required
A child or insane person cannot convey the report properly.
5
Explain why dabt is required
Precision involves hearing, understanding, memorizing, and preserving; without it, truth is not attained.

الأصل الثاني السنة
في حادثة لاتعم بها البلوي، ولم يظهر من الصحابة الاختلاف فيها، وترك
المحاجة به، أنه يوجب العمل بشروط تراعى في المخبر.
شروط أربعة في المخبر]
تلك الشروط
وهي أربعة : الإسلام والعدالة والعقل الكامل والضبط،
أي في الحادثة
بشاهد ويمين، فإنه مخالف للخبر المشهور، وهو قوله عليه: "البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر". الترمذي، رقم : ١٣٤١] وإذا اعتبرت مخالفته بالخبر المشهور فمخالفته بالمتواتر أولى بالاعتبار. والثالث أن يكون في حادثة لا تعم بها البلوى إلخ.
لا تعم بها البلوى بها البلوى لأنه إذا كان فيما عمّ به البلوى فلا بد أن يكون مشهوراً أو متواتراً لحاجة الخلق إليه، ولذا تواتر القرآن، واشتهر أخبار البيع والنكاح والطلاق ولما لم يشتهر عَلِمنا أنه سهو أو منسوخ كما هو مذهب أبي الحسن الكرخى وجميع المتأخرين منا، وقال الشافعي لله وعامة الأصوليين: يقبل إذا ثبت سنده، وإليه ذهب أهل الحديث، وذلك مثل حديث الجهر بالبسملة فإنه مع عموم البلوى لم يبلغ حد الشهرة فضلاً عن التواتر. وترك المحاجة به: أي بخبر الواحد. حاصله لايكون الحديث متروكاً عند اختلاف الصحابة في تلك الحادثة التي ورد فيها ذلك الحديث؛ إذ عند ظهور الاختلاف في الحادثة إذا لم يحتج أحدهم بهذا الحديث علم أنه ليس بثابت عندهم، وإلا ما وجه ترك الاحتجاج به عند مس الحاجة إليه؟ فلا يكون هذا الحديث حجة عند بعض المتقدمين أصحابنا وعامة المتأخرين وقال أهل الحديث وغيرهم من الأصوليين هو حجة، مثاله ماروي عن زيد بن ثابت عن النبي له الا الله أنه قال: "الطلاق بالرجال". فالصحابة اختلفوا في تلك المسألة، فذهب زيد بن ثابت وعمر وعثمان وعائشة له إلى هذا كما هو قول الشافعي له، وذهب علي وابن مسعود الله إلى أنه معتبر بحال المرأة كما هو
من
مذهبنا، فلو كان ذلك الحديث ثابتاً عندهم لاحتج بعضهم به ألبتة، فحكم هذا الخبر المشروط بشروط أربعة. العمل: لا العلم والطمانية بل الظن، وذهب أحمد وأكثر المحدثين إلى أنه يوجب علم اليقين، وهذا خلاف ما نجد في أنفسنا من أخبار الآحاذ، ووجوب العمل إنما يثبت بشروط أخرى غير الأربعة السابقة. والعقل الكامل : الذي يحصل بعد البلوغ والضبط وهو سماع الكلام كما هو حقه، ثم فهم معناه، ثم حفظه ثم الثبات عليه، أما الإسلام فلأن الكفر يورث تهمة في الخبر لعداوتهم وسعيهم في تخريب الدين بإدخال ما ليس منه فيه، وأما العدالة وهي الاستقامة في الدين فلأن الفاسق لايبالي بالكذب، فإذا كان عدلا يترجح الصدق منه، وأما كمال العقل فلأن الخبر خصوصاً في الدين لا يتأدّى كما هو حقه بغيره، وأما الضبط فلأن الصدق لا يحصل إلا به.

فلا يجب العمل بخبر الكافر والفاسق والصبي والمعتوه والذي اشتدت غفلته خلقة
أو مسامحة أو مجازفة.
Chapter of Sunnah. 135. The second source: Sunnah. Regarding an incident that is not of general necessity, and no disagreement among the Companions appears concerning it, and they did not abandon using it as proof, that it necessitates action with conditions to be observed in the reporter. [Four conditions in the reporter] Those conditions are four: Islam, integrity (adalah), complete intellect, and precision (dabt). Meaning regarding the incident: with a witness and an oath, for it contradicts the well-known report which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the denier.' (Tirmidhi, no. 1341). And if its contradiction to the well-known report is considered, then its contradiction to the mutawatir is even more worthy of consideration. The third condition: that the incident is not of general necessity, etc. 'Not of general necessity' because if it is of general necessity, then it must be mashhur or mutawatir due to people's need for it. Hence the Quran is mutawatir, and reports of sale, marriage, divorce are mashhur. When it is not mashhur, we know it is an error or abrogated, as is the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and all later scholars of ours. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) and most usulis say: it is accepted if its chain is authentic, and the people of hadith go to this. An example is the hadith of reciting 'Bismillah' aloud, for despite general necessity, it did not reach the level of mashhur let alone mutawatir. 'And they did not abandon using it as proof' meaning of khabar al-wahid. Its conclusion: the hadith is not abandoned when there is disagreement among the Companions on the incident in which the hadith was reported, for when disagreement appears in the incident and none of them uses this hadith as proof, it is known that it is not established with them. Otherwise, what reason would there be to abandon using it when needed? So this hadith is not a proof according to some early scholars of ours and most later scholars. The people of hadith and other usulis say it is a proof. Example: what is narrated from Zaid ibn Thabit from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Divorce is by the men.' The Companions differed on this issue. Zaid ibn Thabit, Umar, Uthman, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them) went to this, as is the saying of al-Shafi'i, while Ali and Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) went to that it is considered by the state of the woman, as is our madhhab. If that hadith had been established with them, surely some of them would have used it as proof. So the ruling of this report conditioned by four conditions is: action (not knowledge and certainty but conjecture). Ahmad and most hadith scholars went to that it necessitates certain knowledge. This contradicts what we find in ourselves regarding solitary reports. The obligation of action is only established with other conditions besides the previous four. 'Complete intellect' is that which is acquired after puberty, and 'precision' is hearing the speech as it should be, then understanding its meaning, then preserving it, then being steadfast upon it. As for Islam, because disbelief casts suspicion in the report due to their enmity and efforts to destroy the religion by inserting what is not of it. As for integrity (adalah), which is uprightness in religion, because a sinner does not care about lying, so if he is just, truthfulness is preponderant from him. As for complete intellect, because the report, especially in religion, is not conveyed properly without it. As for precision, because truthfulness is not attained except with it. So action is not obligatory upon the report of a disbeliever, a sinner, a boy, an insane person, and one whose heedlessness is intense, whether by nature, leniency, or recklessness.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid (solitary report) as a proof. The author begins by stating that khabar al-wahid is acted upon subject to conditions in the reporter. He lists four conditions: Islam, 'adalah (integrity), complete intellect, and dhabt (precision). These are the standard Hanafi conditions for narrator acceptance. The text also adds contextual conditions: the report must be about an incident that is not of general necessity (umum al-balwa), there must be no known disagreement among the Companions on the matter that would indicate the report was not known to them, and the Companions must not have abandoned acting upon it. The author then elaborates on the condition of umum al-balwa, explaining why reports of general necessity must be widespread (mashhur or mutawatir). He notes the disagreement: Abu Hanifa's school (following Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and later Hanafis) holds that such reports are not accepted unless they reach mashhur level, while al-Shafi'i and most usulis accept them if the chain is authentic. The example of the hadith about reciting 'Bismillah' aloud is given. The passage then discusses the condition of no ikhtilaf among the Companions. If the Sahaba differed on an issue and none used a particular hadith, it indicates the hadith was not considered authentic by them. An example is the hadith 'al-talaq bi al-rijal' (divorce is by men). The author concludes that khabar al-wahid yields obligation of action (zann) not certainty ('ilm). This contrasts with Ahmad and most hadith scholars who hold it gives certain knowledge. The four narrator conditions are then explained in detail: Islam removes suspicion of bias; 'adalah ensures truthfulness; complete intellect ensures proper conveyance; dhabt ensures accuracy. Finally, the text states that reports from a disbeliever, sinner, boy, insane person, or extremely heedless person are not acted upon.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by fewer than the number required for tawatur
العدالة (al-'adalah): Integrity and uprightness in religion, avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision: hearing, understanding, memorizing, and preserving the report without error

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four narrator conditions for khabar al-wahid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Islam
B) Adalah
C) Dabt
D) Wealth

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four specific narrator conditions—Islam, 'adalah, complete intellect, and dabt—to accept a khabar al-wahid.

Contextual Conditions and Epistemic Value of Khabar al-Wahid
Explains contextual conditions and epistemic status of khabar al-wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the contextual conditions (umum al-balwa, no Sahabi ikhtilaf, not abandoned) for accepting a khabar al-wahid and state the Hanafi view that it yields zann (conjecture) not 'ilm (certainty).

Core Idea
A khabar al-wahid on a matter of general necessity must be widespread; otherwise it is rejected, and it only yields probable action, not certainty.

While narrator conditions are internal, the Hanafi school also imposes external conditions on the content of the report. The passage explains that if a report concerns a matter of general necessity (umum al-balwa) but is not widely known, it is likely an error or abrogated. Additionally, if the Companions differed on an issue and none used the report, it indicates it was not authentic. These conditions show the Hanafi emphasis on corroboration. The passage also clarifies that a khabar al-wahid obligates action (zann) but does not produce certainty, contra the view of some hadith scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three contextual conditions
From the text: (1) The incident is not of umum al-balwa, (2) No disagreement among the Companions appears, (3) The Companions did not abandon using it as proof.
2
Explain the condition of umum al-balwa
If an issue is of general need, its report must be widely known (mashhur/mutawatir); otherwise, it is considered erroneous or abrogated. Example: hadith of jahr bi al-basmalah.
3
Explain the condition of no Sahabi ikhtilaf
If the Companions differed on an issue and none used the report, it shows the report was not established among them.
Example: hadith 'al-talaq bi al-rijal' from Zaid ibn Thabit.
4
Explain the condition of not being abandoned (tark al-muhajjah)
The Companions did not leave it out; if they did, it's not a proof.
5
State the epistemic value of khabar al-wahid
It obligates action but yields only conjecture (zann), not certainty. Hanafis reject the view that it gives 'ilm.

This passage discusses the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid (solitary report) as a proof. The author begins by stating that khabar al-wahid is acted upon subject to conditions in the reporter. He lists four conditions: Islam, 'adalah (integrity), complete intellect, and dhabt (precision). These are the standard Hanafi conditions for narrator acceptance. The text also adds contextual conditions: the report must be about an incident that is not of general necessity (umum al-balwa), there must be no known disagreement among the Companions on the matter that would indicate the report was not known to them, and the Companions must not have abandoned acting upon it. The author then elaborates on the condition of umum al-balwa, explaining why reports of general necessity must be widespread (mashhur or mutawatir). He notes the disagreement: Abu Hanifa's school (following Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and later Hanafis) holds that such reports are not accepted unless they reach mashhur level, while al-Shafi'i and most usulis accept them if the chain is authentic. The example of the hadith about reciting 'Bismillah' aloud is given. The passage then discusses the condition of no ikhtilaf among the Companions. If the Sahaba differed on an issue and none used a particular hadith, it indicates the hadith was not considered authentic by them. An example is the hadith 'al-talaq bi al-rijal' (divorce is by men). The author concludes that khabar al-wahid yields obligation of action (zann) not certainty ('ilm). This contrasts with Ahmad and most hadith scholars who hold it gives certain knowledge. The four narrator conditions are then explained in detail: Islam removes suspicion of bias; 'adalah ensures truthfulness; complete intellect ensures proper conveyance; dhabt ensures accuracy. Finally, the text states that reports from a disbeliever, sinner, boy, insane person, or extremely heedless person are not acted upon.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by fewer than the number required for tawatur
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A matter of general necessity affecting all Muslims
العدالة (al-'adalah): Integrity and uprightness in religion, avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision: hearing, understanding, memorizing, and preserving the report without error

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a khabar al-wahid is reported about a matter that is of general necessity (umum al-balwa) but does not reach the level of mashhur, it is:
A) Accepted if the chain is authentic
B) Considered an error or abrogated
C) Accepted but not acted upon
D) Acted upon only if the Quran confirms it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects solitary reports on matters of general necessity unless they are widespread, and such reports only yield conjecture, not certainty.

The Ruling on the Mustur Narrator in Hanafi Usul
Ruling on mustur narrator with exception for early generations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for accepting a narrator in Hanafi usul and apply the exception for the early generations based on the Prophet's hadith.

Core Idea
A mustur narrator's report is rejected unless from the first three generations due to collective tazkiyah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rule for the mustur (hidden-status) narrator. You will learn why his report is generally not accepted in hadith, the crucial exception for the first three generations of Muslims, and an internal Hanafi difference over whether a mustur is treated like an 'adil or a fasiq when reporting impurity. Understanding these nuances is key to evaluating narrators and applying usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
Locate the statement: ''And the mustur is like the fasiq: his report is not a proof in the chapter of hadith until his integrity becomes apparent.'' This is the default rule.
The mustur is defined as one whose sinfulness or integrity is not known.
2
Recall the four conditions for narrator acceptance
The passage states four conditions: Islam, 'adalah, complete intellect, and dabt (precision). The mustur lacks apparent 'adalah, so his report is rejected like that of a fasiq.
These conditions must be apparent (zahir) in the narrator.
3
Understand the exception: the first three generations
The passage excepts reports from the first three generations (Companions, Followers, and their followers) based on the Prophet's hadith: 'The best of generations is my generation...' This hadith serves as a collective tazkiyah, establishing general integrity for that era.
This exception applies only to the chapter of hadith, not judiciary.
4
Trace the internal Hanafi dispute on impurity
Two transmissions from Abu Hanifa: (1) from Hasan ibn Ziyad – mustur is like 'adil; (2) from Kitab al-Istihsan – mustur is like fasiq. The second is preferred in hadith matters.
The practical difference: if a mustur reports water is najis, the first view accepts it, the second rejects it.
5
Distinguish hadith from judiciary
In judiciary, Abu Hanifa accepts testimony of mustur persons due to the apparent integrity of Muslims. In hadith, the stricter rule applies because narrations require certainty.
This distinction is signaled by the author's phrase 'in the chapter of hadith'.

Source Text

بخبر الكافر: لفقدان الشرط الأول، وهو الإسلام والفاسق : أي لا يجب العمل بخبره لفقدان الشرط الثاني وهو العدالة، وكذا لايجب العمل بخبر الصبي والمعتوه لفقدان الشرط الثالث وهو كمال العقل، وكذا لايجب العمل بخبر الذي اشتدّت غفلته خلقة بأن كان سهوه ونسيانه أغلب من حفظه أو مسامحة: أي عدم المبالاة بالسهو والخطأ. مجازفة : أي التكلم من غير خبرة ويقظة؛ لعدم الشرط الرابع وهو الضبط. ف وهذه الشروط الأربعة تجب أن توجد في الراوي ظاهرة؛ لأن المستور لا يقبل حديثه كما بينه المصنف بقوله : والمستور إلخ. والمستور الذي لا يظهر فسقه وعدالته في باب الحديث إلخ واحترز بقوله "في باب الحديث" عن باب القضاء؛ إذ القاضي لو قضى بشهادة المستور جاز عن أبي حنيفة وله نظراً إلى ظاهر العدالة؛ لأن المسلم ظاهره العدالة، وهذا بخلاف من كان مستور الإسلام أو العقل أو الضبط، حيث لايقبل قوله: لا في القضاء ولا في الحديث؛ إذ تلك الأمور ليست ظاهرة في حق المرء، فافهم.
إلا في الصدر الأول: أي لا يكون خبر المستور حجة في جميع الصدور إلا في الصدر الأول، وأراد به قرن الصحابة والتابعين وتبع التابعين فخبر المستور من القرون الثلاثة يكون حجة بشروط على ما نبين من أن العدالة أصل في ذلك الزمان بشهادة النبي بقوله : "خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم. رواه البخاري، [رقم: ٦٦٥٨]
فهذا تعديل من صاحب الشرع، وتعديله أقوى من تعديل غيره. وروى الحسن بن زياد تلميذ أبي حنيفة رحاله. مثل العدل إلخ وهو الظاهر من مذهبه وهو أنه يجوز القضاء بشهادة المستورين إذا لم يطعن؛ لأن العدالة ظاهر من المسلمين مثل الفاسق فيه : أي فيما يخبر عن نجاسة الماء، حتى إذا حضر المسافر الصلاة ولم يجد ماء إلا في إناء فقال رجل وهو مستور الحال: إنه نجس، لا يقبل خبره إلحاقاً بالفاسق، فعليه أن يتوضأ من ذلك الماء.
العقل: فإن قيل كيف يستر العقل؟ إذ البلوغ أقيم مقامه، والبلوغ أمر ظاهري لايستتر في حق من لم يره، فتدبر.
[Ruling of the mustur] And the mustur is like the fasiq: his report is not a proof in the chapter of hadith until his integrity becomes apparent, except in the first generation as we will explain. Al-Hasan (ibn Ziyad) reported from Abu Hanifa that he is like the 'adil regarding what he reports about impurity of water, and it is mentioned in Kitab al-Istihsan that he is like the fasiq in that. ... Meaning Muhammad. 'Mustur' [follows] the report of a disbeliever: due to loss of the first condition, which is Islam; and the fasiq: i.e., action upon his report is not obligatory due to loss of the second condition, which is 'adalah. Likewise, action upon the report of a boy and an insane person is not obligatory due to loss of the third condition, which is complete intellect. Likewise, action upon the report of one whose heedlessness is intense by nature such that his forgetfulness and oversight are more than his memory, or by leniency (i.e., not caring about oversight and error), or by recklessness (i.e., speaking without expertise and alertness) due to the loss of the fourth condition, which is dabt. So these four conditions must be apparently present in the narrator because the mustur's hadith is not accepted, as the author clarified by his saying: 'and the mustur, etc.' The mustur is one whose sinfulness and integrity are not apparent in the chapter of hadith, etc. And he restricted with his saying 'in the chapter of hadith' concerning the chapter of judiciary, because the judge, if he judges based on the testimony of a mustur, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa due to considering the apparent integrity, because a Muslim's apparent state is integrity. This is different from one whose Islam, intellect, or dabt is unknown, for his statement is not accepted neither in judiciary nor in hadith, since those matters are not apparent in a person. So understand. 'Except in the first generation': i.e., the report of a mustur is not a proof in all times except in the first generation. He meant the generation of the Companions, Followers, and the Followers of the Followers. Thus the report of a mustur from these three generations is a proof under conditions, as we will explain: that integrity was the norm in that time, as evidenced by the Prophet's saying: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them' (Bukhari, no. 6658). This is a tazkiyah (validation) from the Lawgiver, and His validation is stronger than that of anyone else. And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, the student of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), narrated: 'Like the 'adil, etc.' This is the apparent view from his madhhab, that it is permissible to judge based on the testimony of mustur persons as long as no criticism is made, because integrity is apparent from Muslims. 'Like the fasiq in that' i.e., regarding what he reports about impurity of water, such that if a traveler is about to pray and finds no water except in a vessel, and a man whose status is mustur says it is impure, his report is not accepted, assimilated to the fasiq, so he must perform wudu with that water. 'Intellect': if it is said, how can intellect be hidden? Since puberty stands in its place, and puberty is an apparent matter that is not hidden for one who has not seen him, so reflect.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of a mustur narrator — one whose 'adalah (integrity) is not known. The author states that like a fasiq (sinner), the mustur's report is not accepted as proof in hadith until his 'adalah becomes apparent. However, there is an exception for the first three generations (Sahaba, Tabi'un, Tabi' al-Tabi'in) due to the general presumption of integrity in that era, supported by the hadith 'The best of generations...' which serves as a collective tazkiyah. The author then discusses a difference of transmission from Abu Hanifa: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reported that Abu Hanifa considered the mustur like an 'adil in matters of impurity (e.g., reporting water is najis), while Kitab al-Istihsan states he is like a fasiq. The author notes that the apparent view is that judgment based on mustur testimony is permissible in judicial contexts (as per Abu Hanifa) but not in hadith. The text also clarifies that the four conditions (Islam, 'adalah, intellect, dabt) must be apparent; if any are hidden, the report is rejected. A subtle point: mustur applies only to 'adalah, not to Islam, intellect, or dabt, because those are generally apparent. The passage concludes with a question about how intellect can be hidden, noting that puberty is the visible marker.

Key Terms
المستور (al-mustur): A narrator whose integrity (adalah) is not known; his sinfulness or righteousness is hidden
الصدر الأول (al-sadr al-awwal): The early generations of Islam: Companions, Followers, and their followers

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mustur narrator's report in hadith is generally not accepted unless he belongs to the first three generations, due to the Prophet's collective tazkiyah.

Conditions for Accepting Hadith Narrators: The Mastur and the Early Generations Exception
Explaining conditions for hadith narrators and status of mastur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four conditions required for a hadith narrator in the Hanafi school and apply the ruling regarding the mastur narrator in different contexts, including the exception for early generations.

Core Idea
The mastur narrator's report is not proof unless uprightness is apparent, except in the early generations where uprightness was guaranteed by the Prophet's testimony.

This passage from the chapter on Sunnah lays out the fundamental conditions for accepting a hadith narrator: Islam, uprightness, complete intellect, and precision. It then delves into the status of the 'mastur'—a narrator whose moral state is unknown. While his reports are generally rejected in hadith, there is an exception for the first three generations, supported by the Prophet's hadith. Additionally, the text notes a dispute about the mastur's report concerning water impurity and distinguishes between hadith and judiciary contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Conditions
Extract the four conditions explicitly mentioned: Islam, uprightness (adalah), complete intellect (aql), and precision (dabt). Note that each corresponds to a deficiency that voids acceptance: disbelief, sinfulness, lack of reason, and excessive heedlessness.
The condition of precision (dabt) includes freedom from careless error or recklessness.
2
Define the Mastur
Understand that 'mastur' means a narrator whose state of uprightness or sinfulness is not apparent. The default ruling: his report is not accepted in hadith until his uprightness becomes known. Recognize the exception: the early generations (Companions, Followers, their followers) where uprightness is presumed due to the Prophet's certification.
The early generations exception is a form of takhsis (specification) of the general rule.
3
Analyze the Intra-Madhhab Dispute on Water Impurity
Compare the two transmissions from Abu Hanifa: Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates that the mastur is like an upright narrator regarding reports of water impurity (so his report is accepted), while the Book of Istihsan states he is like a sinner (so rejected). Identify the thamarah (practical outcome): a traveler finding only water that a mastur claims is impure must perform ablution with it according to one view, or avoid it according to the other.
The text does not definitively choose, but mentions both. In practice, later Hanafi works often adopt the view of rejection.
4
Distinguish Between Hadith and Judiciary
Note the qualification: the mastur's report is rejected 'in the chapter of hadith' but in judiciary, a judge may accept the testimony of a mastur based on the apparent uprightness of Muslims. This distinction is crucial—a person's testimony can be accepted in court even if his reliability is not fully known.
This is based on the principle that a Muslim's default state is uprightness in worldly matters.
5
Apply the Daleel: The Hadith on Early Generations
The exception for early generations is supported by the hadith 'Khayr al-qurun' which the Hanafis treat as a tadeel (certification) of all narrators from those generations. Even if a narrator is mastur, his report is accepted because the Lawgiver has guaranteed the uprightness of that era.
This dalil has qati thubut and qati dalalah in the Hanafi view, making it binding.

Chapter of Sunnah 136 The second foundation: Sunnah. So it is not obligatory to act upon the report of a disbeliever, a sinner, a boy, an insane person, and one whose heedlessness is severe - due to nature, carelessness, or recklessness. Ruling of the mastur: The mastur is like the sinner; his report is not a proof in the chapter of hadith until his uprightness becomes apparent, except in the early generation as we will explain. And Hasan [bin Ziyad] narrated from Abu Hanifa that he [Abu Hanifa] is like the upright [narrator] regarding what he reports about impurity of water. And it is mentioned in the Book of Istihsan that he is like the sinner in that... (unclear) Muhammad [said]: The mastur. Regarding the report of the disbeliever: due to loss of the first condition, which is Islam; and the sinner: meaning it is not obligatory to act upon his report due to loss of the second condition, which is uprightness; likewise it is not obligatory to act upon the report of the boy and the insane due to loss of the third condition, which is complete intellect; likewise it is not obligatory to act upon the report of one whose heedlessness is severe - due to nature, namely that his forgetfulness and negligence are more prevalent than his retention, or carelessness: meaning lack of concern for forgetfulness and error, or recklessness: meaning speaking without experience and vigilance - due to absence of the fourth condition, which is precision. So these four conditions must be apparent in the narrator because the mastur's hadith is not accepted as the author stated: 'and the mastur etc.' The mastur is one whose sinfulness and uprightness are not apparent in the chapter of hadith etc. And he [the author] qualified with his saying 'in the chapter of hadith' to exclude the chapter of judiciary; for if a judge judges by the testimony of the mastur, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, considering the apparent uprightness because the Muslim's apparent state is uprightness. This is unlike one whose Islam, intellect, or precision is concealed, where his statement is accepted neither in judiciary nor in hadith because those matters are not apparent in a person. So understand. Except in the early generation: meaning the report of the mastur is not a proof in all generations except in the early generation; he intends by it the time of the Companions, Followers, and the Followers of the Followers. So the report of the mastur from the three generations is a proof under conditions as we will explain, because uprightness was prevalent in that time, as attested by the Prophet's saying: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' Narrated by al-Bukhari, [no. 6658]. This is a certification of uprightness from the Lawgiver, and His certification is stronger than that of others. And Hasan ibn Ziyad, the student of Abu Hanifa, narrated [from him] that he [the mastur] is like the upright etc., and this is apparent from his madhhab, that it is permissible to judge by the testimony of masturs if not challenged, because uprightness is apparent from Muslims. 'Like the sinner therein': meaning in what he reports about impurity of water, such that if a traveler is present for prayer and finds no water except in a vessel and a man who is mastur says it is impure, his report is not accepted by analogy to the sinner, so he must perform ablution with that water. Intellect: If it is said, how can intellect be concealed? Since puberty stands in its place, and puberty is an apparent matter not concealed in the case of one who has not seen him, then reflect.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for accepting hadith reports. It first states that reports from a disbeliever, sinner, boy, insane person, and the extremely heedless (due to nature, carelessness, or recklessness) are not acted upon. The author then explains the four conditions: Islam, uprightness (adalah), complete intellect, and precision (dabt). These conditions must be apparent in the narrator. The mastur (one whose state is concealed) is treated like the sinner; his report is not a proof in hadith unless his uprightness becomes clear, except in the early generations (the first three centuries) where uprightness was prevalent due to the Prophet’s testimony. Abu Hanifa is reported to have said that the mastur is like the upright narrator regarding reports of water impurity, but according to the Book of Istihsan, he is like the sinner. The passage also distinguishes between the chapter of hadith and the chapter of judiciary: a judge may accept the testimony of a mastur based on apparent uprightness. The early generations exception is supported by the hadith 'The best of generations...' which is a certification from the Lawgiver. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is permissible to judge by the testimony of masturs if not challenged. The passage concludes with a note that intellect is not concealed because puberty is apparent.

Key Terms
المستور (al-mastur): One whose state of uprightness or sinfulness is not apparent; his report is not accepted in hadith unless his uprightness is known
الفاسق (al-fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins; his report is not accepted due to lack of uprightness
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): Uprightness; the quality of being just and avoiding major and minor sins, a condition for acceptance of narration
الضبط (al-ḍabṭ): Precision; the narrator's accuracy in preserving and transmitting reports, free from excessive heedlessness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A disbeliever
B) A sinner (fasiq)
C) A mastur from the early generations
D) A boy

Key Takeaway
Four conditions must be apparent in a narrator for his report to be accepted; a mastur (concealed narrator) is not accepted except in the early generations, where the Prophet's testimony suffices.
