Reports on Impurity from a Fasiq, Kafir, Child, and Insane
Ruling on impurity reports from various reporters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a fasiq, kafir, child, or insane person reports the impurity of water, and explain the reasoning based on taharri and authority.

Core Idea
A fasiq's report requires personal investigation; a kafir/child/insane report is disregarded due to lack of authority.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between categories of reporters in matters of purity. This lesson unpacks the rulings for a fasiq versus a kafir, child, or insane person when they claim water is impure. Understanding these distinctions is key to applying the principle that ilzam (binding effect) is central to the reliability of reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of reporters
Note the three categories: fasiq (sinner), kafir (disbeliever), and those lacking legal capacity (child, insane).
Each has a different ruling in the same scenario of reporting impurity.
2
State the ruling for the fasiq's report
The hearer does not accept it outright; he uses taharri (personal investigation). If his dominant conjecture favors truthfulness, he performs tayammum without pouring the water. Pouring first is more precautionary.
This is because the fasiq lacks 'adalah, but the original purity of water is a counter-evidence.
3
State the ruling for the kafir, child, and insane
Their reports are not considered at all. The hearer performs wudu with the water (assuming it remains pure) and does not perform tayammum. However, if he pours out the water first and then performs tayammum, it is better.
The reason is that these persons have no authority (wilayah) to impose binding obligations.
4
Explain the reasoning behind the difference
The fasiq's report can create a dominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), so taharri is allowed. The others lack even that potential for binding effect because their status precludes any authority.
Ilzam (compulsion) is the key factor: those who cannot impose ilzam have their reports completely disregarded.
5
Analyze the precautionary measures
Pouring out the water before tayammum is a precaution in both cases to eliminate any doubt about the purity of the water. In the fasiq's case, it removes the possibility of performing tayammum while pure water exists; in the other cases, it allows for the best of both possibilities.
The precaution shows sensitivity to potential truthfulness even when the report is not binding.

باب السنة خبر الفاسق ۱۳۷ الأصل الثاني السنة وهو الصحيح. وقال محمد له في الفاسق يخبر بنجاسة الماء: إنه يحكم السامع رأيه، فإن وقع في قلبه أنه صادق يتيمّم من غير إراقة الماء، فإن أراق وتيمّم فهو أحوط أي المخبر الماء للتيمّم، وفي خبر الكافر والصبي والمعتوه إذا وقع في قلب السامع صدقهم بنجاسة الماء يتوضأ ولا يتيمم، فإن أراق الماء ثم تيمّم فهو أفضل، وفي المعاملات التي تنفك عن معنى الإلزام كالوكالات والمضاربات والإذن في التجارة يعتبر خبر كل مميز؛ لعموم الضرورة الداعية إلى سقوط سائر الشرائط، وهو الصحيح لظهور الفسق فيما بعد الصدر الأول، فلا يعتمد على قول المستور ما لم يظهر عدالته مع أن الأصل في الماء هو الطهور. ولما فرغ عن المستور شرع في الفاسق فقال: وقال محمد إلخ. يحكم السامع رأيه: أي يجعل السامع رأيه حاكماً فيتحرّى يتيمم من غير إراقة الماء: فلا يجوز له الوضوء من ذلك الماء؛ لأن أكبر الرأي فيما لم يوقف على حقيقته كاليقين فخبر الفاسق لا يعتد به في نجاسة الماء، وإنما وجب عليه التيمم من غلبة ظنه لا بخبره. أحوط للتيمم لاحتمال أنه كاذب في خبره، فحينئذ لا يجوز له التيمم لوجود الماء الطاهر، فالاحتياط أن الماء ليصير عادماً له، فحينئذ يجوز له التيمم يقيناً وإن كان أكبر رأيه أنه كاذب في خبره، وأما لو أخبر الكافر والصبي والمعتوه فحكمه ما بينه المصنّف بقوله : وفي خبر الكافر إلخ. ولا يتيمم لعدم الاعتبار بخبرهم، وذلك لأن في اعتبار أخبارهم إلزاما، وهؤلاء ليس لهم ولاية الإلزام. فهو أفضل لأن احتمال الصدق غير منقطع عن خبرهم؛ لأن الكفر والصبا والعته لاينافي الصدق؛ وعلى هذا التقدير لايجوز له التوضؤ بالماء النجس فله أن يريق الماء أولاً ليصير عادما له ثم يتيمّم. التي تنفك عن معنى الإلزام، واحترز به عن المعاملات التي فيها إلزام محض من حقوق العباد التي تجري فيها الخصومات، فإن في تلك المعاملات لا يقبل الشهادة بغير الولاية والأهلية، ولفظ الشهادة والعدد، وكذلك احترز به عن الحقوق التي فيها إلزام من وجه دون وجه، كعزل الوكيل وحجر المأذون، فإن فيها يشترط أحد شرطي الشهادة إما العدالة وإما العدد اعتبارا لمعنى الإلزام وعدمه. كالوكالات بأن قال: فإن وكلك والمضاربات بأن قال: فلان جعلك مضارباً. والإذن في التجارة: بأن قال لعبد: إن مولاك أذن لك في التجارة، فإن في تلك المعاملات يعتبر خبر كل إلخ. كل مميز : عدلاً كان أو غير عدل، صبياً كان أو بالغا، مسلما كان أو كافراً، حتى يقبل خبر الفاسق والصبي والكافر لوجهين، أحدهما ما بينه بقوله: لعموم الضرورة إلخ. سائر الشرائط المذكورة من الإسلام والعدالة والعقل الكامل والضبط. فإن الإنسان قلما يجد المستجمع لتلك الشرائط يبعثه إلى وكيله أو غلامه، ولا دليل مع السامع يعمل به سوى هذا الخبر، ولأن اعتبار هذه الشرائط ليترجح جهة الصدق في الخبر فيصلح أن يكون ملزماً، وذلك فيما يتعلّق به اللزوم أمور الدين دون ما لا يتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات، وإنما اعتبر خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته وطهارة الماء ونجاسته إذا تأيد بأكبر الرأي؛ لأن ذلك أمر خاص لا يستقيم تلقيه من جهة العدول، فوجب التحرّي في خبره للضرورة، أي أخذه المستجمع لتلك الشرائط إلخ فلو شرط في هذا القسم ما ذكرنا من الشرائط لتعطلت الأمور ووقع الفتور. ولا دليل مع الخ: هذه مقدمة أخرى لبيان لزوم الضرورة، والأولى كانت لبيان الضرورة. والحاصل أن في تلك المعاملات لا دليل عند السامع حتى يعمل به وقت عدم اعتبار هذا الخبر، بخلاف ما إذا أخبر الفاسق بنجاسة الماء حيث لا يعمل به؛ لأن عنده دليلا يعمل به وهو أن الأصل في الماء الطهارة، فليست الضرورة لازمة هنا حتى يعمل بخبره، فلذا لايعمل بخبره بغير التحرّي، بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإن الضرورة لازمة فيه ولا مفرّ من العمل بخبره فلذا يعمل به والثاني ما بينه بقوله: ولأن إلخ. وذلك: أي اعتبار هذه الشروط ليصلح أن يكون ملزما إنما يكون فيما يتعلق به اللزوم من أمور الدين. فشرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، بخلاف الخبر فيما نحن فيه؛ لأنه لا إلزام فيه ألا ترى أن الوكيل والعبد لايلزمهما الإقدام على التصرف، وإذا لم يكن ههنا إلزام فأي حاجة إلى اعتبار تلك الشروط، وإليه أشار بقوله : دون ما لا يتعلق إلخ أي شرطنا تلك الشرائط فيما قلنا دون أمور لايتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات التي تنفك عن معنى اللزوم كالوكالات والمضاربات، ولما كان یرد أنه لما قلتم: إن تلك الشرائط شرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، لزم عليكم أن لا تقبلوا خبر الفاسق بحل الطعام وحرمته؛ لأنهما من أمور الدين والفاسق لا يوجد فيه شرط العدالة؟ أجاب عنه بقوله: وإنما اعتبر إلخ. لأن ذلك: أي الوقوف على طهارة الماء ونجاسته وحل الطعام وحرمته أمر خاص بالنسبة إلى رواية الحديث، أي ليس بأمر عام يقف عليه جميع الناس بل أمر خاص قد يقف عليه الفساق خاصة فحينئذ لا يستقيم إلخ. لا يستقيم تلقيه إلخ بخلاف الحديث، فإنه أمر عام كثيراً ما يقف عليه عامة الناس، فيمكن الأخذ من العدول منهم. للضرورة: حاصل الجواب أن خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته إنما يقبل لأجل الضرورة، وهي عدم التلقي من جهة العدول لكونه أمرا خاصا.
Chapter of Sunnah: Report of the fasiq. The second foundation: Sunnah. And it is the correct opinion. Muhammad said regarding the fasiq who reports the impurity of water: The hearer acts on his own opinion; if he feels in his heart that he is truthful, he performs tayammum without pouring out the water; if he pours it out and performs tayammum, it is more precautionary. In the report of the disbeliever, the child, and the insane, if the hearer feels in his heart that they are truthful about the impurity of water, he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum; if he pours out the water and then performs tayammum, it is better. In transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion, such as agency, mudaraba, and permission to trade, the report of every discerning person is considered due to the general necessity requiring the dropping of all other conditions. And this is the correct opinion because of the prevalence of sin after the early generation, so the word of one whose state is unknown is not relied upon until his integrity is manifest, even though the original ruling of water is purity. After finishing with the one whose state is unknown, he began with the fasiq and said: 'Muhammad said, etc.' The hearer makes his opinion a judge: i.e., he makes his opinion a judge and thus exercises personal investigation. He performs tayammum without pouring out the water: it is not permissible for him to perform wudu with that water because the strongest opinion regarding what is not known with certainty is like certainty, so the report of a fasiq is not taken into account regarding the impurity of water; rather, tayammum is obligated upon him due to his dominant conjecture, not due to his report. 'More precautionary for tayammum' due to the possibility that he might be lying in his report; in that case tayammum is not permissible for him because of the existence of pure water, so the precaution is to pour out the water to become one who lacks it, then tayammum becomes permissible for him with certainty, even if his strongest opinion is that he is lying in his report. If a disbeliever, child, or insane person reports, his ruling is as the author explained by his saying: 'and in the report of the disbeliever, etc.' He does not perform tayammum because their reports are not considered, because considering their reports would entail compulsion, and these persons have no authority of compulsion. 'It is better' because the possibility of truthfulness is not cut off from their report; for disbelief, childhood, and insanity do not preclude truthfulness. On this assumption, it is not permissible for him to perform wudu with the impure water, so he may first pour out the water to become one who lacks it, then perform tayammum. The transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion—and he distinguishes by this from transactions that contain pure compulsion from the rights of slaves that involve litigation, for in those transactions testimony is not accepted without legal capacity and eligibility, and the wording of testimony and number. Similarly, he distinguishes from rights that contain compulsion from one aspect and not another, such as dismissing an agent and placing a restricted person under guardianship, for in these one of the two conditions of testimony is required: either integrity or number, considering the meaning of compulsion and its absence. Examples: agency like saying 'he appointed you as agent'; mudaraba like saying 'so-and-so made you a mudarib'; permission to trade like saying to a slave 'your master has permitted you to trade'. In such transactions, the report of every discerning person is considered: just or unjust, child or adult, Muslim or disbeliever, so that the report of the fasiq, the child, and the disbeliever is accepted for two reasons: one is what he explained by his saying 'due to the general necessity', dropping all the mentioned conditions of Islam, integrity, complete intellect, and accuracy. For a person rarely finds one who combines those conditions to send as his agent or servant, and the hearer has no evidence to act upon except this report. The second is his saying: 'And because consideration of these conditions is to give preponderance to the side of truthfulness in the report so that it becomes suitable for being binding, and that is regarding matters that involve compulsion in religious affairs, not regarding matters that do not involve compulsion from the transactions.' He only considered the report of the fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food and the purity and impurity of water when it is supported by the strongest opinion, because that is a specific matter that cannot be properly received from righteous persons alone, so investigation is obliged in his report due to necessity. 'One who combines those conditions, etc.' — if conditions were stipulated in this section as mentioned, matters would become disrupted and slackness would occur. 'And no evidence with the hearer' — this is another premise to explain the necessity of compulsion, while the first was to explain necessity. The conclusion is that in those transactions there is no evidence with the hearer to act upon when this report is not considered, unlike when a fasiq reports the impurity of water where he is not acted upon, because he has evidence to act upon: the original purity of water. So necessity is not binding here to act upon his report; hence his report is not acted upon without investigation, unlike our case where necessity is binding and there is no escape from acting upon his report, so it is acted upon. The second reason is what he explained by his saying 'And because, etc.' That is: consideration of these conditions to make it suitable for being binding only pertains to what involves compulsion from religious affairs. So we stipulated them in religious affairs because of the compulsion they entail, unlike the report in our case because there is no compulsion in it. Do you not see that the agent and the slave are not compelled to proceed with the transaction? And when there is no compulsion here, what need is there to consider those conditions? And he pointed to this by his saying: 'in matters that do not involve compulsion'. Then when it might be objected: Since you said that we stipulate those conditions in religious affairs because they entail compulsion, it follows that you should not accept the report of a fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food, because they are religious affairs and the fasiq does not possess the condition of integrity. He answered by his saying: 'he only considered, etc.' Because that: i.e., ascertaining the purity and impurity of water and the permissibility and prohibition of food is a specific matter relative to narrating hadith, i.e., it is not a general matter known to all people but a specific matter that only the sinful may know. In that case, it cannot be properly received from righteous persons, unlike hadith, which is a general matter frequently known to the general public, so it is possible to take from the righteous among them. 'Due to necessity': the sum of the answer is that the report of a fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food is accepted only due to necessity, which is the inability to receive it from righteous persons because it is a specific matter.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from a Hanafi usul work on the topic of accepting reports (khabar) from various categories of people. It addresses three distinct legal scenarios: (1) reports about impurity of water from a fasiq (sinner), (2) reports about impurity from a kafir, child, or insane person, and (3) reports in non-binding transactions like agency and mudaraba. The author first clarifies the correct position (al-sahih) that a report from a fasiq concerning najasa of water is not accepted outright; instead, the hearer must exercise personal judgment (taharrī). If his dominant conjecture suggests truthfulness, he performs tayammum without pouring the water, but pouring first is more precautionary. This is because the fasiq's report lacks authority, and the original ruling of water purity remains a counter-evidence. For a kafir, child, or insane person, their report is completely disregarded—they cannot impose obligations. However, if the hearer pours the water and then performs tayammum, it is better due to the possibility of truthfulness. The commentary then turns to non-binding transactions, where any discerning person's report is accepted regardless of integrity, religion, or age. This is due to necessity: people rarely find fully qualified witnesses for such everyday matters, and there is no alternative evidence. The reasoning distinguishes between binding matters (religious obligations) where conditions like 'adalah are required, and non-binding matters where no compulsion exists, so conditions are relaxed. The final part addresses a potential objection: if religious matters require 'adalah, why is a fasiq's report accepted for food and water issues? The answer is that such specific knowledge is often only available from the sinful, so accepting it is a necessity not present in general hadith narration.

Key Terms
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking 'adalah (moral integrity).
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Personal investigation or weighing of probabilities to determine the most likely truth when evidence is conflicting or incomplete.
الإلزام (al-ilzām): The legal compulsion or binding effect of a report or testimony, necessitating fulfillment of obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a kāfir reports the impurity of water and the hearer believes him?
A) He must pour out the water and perform tayammum
B) He may perform wudu with the water and tayammum is not allowed
C) He investigates and acts on his strongest opinion
D) He performs tayammum without pouring the water

Key Takeaway
A fasiq's report on impurity triggers personal investigation (taharrī), while reports from a kafir, child, or insane person are completely disregarded due to their lack of authority for binding effects.

Reports in Non-Binding Transactions: Agency, Mudaraba, and Permission to Trade
Ruling on accepting reports in non-binding transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the report of any discerning person (mumayyiz) is accepted in non-binding transactions, and explain the two reasons based on general necessity and the absence of compulsion.

Core Idea
In non-binding transactions, necessity dictates accepting reports from any discerning person, regardless of integrity or religion.

The Hanafi school recognizes that in everyday transactions like agency and mudaraba, requiring a just, adult, Muslim witness is impractical. This lesson explains why the report of any discerning person—even a fasiq, child, or kafir—is accepted in such matters, and how this differs from binding transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of transactions
The passage mentions agency (wakala), mudaraba, and permission to trade (idhn fi al-tijara). These are non-binding (munfakka 'an ma'na al-ilzam) because the agent or slave is not compelled to act.
They contrast with transactions that involve pure compulsion, like litigation.
2
State the ruling: report of any discerning person is accepted
The rule: in these transactions, the report of every mumayyiz (discerning person) is considered, regardless of whether he is just, a child, a disbeliever, etc.
This includes the fasiq, the child, and the kafir—all whose reports were rejected in the impurity case.
3
Explain the first reason: general necessity
People rarely find someone who combines all conditions (Islam, 'adalah, complete intellect, accuracy) to send as an agent. If such conditions were required, transactions would be disrupted.
This is a necessity (darura) that overrides the usual requirements.
4
Explain the second reason: absence of compulsion (ilzam)
Conditions like 'adalah are meant to ensure the report is suitable for being binding. In these transactions, there is no compulsion (ilzam) because the agent or slave is not forced to act. Therefore, the stringent conditions are not needed.
The passage contrasts with matters of din (religion) where ilzam exists, thus requiring conditions.
5
Distinguish from cases with partial compulsion
In matters like dismissing an agent or placing someone under guardianship, there is partial ilzam, so one of the two conditions ('adalah or number of witnesses) is required.
This shows that the degree of compulsion affects the required conditions.

اعتبارا لمعنى الإلزام وعدمه. كالوكالات بأن قال: فإن وكلك والمضاربات بأن قال: فلان جعلك مضارباً. والإذن في التجارة: بأن قال لعبد: إن مولاك أذن لك في التجارة، فإن في تلك المعاملات يعتبر خبر كل إلخ. كل مميز : عدلاً كان أو غير عدل، صبياً كان أو بالغا، مسلما كان أو كافراً، حتى يقبل خبر الفاسق والصبي والكافر لوجهين، أحدهما ما بينه بقوله: لعموم الضرورة إلخ. سائر الشرائط المذكورة من الإسلام والعدالة والعقل الكامل والضبط. فإن الإنسان قلما يجد المستجمع لتلك الشرائط يبعثه إلى وكيله أو غلامه، ولا دليل مع السامع يعمل به سوى هذا الخبر، ولأن اعتبار هذه الشرائط ليترجح جهة الصدق في الخبر فيصلح أن يكون ملزماً، وذلك فيما يتعلّق به اللزوم أمور الدين دون ما لا يتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات، وإنما اعتبر خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته وطهارة الماء ونجاسته إذا تأيد بأكبر الرأي؛ لأن ذلك أمر خاص لا يستقيم تلقيه من جهة العدول، فوجب التحرّي في خبره للضرورة، أي أخذه المستجمع لتلك الشرائط إلخ فلو شرط في هذا القسم ما ذكرنا من الشرائط لتعطلت الأمور ووقع الفتور. ولا دليل مع الخ: هذه مقدمة أخرى لبيان لزوم الضرورة، والأولى كانت لبيان الضرورة. والحاصل أن في تلك المعاملات لا دليل عند السامع حتى يعمل به وقت عدم اعتبار هذا الخبر، بخلاف ما إذا أخبر الفاسق بنجاسة الماء حيث لا يعمل به؛ لأن عنده دليلا يعمل به وهو أن الأصل في الماء الطهارة، فليست الضرورة لازمة هنا حتى يعمل بخبره، فلذا لايعمل بخبره بغير التحرّي، بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإن الضرورة لازمة فيه ولا مفرّ من العمل بخبره فلذا يعمل به والثاني ما بينه بقوله: ولأن إلخ. وذلك: أي اعتبار هذه الشروط ليصلح أن يكون ملزما إنما يكون فيما يتعلق به اللزوم من أمور الدين. فشرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، بخلاف الخبر فيما نحن فيه؛ لأنه لا إلزام فيه ألا ترى أن الوكيل والعبد لايلزمهما الإقدام على التصرف، وإذا لم يكن ههنا إلزام فأي حاجة إلى اعتبار تلك الشروط، وإليه أشار بقوله : دون ما لا يتعلق إلخ أي شرطنا تلك الشرائط فيما قلنا دون أمور لايتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات التي تنفك عن معنى اللزوم كالوكالات والمضاربات، ولما كان یرد أنه لما قلتم: إن تلك الشرائط شرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، لزم عليكم أن لا تقبلوا خبر الفاسق بحل الطعام وحرمته؛ لأنهما من أمور الدين والفاسق لا يوجد فيه شرط العدالة؟ أجاب عنه بقوله: وإنما اعتبر إلخ. لأن ذلك: أي الوقوف على طهارة الماء ونجاسته وحل الطعام وحرمته أمر خاص بالنسبة إلى رواية الحديث، أي ليس بأمر عام يقف عليه جميع الناس بل أمر خاص قد يقف عليه الفساق خاصة فحينئذ لا يستقيم إلخ. لا يستقيم تلقيه إلخ بخلاف الحديث، فإنه أمر عام كثيراً ما يقف عليه عامة الناس، فيمكن الأخذ من العدول منهم. للضرورة: حاصل الجواب أن خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته إنما يقبل لأجل الضرورة، وهي عدم التلقي من جهة العدول لكونه أمرا خاصا.
Chapter of Sunnah: Report of the fasiq. The second foundation: Sunnah. And it is the correct opinion. Muhammad said regarding the fasiq who reports the impurity of water: The hearer acts on his own opinion; if he feels in his heart that he is truthful, he performs tayammum without pouring out the water; if he pours it out and performs tayammum, it is more precautionary. In the report of the disbeliever, the child, and the insane, if the hearer feels in his heart that they are truthful about the impurity of water, he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum; if he pours out the water and then performs tayammum, it is better. In transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion, such as agency, mudaraba, and permission to trade, the report of every discerning person is considered due to the general necessity requiring the dropping of all other conditions. And this is the correct opinion because of the prevalence of sin after the early generation, so the word of one whose state is unknown is not relied upon until his integrity is manifest, even though the original ruling of water is purity. After finishing with the one whose state is unknown, he began with the fasiq and said: 'Muhammad said, etc.' The hearer makes his opinion a judge: i.e., he makes his opinion a judge and thus exercises personal investigation. He performs tayammum without pouring out the water: it is not permissible for him to perform wudu with that water because the strongest opinion regarding what is not known with certainty is like certainty, so the report of a fasiq is not taken into account regarding the impurity of water; rather, tayammum is obligated upon him due to his dominant conjecture, not due to his report. 'More precautionary for tayammum' due to the possibility that he might be lying in his report; in that case tayammum is not permissible for him because of the existence of pure water, so the precaution is to pour out the water to become one who lacks it, then tayammum becomes permissible for him with certainty, even if his strongest opinion is that he is lying in his report. If a disbeliever, child, or insane person reports, his ruling is as the author explained by his saying: 'and in the report of the disbeliever, etc.' He does not perform tayammum because their reports are not considered, because considering their reports would entail compulsion, and these persons have no authority of compulsion. 'It is better' because the possibility of truthfulness is not cut off from their report; for disbelief, childhood, and insanity do not preclude truthfulness. On this assumption, it is not permissible for him to perform wudu with the impure water, so he may first pour out the water to become one who lacks it, then perform tayammum. The transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion—and he distinguishes by this from transactions that contain pure compulsion from the rights of slaves that involve litigation, for in those transactions testimony is not accepted without legal capacity and eligibility, and the wording of testimony and number. Similarly, he distinguishes from rights that contain compulsion from one aspect and not another, such as dismissing an agent and placing a restricted person under guardianship, for in these one of the two conditions of testimony is required: either integrity or number, considering the meaning of compulsion and its absence. Examples: agency like saying 'he appointed you as agent'; mudaraba like saying 'so-and-so made you a mudarib'; permission to trade like saying to a slave 'your master has permitted you to trade'. In such transactions, the report of every discerning person is considered: just or unjust, child or adult, Muslim or disbeliever, so that the report of the fasiq, the child, and the disbeliever is accepted for two reasons: one is what he explained by his saying 'due to the general necessity', dropping all the mentioned conditions of Islam, integrity, complete intellect, and accuracy. For a person rarely finds one who combines those conditions to send as his agent or servant, and the hearer has no evidence to act upon except this report. The second is his saying: 'And because consideration of these conditions is to give preponderance to the side of truthfulness in the report so that it becomes suitable for being binding, and that is regarding matters that involve compulsion in religious affairs, not regarding matters that do not involve compulsion from the transactions.' He only considered the report of the fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food and the purity and impurity of water when it is supported by the strongest opinion, because that is a specific matter that cannot be properly received from righteous persons alone, so investigation is obliged in his report due to necessity. 'One who combines those conditions, etc.' — if conditions were stipulated in this section as mentioned, matters would become disrupted and slackness would occur. 'And no evidence with the hearer' — this is another premise to explain the necessity of compulsion, while the first was to explain necessity. The conclusion is that in those transactions there is no evidence with the hearer to act upon when this report is not considered, unlike when a fasiq reports the impurity of water where he is not acted upon, because he has evidence to act upon: the original purity of water. So necessity is not binding here to act upon his report; hence his report is not acted upon without investigation, unlike our case where necessity is binding and there is no escape from acting upon his report, so it is acted upon. The second reason is what he explained by his saying 'And because, etc.' That is: consideration of these conditions to make it suitable for being binding only pertains to what involves compulsion from religious affairs. So we stipulated them in religious affairs because of the compulsion they entail, unlike the report in our case because there is no compulsion in it. Do you not see that the agent and the slave are not compelled to proceed with the transaction? And when there is no compulsion here, what need is there to consider those conditions? And he pointed to this by his saying: 'in matters that do not involve compulsion'. Then when it might be objected: Since you said that we stipulate those conditions in religious affairs because they entail compulsion, it follows that you should not accept the report of a fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food, because they are religious affairs and the fasiq does not possess the condition of integrity. He answered by his saying: 'he only considered, etc.' Because that: i.e., ascertaining the purity and impurity of water and the permissibility and prohibition of food is a specific matter relative to narrating hadith, i.e., it is not a general matter known to all people but a specific matter that only the sinful may know. In that case, it cannot be properly received from righteous persons, unlike hadith, which is a general matter frequently known to the general public, so it is possible to take from the righteous among them. 'Due to necessity': the sum of the answer is that the report of a fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food is accepted only due to necessity, which is the inability to receive it from righteous persons because it is a specific matter.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from a Hanafi usul work on the topic of accepting reports (khabar) from various categories of people. It addresses three distinct legal scenarios: (1) reports about impurity of water from a fasiq (sinner), (2) reports about impurity from a kafir, child, or insane person, and (3) reports in non-binding transactions like agency and mudaraba. The author first clarifies the correct position (al-sahih) that a report from a fasiq concerning najasa of water is not accepted outright; instead, the hearer must exercise personal judgment (taharrī). If his dominant conjecture suggests truthfulness, he performs tayammum without pouring the water, but pouring first is more precautionary. This is because the fasiq's report lacks authority, and the original ruling of water purity remains a counter-evidence. For a kafir, child, or insane person, their report is completely disregarded—they cannot impose obligations. However, if the hearer pours the water and then performs tayammum, it is better due to the possibility of truthfulness. The commentary then turns to non-binding transactions, where any discerning person's report is accepted regardless of integrity, religion, or age. This is due to necessity: people rarely find fully qualified witnesses for such everyday matters, and there is no alternative evidence. The reasoning distinguishes between binding matters (religious obligations) where conditions like 'adalah are required, and non-binding matters where no compulsion exists, so conditions are relaxed. The final part addresses a potential objection: if religious matters require 'adalah, why is a fasiq's report accepted for food and water issues? The answer is that such specific knowledge is often only available from the sinful, so accepting it is a necessity not present in general hadith narration.

Key Terms
المميز (al-mumayyiz): A person who has reached the age of discernment (tamyīz), able to understand and communicate meaningfully, regardless of age or religion.
الإلزام (al-ilzām): The legal compulsion or binding effect of a report or testimony, necessitating fulfillment of obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the report of any discerning person accepted in non-binding transactions?
A) Because such reports are always truthful
B) Because of general necessity and the absence of compulsion
C) Because the Quran explicitly commands it
D) Because the reporters are usually adults

Key Takeaway
In non-binding transactions, necessity overrides the usual conditions of report acceptance, allowing any discerning person's report to be acted upon.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
7 min
The Necessity Exception: Why a Fasiq's Report is Accepted for Food and Water
Objection and response regarding fasiq's report on food and water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi justification for accepting a fasiq's report on food permissibility and water purity, and distinguish this from general hadith narration.

Core Idea
A fasiq's report on food and water is accepted because only sinful people may have that specific knowledge, making necessity override the usual condition of 'adalah.

An objection arises: if the Hanafi school requires 'adalah for binding religious matters, why do they accept a fasiq's report on the permissibility of food and the impurity of water? This lesson unpacks the sophisticated answer: these are specialized matters not widely known, so necessity allows acceptance of reports from those who know them, even if they are sinful.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector says: You Hanafis require 'adalah for religious matters because they involve ilzam. Yet you accept a fasiq's report on food and water. Isn't food and water a religious matter?
This objection is based on consistency: if ilzam requires 'adalah, then all religious matters should have that condition.
2
State the Hanafi response: specific knowledge
The answer: matters of food permissibility and water purity are specific (khass) not general. They are often known only to certain people, including fasiqs. Requiring 'adalah here would make it impossible to obtain this knowledge.
Thus, necessity (darura) justifies accepting the fasiq's report.
3
Contrast with hadith narration
Hadith narration is a general matter known to many people; it is possible to take from just ('adil) narrators. Therefore, the condition of 'adalah is maintained.
The difference lies in the generality of knowledge: specific vs. general.
4
Analyze the role of taharri
Even for food and water, the fasiq's report is not accepted outright; it is supported by taharri (the hearer's dominant conjecture). This ensures that the report is not followed blindly.
This connects back to the first lesson: taharri is required even when necessity allows consideration.
5
Summarize the principle
Conditions for accepting reports are relaxed when necessity demands it and when the matter is specific such that only certain people possess the knowledge. This is a general usul principle in Hanafi madhhab.
The passage labels this as 'الضرورة' (necessity) and 'الأمر الخاص' (specific matter).

Source Text

باب السنة خبر الفاسق ۱۳۷ الأصل الثاني السنة وهو الصحيح. وقال محمد له في الفاسق يخبر بنجاسة الماء: إنه يحكم السامع رأيه، فإن وقع في قلبه أنه صادق يتيمّم من غير إراقة الماء، فإن أراق وتيمّم فهو أحوط أي المخبر الماء للتيمّم، وفي خبر الكافر والصبي والمعتوه إذا وقع في قلب السامع صدقهم بنجاسة الماء يتوضأ ولا يتيمم، فإن أراق الماء ثم تيمّم فهو أفضل، وفي المعاملات التي تنفك عن معنى الإلزام كالوكالات والمضاربات والإذن في التجارة يعتبر خبر كل مميز؛ لعموم الضرورة الداعية إلى سقوط سائر الشرائط، وهو الصحيح لظهور الفسق فيما بعد الصدر الأول، فلا يعتمد على قول المستور ما لم يظهر عدالته مع أن الأصل في الماء هو الطهور. ولما فرغ عن المستور شرع في الفاسق فقال: وقال محمد إلخ. يحكم السامع رأيه: أي يجعل السامع رأيه حاكماً فيتحرّى يتيمم من غير إراقة الماء: فلا يجوز له الوضوء من ذلك الماء؛ لأن أكبر الرأي فيما لم يوقف على حقيقته كاليقين فخبر الفاسق لا يعتد به في نجاسة الماء، وإنما وجب عليه التيمم من غلبة ظنه لا بخبره. أحوط للتيمم لاحتمال أنه كاذب في خبره، فحينئذ لا يجوز له التيمم لوجود الماء الطاهر، فالاحتياط أن الماء ليصير عادماً له، فحينئذ يجوز له التيمم يقيناً وإن كان أكبر رأيه أنه كاذب في خبره، وأما لو أخبر الكافر والصبي والمعتوه فحكمه ما بينه المصنّف بقوله : وفي خبر الكافر إلخ. ولا يتيمم لعدم الاعتبار بخبرهم، وذلك لأن في اعتبار أخبارهم إلزاما، وهؤلاء ليس لهم ولاية الإلزام. فهو أفضل لأن احتمال الصدق غير منقطع عن خبرهم؛ لأن الكفر والصبا والعته لاينافي الصدق؛ وعلى هذا التقدير لايجوز له التوضؤ بالماء النجس فله أن يريق الماء أولاً ليصير عادما له ثم يتيمّم. التي تنفك عن معنى الإلزام، واحترز به عن المعاملات التي فيها إلزام محض من حقوق العباد التي تجري فيها الخصومات، فإن في تلك المعاملات لا يقبل الشهادة بغير الولاية والأهلية، ولفظ الشهادة والعدد، وكذلك احترز به عن الحقوق التي فيها إلزام من وجه دون وجه، كعزل الوكيل وحجر المأذون، فإن فيها يشترط أحد شرطي الشهادة إما العدالة وإما العدد اعتبارا لمعنى الإلزام وعدمه. كالوكالات بأن قال: فإن وكلك والمضاربات بأن قال: فلان جعلك مضارباً. والإذن في التجارة: بأن قال لعبد: إن مولاك أذن لك في التجارة، فإن في تلك المعاملات يعتبر خبر كل إلخ. كل مميز : عدلاً كان أو غير عدل، صبياً كان أو بالغا، مسلما كان أو كافراً، حتى يقبل خبر الفاسق والصبي والكافر لوجهين، أحدهما ما بينه بقوله: لعموم الضرورة إلخ. سائر الشرائط المذكورة من الإسلام والعدالة والعقل الكامل والضبط. فإن الإنسان قلما يجد المستجمع لتلك الشرائط يبعثه إلى وكيله أو غلامه، ولا دليل مع السامع يعمل به سوى هذا الخبر، ولأن اعتبار هذه الشرائط ليترجح جهة الصدق في الخبر فيصلح أن يكون ملزماً، وذلك فيما يتعلّق به اللزوم أمور الدين دون ما لا يتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات، وإنما اعتبر خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته وطهارة الماء ونجاسته إذا تأيد بأكبر الرأي؛ لأن ذلك أمر خاص لا يستقيم تلقيه من جهة العدول، فوجب التحرّي في خبره للضرورة، أي أخذه المستجمع لتلك الشرائط إلخ فلو شرط في هذا القسم ما ذكرنا من الشرائط لتعطلت الأمور ووقع الفتور. ولا دليل مع الخ: هذه مقدمة أخرى لبيان لزوم الضرورة، والأولى كانت لبيان الضرورة. والحاصل أن في تلك المعاملات لا دليل عند السامع حتى يعمل به وقت عدم اعتبار هذا الخبر، بخلاف ما إذا أخبر الفاسق بنجاسة الماء حيث لا يعمل به؛ لأن عنده دليلا يعمل به وهو أن الأصل في الماء الطهارة، فليست الضرورة لازمة هنا حتى يعمل بخبره، فلذا لايعمل بخبره بغير التحرّي، بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإن الضرورة لازمة فيه ولا مفرّ من العمل بخبره فلذا يعمل به والثاني ما بينه بقوله: ولأن إلخ. وذلك: أي اعتبار هذه الشروط ليصلح أن يكون ملزما إنما يكون فيما يتعلق به اللزوم من أمور الدين. فشرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، بخلاف الخبر فيما نحن فيه؛ لأنه لا إلزام فيه ألا ترى أن الوكيل والعبد لايلزمهما الإقدام على التصرف، وإذا لم يكن ههنا إلزام فأي حاجة إلى اعتبار تلك الشروط، وإليه أشار بقوله : دون ما لا يتعلق إلخ أي شرطنا تلك الشرائط فيما قلنا دون أمور لايتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات التي تنفك عن معنى اللزوم كالوكالات والمضاربات، ولما كان یرد أنه لما قلتم: إن تلك الشرائط شرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، لزم عليكم أن لا تقبلوا خبر الفاسق بحل الطعام وحرمته؛ لأنهما من أمور الدين والفاسق لا يوجد فيه شرط العدالة؟ أجاب عنه بقوله: وإنما اعتبر إلخ. لأن ذلك: أي الوقوف على طهارة الماء ونجاسته وحل الطعام وحرمته أمر خاص بالنسبة إلى رواية الحديث، أي ليس بأمر عام يقف عليه جميع الناس بل أمر خاص قد يقف عليه الفساق خاصة فحينئذ لا يستقيم إلخ. لا يستقيم تلقيه إلخ بخلاف الحديث، فإنه أمر عام كثيراً ما يقف عليه عامة الناس، فيمكن الأخذ من العدول منهم. للضرورة: حاصل الجواب أن خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته إنما يقبل لأجل الضرورة، وهي عدم التلقي من جهة العدول لكونه أمرا خاصا.
Chapter of Sunnah: Report of the fasiq. The second foundation: Sunnah. And it is the correct opinion. Muhammad said regarding the fasiq who reports the impurity of water: The hearer acts on his own opinion; if he feels in his heart that he is truthful, he performs tayammum without pouring out the water; if he pours it out and performs tayammum, it is more precautionary. In the report of the disbeliever, the child, and the insane, if the hearer feels in his heart that they are truthful about the impurity of water, he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum; if he pours out the water and then performs tayammum, it is better. In transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion, such as agency, mudaraba, and permission to trade, the report of every discerning person is considered due to the general necessity requiring the dropping of all other conditions. And this is the correct opinion because of the prevalence of sin after the early generation, so the word of one whose state is unknown is not relied upon until his integrity is manifest, even though the original ruling of water is purity. After finishing with the one whose state is unknown, he began with the fasiq and said: 'Muhammad said, etc.' The hearer makes his opinion a judge: i.e., he makes his opinion a judge and thus exercises personal investigation. He performs tayammum without pouring out the water: it is not permissible for him to perform wudu with that water because the strongest opinion regarding what is not known with certainty is like certainty, so the report of a fasiq is not taken into account regarding the impurity of water; rather, tayammum is obligated upon him due to his dominant conjecture, not due to his report. 'More precautionary for tayammum' due to the possibility that he might be lying in his report; in that case tayammum is not permissible for him because of the existence of pure water, so the precaution is to pour out the water to become one who lacks it, then tayammum becomes permissible for him with certainty, even if his strongest opinion is that he is lying in his report. If a disbeliever, child, or insane person reports, his ruling is as the author explained by his saying: 'and in the report of the disbeliever, etc.' He does not perform tayammum because their reports are not considered, because considering their reports would entail compulsion, and these persons have no authority of compulsion. 'It is better' because the possibility of truthfulness is not cut off from their report; for disbelief, childhood, and insanity do not preclude truthfulness. On this assumption, it is not permissible for him to perform wudu with the impure water, so he may first pour out the water to become one who lacks it, then perform tayammum. The transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion—and he distinguishes by this from transactions that contain pure compulsion from the rights of slaves that involve litigation, for in those transactions testimony is not accepted without legal capacity and eligibility, and the wording of testimony and number. Similarly, he distinguishes from rights that contain compulsion from one aspect and not another, such as dismissing an agent and placing a restricted person under guardianship, for in these one of the two conditions of testimony is required: either integrity or number, considering the meaning of compulsion and its absence. Examples: agency like saying 'he appointed you as agent'; mudaraba like saying 'so-and-so made you a mudarib'; permission to trade like saying to a slave 'your master has permitted you to trade'. In such transactions, the report of every discerning person is considered: just or unjust, child or adult, Muslim or disbeliever, so that the report of the fasiq, the child, and the disbeliever is accepted for two reasons: one is what he explained by his saying 'due to the general necessity', dropping all the mentioned conditions of Islam, integrity, complete intellect, and accuracy. For a person rarely finds one who combines those conditions to send as his agent or servant, and the hearer has no evidence to act upon except this report. The second is his saying: 'And because consideration of these conditions is to give preponderance to the side of truthfulness in the report so that it becomes suitable for being binding, and that is regarding matters that involve compulsion in religious affairs, not regarding matters that do not involve compulsion from the transactions.' He only considered the report of the fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food and the purity and impurity of water when it is supported by the strongest opinion, because that is a specific matter that cannot be properly received from righteous persons alone, so investigation is obliged in his report due to necessity. 'One who combines those conditions, etc.' — if conditions were stipulated in this section as mentioned, matters would become disrupted and slackness would occur. 'And no evidence with the hearer' — this is another premise to explain the necessity of compulsion, while the first was to explain necessity. The conclusion is that in those transactions there is no evidence with the hearer to act upon when this report is not considered, unlike when a fasiq reports the impurity of water where he is not acted upon, because he has evidence to act upon: the original purity of water. So necessity is not binding here to act upon his report; hence his report is not acted upon without investigation, unlike our case where necessity is binding and there is no escape from acting upon his report, so it is acted upon. The second reason is what he explained by his saying 'And because, etc.' That is: consideration of these conditions to make it suitable for being binding only pertains to what involves compulsion from religious affairs. So we stipulated them in religious affairs because of the compulsion they entail, unlike the report in our case because there is no compulsion in it. Do you not see that the agent and the slave are not compelled to proceed with the transaction? And when there is no compulsion here, what need is there to consider those conditions? And he pointed to this by his saying: 'in matters that do not involve compulsion'. Then when it might be objected: Since you said that we stipulate those conditions in religious affairs because they entail compulsion, it follows that you should not accept the report of a fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food, because they are religious affairs and the fasiq does not possess the condition of integrity. He answered by his saying: 'he only considered, etc.' Because that: i.e., ascertaining the purity and impurity of water and the permissibility and prohibition of food is a specific matter relative to narrating hadith, i.e., it is not a general matter known to all people but a specific matter that only the sinful may know. In that case, it cannot be properly received from righteous persons, unlike hadith, which is a general matter frequently known to the general public, so it is possible to take from the righteous among them. 'Due to necessity': the sum of the answer is that the report of a fasiq regarding the permissibility and prohibition of food is accepted only due to necessity, which is the inability to receive it from righteous persons because it is a specific matter.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from a Hanafi usul work on the topic of accepting reports (khabar) from various categories of people. It addresses three distinct legal scenarios: (1) reports about impurity of water from a fasiq (sinner), (2) reports about impurity from a kafir, child, or insane person, and (3) reports in non-binding transactions like agency and mudaraba. The author first clarifies the correct position (al-sahih) that a report from a fasiq concerning najasa of water is not accepted outright; instead, the hearer must exercise personal judgment (taharrī). If his dominant conjecture suggests truthfulness, he performs tayammum without pouring the water, but pouring first is more precautionary. This is because the fasiq's report lacks authority, and the original ruling of water purity remains a counter-evidence. For a kafir, child, or insane person, their report is completely disregarded—they cannot impose obligations. However, if the hearer pours the water and then performs tayammum, it is better due to the possibility of truthfulness. The commentary then turns to non-binding transactions, where any discerning person's report is accepted regardless of integrity, religion, or age. This is due to necessity: people rarely find fully qualified witnesses for such everyday matters, and there is no alternative evidence. The reasoning distinguishes between binding matters (religious obligations) where conditions like 'adalah are required, and non-binding matters where no compulsion exists, so conditions are relaxed. The final part addresses a potential objection: if religious matters require 'adalah, why is a fasiq's report accepted for food and water issues? The answer is that such specific knowledge is often only available from the sinful, so accepting it is a necessity not present in general hadith narration.

Key Terms
الضرورة (al-darūra): Legal necessity that permits relaxation of normal rules to prevent hardship.
الأمر الخاص (al-amr al-khāṣṣ): A specific matter not widely known, often known only to a limited group of people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a fasiq's report on food permissibility accepted despite being a religious matter?
A) Because food matters are less important than prayer
B) Because it is a specific matter that may only be known to the fasiq, making acceptance necessary
C) Because the Hanafi school does not consider food permissibility a religious matter
D) Because the fasiq's integrity is assumed in such matters

Key Takeaway
A fasiq's report on food permissibility and water purity is accepted with taharri due to the specific nature of such knowledge and the necessity of obtaining it from those who possess it.

Accepting a Sinner's Report: Necessity Overrides 'Adala in Transactions
Explains why a fasiq's report is accepted in transactions with scrutiny

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing between binding religious reports and non-binding transactional reports, and identify when a fasiq's report is accepted with scrutiny.

Core Idea
A fasiq's report is accepted in transactions due to necessity, but not in binding religious matters requiring 'adala.

In Hanafi usul, not all reports are treated equally. The school draws a sharp line between matters that bind (umur al-din) and those that do not (mu'amalat). This lesson unpacks why a sinner's report, normally rejected for lack of integrity, becomes permissible in everyday transactions and specialized fields like food purity—provided scrutiny is applied. You will see how necessity (darura) overrides the standard condition of 'adala, and where the limits of this exception lie.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish binding and non-binding reports
Identify the two categories in the passage: religious matters (din) require the reporter to have 'adala (integrity) because the accepted report becomes binding (luzum). Transactions (mu'amalat) do not involve such binding, so the strict condition is relaxed.
The binding nature is key: in hadith, acceptance implies obligation; in agency, no one is forced to act.
2
Identify the necessity exception
Note that in transactions and specialized fields (food/water), the fasiq's report is accepted because trustworthy reporters are scarce. The text says: 'people rarely find one who combines those conditions' and 'the listener has no evidence to act upon except this report.'
Necessity (darura) is the illa (cause) for the exception.
3
Apply the condition of scrutiny (taharri)
The fasiq's report is not blindly accepted; it must be supported by 'the greater opinion' (akbar al-ra'y) or scrutiny. The reporter must also be eligible for testimony (ahl al-shahada) and free from suspicion of lying.
This prevents unconditional acceptance and maintains some gatekeeping.
4
Analyze the objection and response
Consider the objection: if religious matters require 'adala, why accept the fasiq's report on food/water (which are religious)? The author answers: these are specific matters not commonly known by trustworthy people, so necessity demands acceptance.
The response shows that the exception is narrowly tailored to necessity.

Source Text

فإن الإنسان قلما يجد المستجمع لتلك الشرائط يبعثه إلى وكيله أو غلامه، ولا دليل مع السامع يعمل به سوى هذا الخبر، ولأن اعتبار هذه الشرائط ليترجح جهة الصدق في الخبر فيصلح أن يكون ملزماً، وذلك فيما يتعلّق به اللزوم أمور الدين دون ما لا يتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات، وإنما اعتبر خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته وطهارة الماء ونجاسته إذا تأيد بأكبر الرأي؛ لأن ذلك أمر خاص لا يستقيم تلقيه من جهة العدول، فوجب التحرّي في خبره للضرورة، المستجمع لتلك الشرائط إلخ فلو شرط في هذا القسم ما ذكرنا من الشرائط لتعطلت الأمور ووقع الفتور. ولا دليل مع الخ: هذه مقدمة أخرى لبيان لزوم الضرورة، والأولى كانت لبيان الضرورة. والحاصل أن في تلك المعاملات لا دليل عند السامع حتى يعمل به وقت عدم اعتبار هذا الخبر، بخلاف ما إذا أخبر الفاسق بنجاسة الماء حيث لا يعمل به؛ لأن عند دليلا يعمل به وهو أن الأصل في الماء الطهارة، فليست الضرورة لازمة هنا حتى يعمل بخبره، فلذا لا يعمل بخبره بغير التحرّي، بخلاف ما نحن فيه، فإن الضرورة لازمة فيه ولا مفرّ من العمل بخبره فلذا يعمل به. وذلك: أي اعتبار هذه الشروط ليصلح أن يكون ملزما إنما يكون فيما يتعلق به اللزوم من أمور الدين. فشرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، بخلاف الخبر فيما نحن فيه؛ لأنه لا إلزام فيه ألا ترى أن الوكيل والعبد لا يلزمهما الإقدام على التصرف، وإذا لم يكن ههنا إلزام فأي حاجة إلى اعتبار تلك الشروط، وإليه أشار بقوله: دون ما لا يتعلق إلخ أي شرطنا تلك الشرائط في أمور الدين دون الأمور لا يتعلق به اللزوم من المعاملات التي تنفك عن معنى اللزوم كالوكالات والمضاربات. ولما كان يرد أنه لما قلتم: إن تلك الشرائط شرطناها في أمور الدين لما يتعلق بها من اللزوم، لزم عليكم أن لا تقبلوا خبر الفاسق بحل الطعام وحرمته؛ لأنهما من أمور الدين والفاسق لا يوجد فيه شرط العدالة؟ أجاب عنه بقوله: وإنما اعتبر إلخ. لأن ذلك: أي الوقوف على طهارة الماء ونجاسته وحل الطعام وحرمته أمر خاص بالنسبة إلى رواية الحديث، أي ليس بأمر عام يقف عليه جميع الناس بل أمر خاص قد يقف عليه الفساق خاصة فحينئذ لا يستقيم تلقيه من جهة العدول. للضرورة: حاصل الجواب أن خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته إنما يقبل لأجل الضرورة، وهي عدم التلقي من جهة العدول لكونه أمرا خاصا.
For a person rarely finds one who combines those conditions, so he sends his agent or his slave, and the listener has no evidence to act upon except this report. And because requiring these conditions would give preponderance to the side of truthfulness in the report so that it becomes binding, and that is only concerning matters of religion which involve binding obligation, not concerning transactions that do not involve binding obligation. And the report of a sinner is considered regarding the permissibility of food and its prohibition, and the purity of water and its impurity, if supported by the greater opinion, because that is a specific matter that cannot properly be obtained from trustworthy people, so scrutiny in his report is obligatory due to necessity. If we had required those conditions in this section, matters would have come to a standstill and lethargy would have occurred. This is another introduction to explain the necessity of binding, while the first was to explain necessity. The conclusion is that in those transactions the listener has no evidence to act upon at the time of disregarding this report, unlike when a sinner reports the impurity of water, where he does not act upon it because he has evidence to act upon, namely that the original state of water is purity, so necessity is not pressing there for acting upon his report, so his report is not acted upon without scrutiny. In our case, necessity is pressing and there is no escape from acting upon his report, so it is acted upon. That is, requiring these conditions so that it becomes binding only applies to matters of religion that involve binding obligation. So we required them in matters of religion because of the binding involved, unlike the report in our case, because there is no binding in it. Do you not see that the agent and the slave are not obliged to proceed with the transaction? And if there is no binding here, what need is there to require those conditions? He pointed to this by saying: "except matters that do not involve binding obligation," meaning we required those conditions in matters of religion, not in matters that do not involve binding obligation from transactions that are free from the meaning of binding, like agency and mudaraba. And when it might be objected that if you required those conditions in matters of religion due to the binding involved, you would have to not accept the report of a sinner regarding the permissibility of food and its prohibition because these are matters of religion and the sinner lacks the condition of integrity, he answered by saying: "And the report of a sinner is considered" etc. Because that, i.e., knowing the purity of water and its impurity, and the permissibility of food and its prohibition, is a specific matter relative to hadith narration, i.e., it is not a general matter that all people come to know, but a specific matter that may be known only by sinners, so it cannot be obtained from trustworthy people. Due to necessity: the summary of the answer is that the report of a sinner regarding the permissibility of food and its prohibition is only accepted for the sake of necessity, which is the inability to obtain it from trustworthy people because it is a specific matter.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from usul al-fiqh explaining the conditions for accepting the report of a single narrator (khabar al-wahid) when the narrator is a sinner (fasiq). The author distinguishes between matters of religion (umur al-din) which involve binding obligation (luzum) and transactions (mu'amalat) which do not. In matters of religion, strict conditions (justice, memory, etc.) are required because the report, once accepted, becomes binding. In transactions like agency or mudaraba, no such binding exists—the agent is not forced to act—so requiring those conditions would cause hardship and breakdown of practical affairs. Therefore, in transactions, the report of a sinner is accepted with scrutiny (taharri) if necessity demands, because people rarely find a perfectly trustworthy reporter for everyday dealings. However, in matters like food and water purity, the report of a sinner is also accepted with scrutiny because these are specialized fields not commonly known by all trustworthy people. The underlying principle is necessity (darura). The commentary explains that the listener has no other evidence to act upon in these transactions, unlike the case of water where the original ruling (asalat al-tahara) provides a default. Thus, the sinner's report is not accepted blindly but requires the reporter to be at least eligible for testimony (ahliyyat al-shahada) and free from suspicion of lying, unlike a disbeliever or child whose reports are rejected entirely.

Key Terms
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking 'adala (integrity).
التحري (al-taharri): Scrutiny and seeking the best opinion; not mere conjecture but a reasoned effort to determine the truth.
الضرورة (al-darura): A pressing need that makes the otherwise impermissible permissible; here, the inability to obtain the information from trustworthy sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the fasiq is considered a reliable narrator in all fields.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a fasiq's report in non-binding matters to prevent hardship, requiring scrutiny but not the full condition of 'adala.

Rejecting the Report of an Innovator (Sahib al-Hawa)
States the relied-upon ruling that an innovator's report is rejected because he calls to his innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting narrations from an innovator who calls to his innovation, and explain the rationale (ta'lil) for rejection.

Core Idea
The narration of an innovator who calls to his bid'a is rejected because his motive to fabricate is presumed.

This passage addresses a key principle in Hanafi usul al-hadith: the acceptability of narrations from an innovator. The school distinguishes between a mere sinner (fasiq), whose report may be accepted with scrutiny, and an innovator who actively proselytizes his heresy (sahib al-hawa). The latter's narrations are absolutely rejected because his commitment to his innovation creates a strong motive to distort or fabricate hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Identify the type of narrator under consideration: sahib al-hawa (an innovator who calls to his bid'a). This is a specific subset of narrators distinguished from a fasiq.
Sahib al-hawa literally means 'follower of desire' but here refers to a religious innovator.
2
State the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: his narration is not accepted. Note that this is the 'chosen madhhab' (al-madhhab al-mukhtar), meaning it is the operative position for fatwa.
There may be weaker opinions within the school, but this is the relied-upon view.
3
Identify the dalil
Identify the proof: the text cites a causal rationale (ta'lil) — arguing and calling to desire is a cause (sabab) that leads to fabrication (taqawwul). This is based on consensus (ijma) of scholars that such narrators are unreliable.
The dalil is not a specific text but a reasoned consensus.
4
Analyze the ta'lil
Analyze why the motive to fabricate is presumed. The innovator's engagement in polemics (muhajaja) and his missionary zeal create a strong incentive to lie to support his views. This makes his testimony untrustworthy even if he appears outwardly truthful.
The phrase 'which he has taken as his religion' emphasizes that his innovation is now a foundational belief.
5
Contrast with fasiq
Contrast with a fasiq (sinner) who does not call to sin. The fasiq's narration is accepted with scrutiny; the innovator's is absolutely rejected because his motive is stronger and his reliability more compromised.
This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صاحب الهوى فالمذهب المختار أنه لا تقبل رواية من انتحل الهوى ودعا الناس إليه؛ لأن المحاجة والدعوة إلى الهوى سبب داع إلى التقول الذي اتخذه ملة.
As for the follower of desire (sahib al-hawa), the chosen madhhab is that the narration of one who adopts desire as his creed and calls people to it is not accepted, because arguing and calling to desire is a cause that leads to fabricating (sayings) attributed to the Prophet, which he has taken as his religion.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Hanafi usul regarding the acceptance of narrations from a sahib al-hawa, i.e., an innovator in religious matters who not only holds heretical views but actively proselytizes them. The relied-upon position (al-madhhab al-mukhtar) is that such a person's narrations are rejected. The reason (ta'lil) is that his engagement in polemics (muhajaja) and call (da'wa) to his innovation creates a strong motive (sabab da'in) to fabricate hadith or distort narrations to support his beliefs. The phrase 'which he has taken as his religion' indicates that his innovation has become a foundational part of his worldview, making him more likely to lie for its sake. This rejection is stricter than the treatment of a fasiq (sinner), whose report may be accepted with scrutiny; here, the innovator's report is absolutely rejected because the motive for lying is presumed, and there is no necessity because trustworthy narrators are abundant. The commentary likely connects to the earlier discussion of fasigs: an innovator who calls to his innovation is considered unreliable regardless of circumstances.

Key Terms
صاحب الهوى (sahib al-hawa): A person who adopts his own desire (hawa) as his creed, i.e., an innovator who makes his bid'a a matter of religion and calls others to it.
التقول (al-taqawwul): Fabricating sayings and attributing them to the Prophet, i.e., lying in hadith.
المذهب المختار (al-madhhab al-mukhtar): The chosen (relied-upon) position within the Hanafi school, as opposed to weaker opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because his engagement in arguing and calling to his innovation creates a strong motive to fabricate hadith.
C) Because his faith is incomplete.
D) Because he cannot be a witness in court.

Key Takeaway
The narration of an innovator who calls to his innovation is absolutely rejected in the Hanafi school because his missionary zeal creates a presumptive motive to fabricate.

Conditions for Accepting Narration of a Fasiq and a Sahib al-Hawa
Usul rule with expansion on narrator acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for accepting a fasiq's narration, explain the role of necessity and taharri, and distinguish between the rulings for a fasiq and a sahib al-hawa in testimony and narration.

Core Idea
A fasiq's narration is accepted only with investigation and necessity; a propagating sahib al-hawa's narration is rejected entirely.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the reliability of narrators is crucial for accepting hadith. This passage from the chapter on Sunnah distinguishes between a fasiq (sinner) and a sahib al-hawa (person of desire) in terms of their testimony (shahada) and narration (riwaya). Understanding these distinctions helps us apply the principles of necessity, availability of trustworthy narrators, and the impact of propagating falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of narrators
The passage discusses two types: the fasiq (sinner who commits major sins) and the sahib al-hawa (person who follows personal desire, especially heretical doctrines). For each, we need to determine the ruling on accepting their testimony and narration.
2
State the ruling for the fasiq
The Hanafi position: A fasiq is eligible for testimony but his narration in religious matters is accepted only with investigation (taharri) and out of necessity. The reason is that upright narrators are plentiful, so no necessity exists to rely on a fasiq's report without verification.
Compare with testimony: the judge's verdict based on a fasiq's testimony is valid.
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil) for the fasiq's narration
The passage explains that for matters like halal/haram of food, the default is purity (water/food is pure originally), so necessity is limited. Therefore, a fasiq's report is accepted only with taharri. In hadith, no such necessity exists because many trustworthy narrators are available.
Unlike a disbeliever or minor, whose reports are not accepted at all because they are not eligible for testimony and suspicion of lying remains.
4
State the ruling for the sahib al-hawa
The chosen madhhab (mukhtar) is that if a sahib al-hawa adopts a heretical doctrine and actively propagates it, his narration is rejected. The reasoning: argumentation and calling to desire lead to fabrication of hadith. If he merely holds a belief without propagation, some accept his narration, but the majority reject it.
For testimony, the majority accept it; some (al-Baqillani) reject both testimony and narration because he is a fasiq.
5
Apply the ikhtilaf
The passage details disagreements: if the sahib al-hawa's belief reaches kufr, some accept his testimony/riwaya (as he is still Muslim), but the majority reject both. If it does not reach kufr, the majority accept testimony, and for narration, the strongest view (taken by the author) is to reject it if he propagates.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): a judge may accept his testimony in court but not his hadith narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السنة الأصل الثاني السنة وكونه مع الفسق أهلاً للشهادة وانتفاء التهمة، حيث يلزمه بخبره ما يلزم غيره، إلا أن هذه الضرورة غير لازمة؛ لأن العمل بالأصل ممكن، وهو أن الماء طاهر في الأصل. فلم يُجعل الفسق هدراً ولا ضرورة في المصير إلى روايته في أمور الدين أي الفاسق أصلاً؛ لأن في العدول من الرواة كثرة، وبهم غنية، فلا يصار إليه بالتحري. أي إلى خبر الفاسق خبر صاحب الهوى] وأما صاحب الهوى فالمذهب المختار أنه لا تقبل رواية من انتحل الهوى ودعا الناس إليه؛ لأن المحاجة والدعوة إلى الهوى سبب داع إلى التقول الذي اتخذه ملة وكونه أي إنما يقبل لأجل الضرورة. ولكون الفاسق مع الفسق أهلا للشهادة حتى لو قضى القاضي بشهادته ينفذ. وانتفاء التهمة أي تهمة الكذب عن خبره. ما يلزم غيره من الاجتناب والاقتراب فلايكون خبره ملزماً على الغير بدون أن يلزمه أولا من الخبر ما يلزم غيره منه، بخلاف الكافر والصبي حيث لا يقبل خبرهما في حل الطعام وحرمته أيضا؛ لأن الكافر ليس أهلا للشهادة على المسلم والصبي ليس بأهل الشهادة أصلا، ومع ذلك تهمة الكذب غير مدفوع عن خبرهما حيث لا يلزمهما ما يلزم غيرهما، أما الكافر فلأنه غير مخاطب بالشرائع، وأما الصبي فلأنه غير مكلف، ولما كان يرد أن الضرورة لما تحققت في قبول خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته وجب أن يقبل خبره من غير وجوب التحري في خبره أجاب بقوله: إلا أن هذه الضرورة إلخ. غير لازمة في قبول خبره في حل الطعام وحرمته. الماء طاهر إلخ وكذا الطعام وذلك لأن الماء والطعام طاهران في بدء الخلقة وإنما يعرضهما النجاسة بسبب عارض، وإذا كان كذلك فلم يجعل الفسق هدراً، بل اعتبر من وجه حيث لا يعتبر خبره بغير التحرى فيه، ولما كان يتوهم أنكم كما قبلتم خبر الفاسق في حل الطعام وحرمته مع التحرّي فكذلك ينبغي أن يقبل خبره في الحديث مع التحري دفعه بقوله : ولا ضرورة إلخ. أصلا مع التحري ولا بغير التحري. وبهم غنية من غيرهم، فلما انتفى الضرورة برأسها هنا بالتحري لأن قبول خبره فرع الضرورة، وإذا انعدمت الضرورة انعدم القبول برأسه. الهوى والهوى ميلان النفس إلى الشهوات من غير داعية الشرع. فالمذهب المختار في قبول روايته وعدم قبولها. انتحل الهوى والانتحال اتخاذ النحلة، الملة. والحاصل أن صاحب الهوى إن كان ممن اتخذ هواه ملة ومذهبا. ودعا الناس إليه: أي إلى الهوى الذي اتخذه ملة لا يقبل روايته في ذلك لأن المحاجة أي مخاصمة صاحب الهوى مع . أهل الحق والدعوة: أي دعوة صاحب الهوى الناس. التقول: أي الكذب والافتراء على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كما يشاهد = وهي في الفرق الضالة حيث يدعون الحديث على مزخرفاتهم وينسبونه إلى النبي فلا يؤتمن أي لايظن صاحب الهوى أنه أمين على حديث رسول الله ، وتفصيل المقام أنه لا يخلو أهل الهوى إما أن بلغ اعتقاده إلى الكفر ، كغُلاة الروافض والمجسّمة أو لا، فإن كان الأول فقد اختلف فيه، فذهب جماعة من أهل الأصول إلى قبول شهادته وروايته؛ لأنه من أهل القبلة يتمسك بالإسلام، وذهب الأكثرون إلى ردهما؛ لأنه كافر، وهو ليس بأهل الشهادة ولا الرواية، واختلف في القسم الثاني أيضاً فقال القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني ومن تبعه لا يقبل شهادته ولا روايته؛ لأنه فاسق لايبالي بالمعصية، فكيف يعتمد على قوله، وذهب الجمهور إلى أنه يقبل شهادته وأما الرواية فعند البعض مقبولة على الإطلاق، وقال البعض: لا يقبل إذا كان اتخذ ودعا الناس إليه وهو مذهب عامة أهل الفقه والحديث وبه رضي المصنف في المتن واختصاره، ونقل عن أبي اليسر الله أنه إن كان يكفّر لا يقبل حديثه، وإن لم يكن يكفّر فإن كان ممن يجوز وضع الأحاديث على رسول الله له لا يقبل خبره لتوهم الكذب كالكرامية.
Chapter of Sunnah. The second foundation is the Sunnah. And his [the fasiq] being, despite his fisq, eligible for testimony and absence of suspicion, since his report obligates him what it obligates others, except that this necessity is not binding because acting upon the original principle is possible, i.e., water is pure in origin. So fisq is not disregarded, and there is no necessity to resort to his narration in religious matters, because there are many upright narrators, and they suffice, so one does not resort to [his report] with investigation. As for the person of desire (sahib al-hawa), the chosen madhhab is that the narration of one who adopts desire and calls people to it is not accepted, because argumentation and calling to desire are reasons leading to fabrication, which he has taken as a religion. And his [the fasiq's] acceptance is only for necessity. And because the fasiq, despite fisq, is eligible for testimony, so if a judge gives a verdict based on his testimony it is effective. And absence of suspicion, i.e., suspicion of lying about his report. What obligates others of avoidance and approach; so his report does not obligate others without first obligating him from the report what obligates others, unlike the disbeliever and the minor, whose reports are not accepted regarding permissibility and prohibition of food, because the disbeliever is not eligible for testimony against a Muslim, and the minor is not eligible for testimony at all. Moreover, the suspicion of lying is not removed from their reports because they are not obligated what obligates others. As for the disbeliever, he is not addressed by the laws; as for the minor, he is not legally responsible. And when it might be objected that since necessity is realized in accepting the fasiq's report regarding permissibility and prohibition of food, it should be accepted without requiring investigation, he replied: 'Except that this necessity ... etc.' is not binding in accepting his report regarding permissibility and prohibition of food. Water is pure etc., and likewise food, because water and food are pure in initial creation, and impurity only affects them due to an accidental cause. And if so, fisq is not disregarded entirely, but is considered from one aspect, where his report is not accepted without investigation. And when it might be thought that just as you accepted the fasiq's report regarding food permissibility with investigation, so should his report in hadith be accepted with investigation, he refuted it by saying: 'And no necessity ... etc.' absolutely, with investigation or without investigation. And there is sufficiency from others. Since necessity is completely absent here, because acceptance of his report is conditional on necessity, and when necessity is absent, acceptance is absolutely absent. Al-Hawa: desire is the inclination of the soul towards lusts without a call from the Shari'a. The chosen madhhab regarding accepting his narration or not. He adopted desire: adopting a creed, a religion. The gist is that the person of desire, if he is one who takes his desire as a religion and doctrine, and calls people to it, his narration in that regard is not accepted because argumentation (i.e., disputing with the people of truth) and calling (i.e., his calling people) leads to fabrication, i.e., lying and forging against the Prophet ﷺ, as seen in the deviant sects who fabricate hadith for their embellishments and attribute them to the Prophet. So he is not trusted, i.e., the person of desire is not considered trustworthy over the hadith of the Messenger of Allah. Detailed discussion: The people of desire are either such that their belief reaches disbelief, like the extremist Rafidis and Mujassima, or not. If the first, there is disagreement: a group of usul scholars accept his testimony and narration because he is from the people of the qibla adhering to Islam; the majority reject both because he is a disbeliever, not eligible for testimony or narration. For the second category also there is disagreement: Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and his followers do not accept his testimony or narration because he is a fasiq who does not care about sin; the majority accept his testimony. As for narration, some accept it absolutely; some do not accept if he adopts desire and calls people to it, which is the madhhab of most jurists and hadith scholars, and the author chose this in the matn. It is reported from Abu al-Yusr that if he declares takfir [of others], his hadith is not accepted; if he does not declare takfir, if he is one who permits forging hadith upon the Prophet for his [desire], his report is not accepted due to suspicion of lying, like the Karramiyya.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Sunnah, discussing the conditions for accepting reports from sinful (fasiq) narrators and from those who follow personal desire (sahib al-hawa). The author first explains that a fasiq is eligible for testimony in court despite his sin, but his narration in religious matters is only accepted out of necessity, and only after investigation (taharri) because pure water and food are assumed pure by origin, so there is no need to rely on a fasiq's report when upright narrators are available. The commentary contrasts the fasiq with the disbeliever and minor, whose reports are not accepted at all because they are not eligible for testimony and suspicion of lying remains. The text then addresses a potential objection: if necessity justifies accepting the fasiq's report in food cases, why not in hadith? The response is that in food cases, necessity is limited because the default is purity; in hadith, there is no such necessity because many upright narrators exist. Regarding the person of desire (sahib al-hawa), the chosen Hanafi position is that if he actively propagates his deviant views and takes them as a religion, his narration is rejected because his inclination leads to fabrication. The detailed discussion later reveals disagreements among scholars: if the sahib al-hawa's belief reaches kufr, some accept his testimony/riwaya (as he is still a Muslim), but the majority reject it; if not kufr, the majority accept his testimony but differ on his riwaya—the preferred view (and the author's) is that it is rejected if he propagates his heresy, echoing the Hanafi school. The passage concludes with a nuanced differentiation: if the person is known to permit forging hadith for his sect (like Karramiyya), his report is rejected due to strong suspicion of lying.

Key Terms
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): A Muslim who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, thus lacking 'adala.
صاحب الهوى (ṣāḥib al-hawā): One who follows personal desires in religious matters, especially one who adopts a heretical doctrine and calls others to it.
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Investigation to ascertain the truthfulness or accuracy of a report, especially when accepting a fasiq's report in worldly matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on accepting the narration of a fasiq in matters of halal and haram of food?
A) Accepted without investigation because necessity is general.
B) Accepted only with investigation (taharri) due to limited necessity.
C) Never accepted because fisq destroys credibility.
D) Accepted if he is also a jurist (faqih).

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul accepts a fasiq's narration only with necessity and investigation, and rejects the narration of a propagating sahib al-hawa due to the risk of fabrication.
