Classification of Narrators: Known for Fiqh vs. Known for 'Adala
Distinguishes narrators known for fiqh (whose hadith overrides qiyas) and those only reliable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a narrator known for fiqh from one known only for 'adala, and apply the Hanafi rule that the hadith of a faqih narrator overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
A hadith from a jurist-companion overrides analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Hanafi usul.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all narrators are treated equally when their hadith conflicts with qiyas. This passage explains a crucial distinction: narrators known for fiqh and ijtihad carry extra weight, and their reports can set aside qiyas. The author clarifies this rule and contrasts it with Imam Malik's approach, using the example of the 'Abdallahs and the hadith on washing the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator classification
The passage divides known narrators into two types: those known for fiqh (like the three 'Abdallahs) and those known only for 'adala (reliability). Note the further list of four 'Abdallahs mentioned by al-Kirmani.
2
Understand the Hanafi rule
For a narrator known for fiqh, his hadith (khabar al-wahid) is given precedence over qiyas: 'yutraku bihi al-qiyas' (qiyas is abandoned due to it). This is the core ruling.
This rule applies only when the narrator is a faqih mujtahid.
3
Examine the madhhab dispute
Contrast with Imam Malik: Malik gives precedence to qiyas over khabar al-wahid when they conflict, even if the narrator is reliable. The example of Abu Hurayra's hadith on washing the dead shows this difference.
Malik's position is based on the strength of systematic reasoning and perceived weakness of ahad reports.
4
Analyze the evidence
The passage cites a specific hadith (marfu') from Abu Hurayra: 'Whoever washes the dead should perform ghusl...' Although the hadith's authenticity is debated (Ahmad said nothing authentic in this chapter), the principle of narrator classification remains.
The Hanafi position is that even if the hadith is weak, the rule stands for authentic narrations from faqih narrators.
5
Apply the rule
Think of a scenario: If a reliable narrator known for fiqh reports a command that contradicts a well-established qiyas, the command is taken as overriding analogy. This affects how we derive rulings in ibadat and mu'amilat.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is evident in fiqh: e.g., the ghusl for washing the dead – Hanafis consider it mustahabb (recommended) due to other proofs, not wajib, but the principle ensures qiyas does not void the hadith completely.

Source Text

قلنا: ولما فرغ من تقسيم الحديث باعتبار قلة رواته وكثرته واتصاله وانفصاله شرع في تقسيمه باعتبار حال الراوي بأنه إما معروف أو مجهول، والمعروف إما معروف بالفقه أو بالعدالة والمجهول على خمسة أنواع. في الاجتهاد كلمة "في" بمعنى اللام والمعنى أن له تقدما على غيره درجة لأجل الاجتهاد. والعبادلة الثلاثة: والعبادلة جمع عبدل، مرحم عبد الله، والمراد بهم عبد الله بن مسعود وعبد الله بن عمر وعبد الله بن عباس، وقيل: عبد الله بن زبير بدل عبد الله بن مسعود وقال الكرماني: العبادلة أربعة: عبد الله بن زبير، وعبد الله بن عباس، وعبد بن عمر، وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص . اشتهر بالفقه والنظر: مثل أبي بن كعب وأبي الدرداء ما يترك به القياس خلافاً لمالك؛ لأن عنده القياس مقدّم على خبر الواحد إذا خالفه، كما روي أن أبا هريرة لما روى مرفوعاً: "من غسل الميت فليغتسل، ومن حمله فليتوضأ . (رواه أبو داود رقم: ٣١٦١ والترمذي رقم: ۹۹۳ وابن ماجه رقم: ١٤٦٣ وابن حبان والنسائي وأحمد، وقال أحمد: لايصح في هذا الباب شيء) =
We say: When he finished dividing the hadith according to fewness and manyness of its narrators and its connectedness and disconnectedness, he began dividing it according to the condition of the narrator: either known or unknown. The known is either known for fiqh or for 'adala (reliability). The unknown is of five types. 'In ijtihad' – the word 'in' is in the sense of 'lam' (for), meaning that he has precedence over others by a degree due to ijtihad. The three 'Abdallahs': 'al-ʿabādila' is the plural of 'ʿabdalla', meaning 'Abdallah'. What is meant by them are 'Abdallah ibn Mas'ud, 'Abdallah ibn 'Umar, and 'Abdallah ibn 'Abbas. It is said: 'Abdallah ibn al-Zubayr instead of 'Abdallah ibn Mas'ud. Al-Kirmani said: The 'Abdallahs are four: 'Abdallah ibn al-Zubayr, 'Abdallah ibn 'Abbas, 'Abd (i.e., 'Abdallah) ibn 'Umar, and 'Abdallah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As. Those famous for fiqh and consideration (nazar): such as Ubayy ibn Ka'b and Abu al-Darda'. His hadith causes qiyas to be abandoned, contrary to Malik, because according to him qiyas is given precedence over khabar al-wahid if it contradicts it. As is narrated that when Abu Hurayra related marfu'an: 'Whoever washes the dead should perform ghusl, and whoever carries him should perform wudu.' (Narrated by Abu Dawud no. 3161, al-Tirmidhi no. 993, Ibn Majah no. 1463, Ibn Hibban, al-Nasa'i, and Ahmad; Ahmad said: Nothing authentic is established in this chapter.) =
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that transitions from discussing the divisions of hadith based on chain (mutawatir/ahad, muttasil/munqati') to divisions based on the narrator's personal qualities. The author classifies narrators as known (ma'ruf) or unknown (majhul). Known narrators are further subdivided: (1) Those known for fiqh and ijtihad — like the three 'Abdallahs (Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas), and others like Ubayy ibn Ka'b and Abu Darda'. Their hadith is considered strong enough to override qiyas (analogical reasoning). This is the Hanafi position. (2) Those known only for 'adala (reliability) and memory, but not for fiqh — their hadith is accepted but does not override qiyas as automatically. The commentary explicitly mentions the disagreement with Imam Malik, who gives precedence to qiyas over khabar ahad when they conflict, citing the example of Abu Hurayra's hadith about washing the dead (requiring ghusl and wudu). The Hanafi view, following the majority, is that even though this hadith may not be authentic (as Ahmad said), the principle stands: a hadith from a faqih narrator is a stronger proof than qiyas. The passage also notes the variant lists for the 'Abdallahs: three or four, with al-Kirmani including four. The commentary serves to clarify the types of narrators and their respective evidentiary weight in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الراوي المعروف (al-rāwī al-maʿrūf): A known narrator, either famous for fiqh and ijtihad or famous for 'adala and hifz (reliability and memory).
العبادلة (al-ʿabādila): Companions named 'Abdallah who were famous for fiqh: Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and sometimes Ibn al-Zubayr or Ibn 'Amr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding the hadith of a narrator known for fiqh (like the three 'Abdallahs) when it conflicts with qiyas?
A) Qiyas is given precedence because it is based on clear reasoning.
B) The hadith is taken as evidence, and qiyas is abandoned.
C) Both are given equal weight and a middle ground is sought.
D) The hadith is accepted only if it is mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the hadith of a narrator known for fiqh can override qiyas, unlike the Maliki position.

Two Types of Known Narrators and the Ruling on Innovators
Defining two types of reliable narrators and addressing innovators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two categories of known narrators in Hanafi usul and apply the rule for accepting or rejecting reports from innovators.

Core Idea
A narrator known for fiqh and ijtihad has his report preferred over qiyas; otherwise only uprightness suffices, but innovators who call to their innovation are rejected.

Once it is established that a solitary report (khabar al-wāḥid) is a valid proof (ḥujjah), the next step is to evaluate the narrator's qualifications. This passage from a Hanafi uṣūl text divides known narrators into two types: those with deep fiqh and ijtihād, and those with only uprightness and memory. It then addresses the delicate issue of accepting reports from people of innovation (ahl al-hawā), clarifying when their narration is accepted or rejected according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the conditional context
The passage begins with 'When it is established that the solitary report is a proof (ḥujjah)', meaning the discussion applies only after accepting khabar al-wāḥid as a valid source. This frames the subsequent classification.
2
Identify the two categories of known narrators
The first category: narrator known for fiqh and ijtihād (like the rightly guided caliphs, the three ʿAbdallāhs, Zayd ibn Thābit, etc.). The second: narrator known only for ʿadālah and ḥifẓ without fiqh. Understand the defining traits of each.
The first category includes Companions who were muftīs and mujtahids; the second includes trustworthy but non-mujtahid Companions.
3
Understand the consequence for each category
For the first category, their report is taken over qiyās (i.e., it overrides analogical reasoning). For the second, their report is not taken over qiyās, and the text adds 'فلا يؤتمن' which the commentator restricts to innovators among them.
The phrase 'فلا يؤتمن' is a general warning, but the commentary clarifies it applies to ahl al-hawā, not all non-faqīh narrators.
4
Analyze the discussion on ahl al-hawā (innovators)
The passage presents three levels: (1) innovation that reaches kufr (e.g., extreme Rāfiḍah, Mujassimah) – majority reject their report. (2) innovation that is fisq without kufr but the narrator calls to it – the preferred view (chosen by the author) is rejection. (3) innovation without calling – some accept, others reject; the majority of fiqh and ḥadīth scholars accept if the narrator is otherwise trustworthy.
The author (al-Husāmī?) approves of the view that a caller to innovation is rejected.
5
Derive the Hanafi operative rule
From the passage: (a) A narrator known for fiqh and ijtihād: his report is accepted and preferred over qiyās. (b) A narrator known for ʿadālah and ḥifẓ but not fiqh: his report is accepted but not preferred over qiyās, unless he is from ahl al-hawā who calls to his innovation – in which case it is rejected. Innovators who do not call are accepted if upright and memorizers.
This is the muftā bihī position in the Ḥanafī school.

Source Text

فلا يؤتمن على حديث رسول الله .
خبر الراوي المعروف]
وإذا ثبت أن خبر الواحد حجة قلنا: إن كان الراوي معروفاً بالفقه والتقدم في الاجتهاد، كالخلفاء الراشدين والعبادلة الثلاثة وزيد بن ثابت ومعاذ بن جبل وأبي موسى الأشعري وعائشة رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين وغيرهم ممن اشتهر بالفقه والنظر، كان حديثهم حجة، يترك به القياس، وإن كان الراوي معروفاً بالعدالة والحفظ دون الفقه، = هواه في الفرق الضالة حيث يدعون الحديث على مزخرفاتهم وينسبونه إلى النبي فلا يؤتمن أي لايظن صاحب الهوى أنه أمين على حديث رسول الله ، وتفصيل المقام أنه لا يخلو أهل الهوى إما أن بلغ اعتقاده إلى الكفر ، كغُلاة الروافض والمجسّمة أو لا، فإن كان الأول فقد اختلف فيه، فذهب جماعة من أهل الأصول إلى قبول شهادته وروايته؛ لأنه من أهل القبلة يتمسك بالإسلام، وذهب الأكثرون إلى ردهما؛ لأنه كافر، وهو ليس بأهل الشهادة ولا الرواية، واختلف في القسم الثاني أيضاً فقال القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني ومن تبعه لا يقبل شهادته ولا روايته؛ لأنه فاسق لايبالي بالمعصية، فكيف يعتمد على قوله، وذهب الجمهور إلى أنه يقبل شهادته وأما الرواية فعند البعض مقبولة على الإطلاق، وقال البعض: لا يقبل إذا كان اتخذ ودعا الناس إليه وهو مذهب عامة أهل الفقه والحديث وبه رضي المصنف في المتن واختصاره، ونقل عن أبي اليسر الله أنه إن كان يكفّر لا يقبل حديثه، وإن لم يكن يكفّر فإن كان ممن يجوز وضع الأحاديث على رسول الله له لا يقبل خبره لتوهم الكذب كالكرامية.
Chapter of the Sunnah. 12. The second source is the Sunnah. So he is not to be trusted upon the hadith of the Messenger of Allah. [The report of the known narrator]. And when it is established that the solitary report is a proof, we say: If the narrator is known for jurisprudence and advancement in ijtihad, like the rightly guided caliphs, the three Abdullahs, Zayd ibn Thabit, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Aisha – may Allah be pleased with them all – and others who are famous for jurisprudence and scholarly insight, then their hadith is a proof, and qiyas is abandoned for it. But if the narrator is known for uprightness and memory without jurisprudence, then [consider] the innovator among the deviant sects who fabricate hadith according to their embellishments and attribute them to the Prophet, so he is not trusted – meaning, the person of innovation should not think he is trustworthy concerning the hadith of the Messenger of Allah. And the detailed discussion of the matter: The people of innovation are not free from either their belief reaching kufr, like the extreme Rafidah and the Mujassimah, or not. If the first, then there is disagreement: a group of usul scholars accept his testimony and narration because he is among the people of the qibla clinging to Islam, while the majority reject both because he is a disbeliever and not qualified for testimony or narration. Regarding the second category as well, al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and those who follow him say: his testimony and narration are not accepted because he is a transgressor who does not care about sin, so how can his word be relied upon? The majority hold that his testimony is accepted; as for narration, some accept it absolutely, while others say it is not accepted if he has adopted the innovation and calls people to it, and this is the madhhab of the majority of scholars of fiqh and hadith, and the author approved of it in the matn and its abridgement. It is transmitted from Abu al-Yusr that if he declares takfir, his hadith is not accepted; and if he does not declare takfir, then if he is among those who permit fabricating hadith upon the Messenger of Allah for his own sake, his report is not accepted due to suspicion of lying, like the Karramiyyah.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding the second source (al-Sunnah) and the condition of the narrator. It establishes that once it is proven that khabar al-wahid is hujjah, the next step is to consider the narrator's qualifications. The author divides known (ma‘ruf) narrators into two categories: those known for fiqh and ijtihad (like the major companions listed), and those known only for ‘adalah and hifz without fiqh. The report of the first category is taken over qiyas. For the second category, the text initially appears to say they are not trusted, but the commentator clarifies that this applies specifically to ahl al-hawa (innovators) among them. The commentator then delves into the ruling on ahl al-hawa: if their innovation reaches kufr, the majority reject their narration and testimony; if it is fisq without kufr, there are differences. The preferred view (chosen by the author) is that if they actively call to their innovation, their narration is rejected. This passage highlights the nuance in Hanafi usul regarding narrator reliability beyond mere ‘adalah.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A hadith narrated by one or a few narrators not reaching tawatur
راوٍ معروف بالفقه (rāwī maʿrūf bi-l-fiqh): A narrator known for deep understanding and ijtihad
أهل الهوى (ahl al-hawā): People of innovation who follow their desires and deviate from orthodox creed
راوٍ معروف بالعدالة والحفظ (rāwī maʿrūf bi-l-ʿadāla wa-l-ḥifẓ): A narrator known for uprightness and memory but not necessarily for fiqh
دعا إلى هواه (daʿā ilā hawāh): He calls others to his innovation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, when is the report of a solitary narrator (khabar al-wahid) taken over qiyas?
A) When the narrator is known for uprightness and memory, regardless of fiqh
B) When the narrator is known for jurisprudence and ijtihad
C) When the narrator is one of the Companions
D) When the narrator is not an innovator

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a narrator's report depends not only on his uprightness but also on his level of fiqh; and innovators who call to their innovation are rejected.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Preferring Qiyas over Hadith of Non-Faqih Narrator
Expands the Hanafi dispute on qiyas vs khabar wahid from non-faqih narrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on prioritizing qiyas over a khabar wahid when the narrator is not a faqih, and articulate the shift from Isa ibn Aban to al-Karkhi.

Core Idea
A non-faqih narrator's hadith is set aside for qiyas only out of necessity—but later Hanafis accept it if reliable.

This passage addresses a key usul al-fiqh problem: what happens when a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) conflicts with analogical reasoning (qiyas)? The Hanafi school has internal disagreement, with an early view (Isa ibn Aban) abandoning the hadith to keep qiyas operative, and a later view (al-Karkhi) giving precedence to the hadith provided it is authentic and reliable. The famous example is the hadith of musarrah, where the Prophet gave a buyer the option to return an animal with retained milk along with a sa' of dates. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting sources
The passage presents a conflict between the hadith of musarrah (which gives a buyer a right to return with a sa' of dates) and qiyas (which would require compensation by similar milk or value). Identify the exact ruling each source produces.
The hadith is from Abu Hurayra, a non-faqih companion.
2
Understand the condition of the narrator
The narrator (Abu Hurayra) is described as non-faqih. This is crucial for the early Hanafi position: if the narrator were a faqih, the hadith would be accepted. Explain why a non-faqih might err in transmission by meaning.
The passage suggests the narrator could have transmitted the hadith by meaning and misunderstood the intent.
3
Trace the necessity argument
The early view (Isa ibn Aban) abandons the hadith to prevent the closing of the door of qiyas (insidad bab al-ra'y), citing the Qur'anic command 'fa'tabiroo ya uli al-absar' (59:2). Analyze how this verse commands qiyas and why preserving qiyas is prioritized.
"Necessity" (darura) here means that if every hadith contradicting qiyas were accepted, qiyas would be rendered inoperative.
4
Contrast with the later Hanafi position
Al-Karkhi accepts the hadith because the narrator is reliable and the hadith does not contradict the Qur'an or mass-transmitted sunna. Identify the conditions he sets for accepting a hadith over qiyas.
The passage states this is the 'clear truth' and the majority view.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the early view denies the buyer the right to return due to tasriya; the later view grants that right. State the practical difference in rulings between the two positions.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows how usul disagreements directly affect fiqh outcomes.

باب السنة

الأصل الثاني السننة مثل أبي هريرة وأنس بن مالك ما. فإن وافق حديثه القياس عمل به، وإن خالفه لم يترك إلا للضرورة وانسداد باب الرأي، وذلك مثل حديث أبي هريرة في المصراة.
قالت عائشة: أو ينجس موتى المسلمين؟ وما على رجل لوحمل عوداً . (أخرجه أبو منصور البغدادي في كتابه من طريق محمد بن عمرو بن يحيى بن عبد الرحمن بن حاطب فتأمل. ونحن نقول : القياس محتمل بأصله في كل وصف؛ إذ كل وصف من أوصاف النص يحتمل أن يكون هو المؤثر في الحكم ويحتمل أن لا يكون وخبر الواحد يقين بأصله، وإنما الشبهة في طريق وصوله والاحتمال الثابت في الأصل أقوى من الاحتمال الثابت في الطريق بعد اليقين بالأصل فلا يعارض الخبر.
وانسداد باب الرأي قوله : وانسداد" عطف تفسيري لقوله: "للضرورة"، والمعنى إنما يترك حديث غير الفقيه إذا خالف القياس للضرورة، وهي أنه لو عمل بالحديث وقت المخالفة أيضاً لانسدّ باب القياس من كل وجه، وقد أمر الله تعالى بالقياس بقوله: ﴿فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ﴾ (الحشر : ۲)، والحال أن الراوي غير فقيه، ويحتمل أنه نقل ذلك الحديث بالمعنى؛ لأنه كان شائعاً ذائعا فيهم فيمكن أنه أخطأ فيه، ولم يدرك مراد رسول الله الله فحينئذ كيف يعتمد على قوله ويترك به القياس الثابت بقوله تعالى فلهذه الضرورة تركنا هذا الحديث وعملنا بالقياس حديث أبي هريرة الله وهو ما روى أبو هريرة أن النبي الله قال: "لا تصروا الإبل والغنم فمن ابتاعها بعد ذلك فهو بخير النظرين بعد أن يحلبها، إن رضيها أمسكها وإن سخطها ردّها وصاعاً من تمر". رواه مسلم[رقم:٣٨١٥]وأبو داود، [رقم:٣٤٤٣] والتصرية تفعيل من الصرعى، وهو في اللغة الجمع، يقال: صرّيت الماء وصريته إذا جمعته والمراد به في الحديث جمع اللبن في الضرع بالشد وترك الحلب مدة ليحلب المشتري بعد ذلك، فيغتر بكثرة لبنه ويشريه بثمن غال.
فهذا الحديث مخالف للقياس من كل وجه؛ لأن القياس في ضمان العدوانات والبياعات كلها أن يكون مقدراً بالمثل في المثلي، وبالقيمة في ذوات القيم، فضمان اللبن المشروب إما باللبن مثله وإما بالقيمة، ولو كان التمر قيمة فيه فينبغي أن يكون بحسب اللبن، لا أنه يجب صاع التمر قل اللبن أو كثر ، فإذا لم يعمل بالحديث لكونه مخالفاً للقياس فليس للمشترى ولاية الردّ بسبب التصرية من غير شرط؛ لأن البيع يقتضي سلامة المبيع، وبقلة اللبن لاتفوت وصف السلامة؛ لأن اللبن ،ثمرة، وبعدمها لا ينعدم وصف السلامة، فبقلتها ،أولى، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له.
* فتأمل : إشارة إلى أنه لا يحسن إيراد هذه الرواية كأن أبا هريرة لم يكن مجتهداً.
باب السنة
خبر الراوي المجهول]
١٤٢
الأصل الثاني السنة
وإن كان الراوي مجهولا لا يعرف إلا بحديث رواه أو بحديثين، مثل وابصة بن معبد المحبق، فإن روى عنه السلف وشهدوا بصحته، أو سكتوا عن الطعن صار بن حديثه مثل حديث المعروف، وإن اختلف فيه مع نقل الثقات عنه فكذلك عندنا ...
وسلمة
=
في القسمين
وذهب الشافعي ومالك رحمها إلى أن التصرية عيب حتى كان للمشتري الخيار إن شاء ردّها وصاعاً من تمر، وإن شاء أمسكها عملاً بظاهر الحديث.
هذا
ف: اعلم أن هذا مذهب عيسى بن أبان، وأما عند الكرخي ومن تابعه من أصحابنا فليس فقه الراوي شرطا لتقدم الحديث على القياس، بل يقبل خبر كل عدل ضابط إذا لم يكن مخالفا للكتاب والسنة المشهورة، ويقدم على القياس، وهذا هو الحق المبين، وإليه مال أكثر العلماء، وهو المأثور من الصحابة والتابعين.
Chapter of Sunna. 121 The second source: Sunna. [Hadiths] like those of Abu Hurayra and Anas ibn Malik. If their hadith agrees with qiyas, act by it; if it contradicts it, it is not abandoned except for necessity and the blocking of the door of opinion (ra'y). For example, the hadith of Abu Hurayra on musarrah (milk retention). Aisha said: "Or do the dead of Muslims become impure?" And what is upon a man if he carries a stick? (Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi narrated it in his book via Muhammad ibn Amr ibn Yahya ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Hatib. So reflect.) We say: Qiyas is probable in its root in every attribute; for every attribute of the text may be the effective cause ('illa) for the ruling or may not be. Khabar al-wahid is certain in its origin, but the doubt is in the path of its transmission. The probability established in the origin is stronger than the probability established in the path after certainty of the origin, so the khabar does not oppose [qiyas]. "And the blocking of the door of opinion" (wa insidad bab al-ra'y). His saying "and blocking" is an explanatory conjunction to his saying "for necessity." The meaning: The hadith of a non-faqih is only abandoned when it contradicts qiyas out of necessity, which is that if one were to act by the hadith at the time of opposition, the door of qiyas would be closed from every aspect. Allah most high commanded qiyas by His saying: "So take heed, O people of insight" (59:2). While the narrator is not a faqih, and it is possible that he transmitted the hadith by meaning because it was widespread among them, so he may have erred in it and not grasped the intent of the Messenger of Allah, may peace be upon him. So how can one rely on his statement and abandon qiyas established by the verse? For this necessity we abandoned this hadith and acted by qiyas. The hadith of Abu Hurayra (may Allah be pleased with him) is what Abu Hurayra narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Do not retain milk (by not milking) camels and sheep. Whoever buys them after that has the choice after milking them: if he is pleased, he keeps them; if he is displeased, he returns them along with a sa' of dates." Narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud. 'Tasriya' is a verbal noun from 'sar' (to collect). In language, it means collection. Water is said to be 'saraytu al-ma' or 'sarraytuhu' (I collected it). What is meant in the hadith is the collection of milk in the udder by tying and leaving milking for a period so that the buyer later milks and is deceived by the abundance of milk and buys it at a high price. This hadith contradicts qiyas from every aspect because qiyas in compensation for torts and sales is that it is measured by the like in fungible goods (mithli) and by value in non-fungibles. Compensation for the drunk milk is either by similar milk or by its value. If dates were a value for it, it should be according to the amount of milk, not that a sa' of dates is obligatory whether the milk is little or much. So if the hadith is not acted upon because it contradicts qiyas, the buyer has no right to return due to tasriya without a condition, because the sale implies soundness of the sold item, and the scarcity of milk does not negate the attribute of soundness, because milk is a fruit, and its absence does not negate the attribute of soundness, so even less does its lack [negate it]. This is according to Abu Hanifa. * 'So reflect': an indication that it is not appropriate to present this narration as if Abu Hurayra was not a mujtahid. Chapter of Sunna: Hadith of the Unknown Narrator. 142 The second source: Sunna. If the narrator is unknown (majhul), not known except by one or two hadiths he narrated, like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad al-Muhabbaq, then if the earlier generation narrated from him and attested to his authenticity, or they remained silent about criticism, his hadith becomes like a well-known hadith. If disagreement arises about him despite the reliable narrators' transmission from him, it is likewise according to us... and Salamah = in both categories. Al-Shafi'i and Malik (may Allah have mercy on them) held that tasriya is a defect, so the buyer has the option to return it along with a sa' of dates, or to keep it, acting by the apparent meaning of the hadith. This: Know that this is the madhhab of 'Isa ibn Aban. As for al-Karkhi and his followers from our school, the fiqh of the narrator is not a condition for giving precedence to the hadith over qiyas; rather, every reliable, precise narrator's report is accepted unless it contradicts the Book and the well-known Sunnah, and it is given precedence over qiyas. This is the clear truth, and most scholars incline towards it, and it is the transmitted practice from the Companions and Successors.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical usul al-fiqh issue: how to reconcile a khabar wahid (solitary hadith) with qiyas when they conflict, particularly when the narrator is not a faqih (legal expert). The text begins by stating the second source of Islamic law: the Sunna. It then presents the position that hadiths from narrators like Abu Hurayra and Anas ibn Malik, who are non-faqihs, are followed only when they agree with qiyas. If they contradict qiyas, they are abandoned only out of necessity, specifically to prevent the closing of the door of ra'y (opinion/analogical reasoning). The key example is the hadith of musarrah (milk-retention). The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave the buyer of an animal with retained milk the choice to keep it or return it with a sa' of dates. Qiyas would demand compensation in kind (similar milk) or value, not a fixed amount of dates regardless of the milk quantity. Abu Hanifa therefore did not apply the hadith, holding that the buyer has no right to return due to this hidden defect because the sale contract implies soundness, and a temporary decrease in milk does not affect soundness. The text then contrasts this with the position of al-Shafi'i and Malik, who considered tasriya a defect giving the buyer an option. Later, the author clarifies that this view (requiring the narrator to be a faqih) is from 'Isa ibn Aban, while al-Karkhi and the majority of Hanafi scholars (and indeed most scholars) accept the hadith of any reliable, precise narrator as long as it does not contradict the Qur'an and mass-transmitted sunna, and give it precedence over qiyas. This latter view is presented as the correct and transmitted position from the early generations.

Key Terms
تصرية (tasriya): Retention of milk in the udder by not milking for a period to deceive the buyer.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; deriving a ruling for a new case from an original case due to shared effective cause ('illa).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report narrated by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
انسداد باب الرأي (insidad bab al-ra'y): The closing of the door of independent reasoning (ijtihad by ra'y), which is prevented by adhering to a hadith that conflicts with qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the early Hanafi position (Isa ibn Aban) abandons the hadith of musarrah?
A) The hadith is not authentic.
B) To prevent the closing of the door of qiyas, which is commanded by the Qur'an.
C) Because the narrator (Abu Hurayra) is unreliable.
D) Because the hadith contradicts the consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The conflict between khabar wahid and qiyas is resolved differently within the Hanafi school: early scholars prioritized qiyas over hadiths from non-faqih narrators to preserve the juristic method, while later scholars accepted any reliable hadith, shifting the balance towards hadith acceptance.

Al-Sunnah as Source

The Unknown Narrator (Majhul) in Hanafi Usul
Explains categories of unknown narrator and acceptance conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five categories of the majhul narrator and apply the Hanafi rule that a majhul's hadith is accepted if the salaf narrated from him or remained silent about him.

Core Idea
The Hanafis accept a hadith from an unknown narrator if the salaf narrated from him or remained silent.

In Hanafi usul, the reliability of a narrator ('adala) is not always established by explicit statements. The unknown narrator (majhul) poses a challenge. This lesson parses the five categories of majhul narrators and demonstrates how the practice of the early generations (salaf) can establish a narrator's trustworthiness, using the famous case of Barwa' bint Washiq as a concrete example.

Guided Path
1
Define 'Majhul'
Understand the meaning of 'majhul' in this context: a narrator whose 'adala is not known through explicit statements but only through the hadiths he narrated. Distinguish between unknown in narration vs. unknown in lineage.
The text says: 'majhul i.e., in narration and reliability, not in lineage.'
2
List the Five Categories
Identify the five categories of majhul narrators mentioned in the text. The first three are described: (1) if the salaf narrated from him; (2) if he is criticized after his narration spread; (3) if he is known for fiqh, 'adala, and precision. The text hints at all five by saying 'his case is not free from five categories'.
The text explicitly covers the first three; the last two are implied by the structure.
3
Analyze the Example of Barwa' bint Washiq
Study the narrative: Ibn Mas'ud's initial ruling (mahr al-mithl) vs. his later qiyas (no mahr). Examine how Ma'qil ibn Sinan brought the Prophet's hadith. Identify why the Hanafis accept this hadith despite Ibn Mas'ud's own rejection: because the salaf (including Ibn Mas'ud, 'Alqama, Masruq, etc.) narrated and acted upon it, establishing the narrator's 'adala.
This example illustrates the first category: the salaf narrated from the originally unknown narrator.
4
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i Positions
Contrast the two schools: Hanafis give precedence to the hadith over qiyas because the salaf accepted it. Shafi'is prefer Ibn Mas'ud's qiyas and reject the hadith due to dispute. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis impose mahr al-mithl; Shafi'is impose no mahr.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf about the hierarchy of evidence.
5
Derive the Hanafi Usul Rule
Formulate the rule: A hadith from a majhul narrator is accepted and given precedence over qiyas if the salaf transmitted from him and acted upon his report, thereby establishing his 'adala. This is the basis for accepting ahad hadiths like the Barwa' hadith.
This rule is a distinguishing feature of Hanafi usul.

مجهولا أي في رواية الحديث والعدالة لا في النسب من حيث لا يعرف إلخ. بحديث رواه أو بحديثين: فحاله لايخلو عن خمسة أقسام. فإن روى عنه إلخ هذا هو القسم الأول من الأقسام الخمسة الطعن فيه بعد ما بلغتهم روايته، هو القسم الثاني المعروف بالفقه والعدالة والضبط، حتى يقبل ويقدّم على القياس فيه: أي في حديثه بأن قبل البعض وردّ البعض مع نقل الثقات عنه، هذا هو القسم الثالث. فكذلك أي كحديث المعروف حتى يقبل ويقدّم على القياس عندنا مثاله ماروى الترمذي عن ابن مسعود لله أنه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقاً ولم يدخل بها حتى مات، فقال ابن مسعود: لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط، وعليها العدة، ولها الميراث، فقام معقل بن سنان الأشجعي فقال: قضى في بروع بنت واشق امرأة منا مثل ما قضيت، ففرح بها ** ابن مسعود رقم : ١١٤٥ و لم يعمل بهذا الحديث على وقال لها الميراث، ولا صداق لها، وعليها العدة عملاً برأيه، وهو أن المعقود عليه عاد إليها سالماً، فلا تستحق بمقابلته مهراً كما لو طلّقها قبل الدخول و لم يسمّ لها مهراً ، فالشافعي ليه يعمل بما عمل به على وهو قياسه، ويردّ هذا الخبر لكونه مختلفاً فيه، فيقدم القياس عليه. ونحن عملنا بهذا الحديث؛ لأن الثقات رووا هذا الخبر منه، مثل ابن مسعود لله من القرن الأول، وعلقمة و مسروق ونافع بن جبير والحسن من القرن الثاني، فثبت بروايتهم عنه وعملهم بخبره عدالته، مع أنه مؤكد بالقياس أيضاً، وهو أن الموت يؤكد مهر المثل كما يؤكد المسمّى.
* لاوكس: الوكس ،النقصان والشطط الزيادة. ** بها: الموافقة.
Unknown (majhul) i.e., in narration and reliability, not in lineage, in that he is not known etc. By one hadith he narrated or two: his case is not free from five categories. If the earlier generation narrated from him etc., this is the first of the five categories. [If they] criticized him after his narration reached them, that is the second category. [If he is] known for fiqh, reliability, and precision, so that he is accepted and his hadith is given precedence over qiyas, this is the third category. 'Likewise' i.e., like a well-known hadith, so it is accepted and given precedence over qiyas according to us. Example: What al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he was asked about a man who married a woman without fixing a dowry and did not consummate until he died. Ibn Mas'ud said: She is entitled to the mahr of her peers, no reduction and no excess; she must observe the waiting period, and she inherits. Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan al-Ashja'i stood and said: You have given a verdict like the verdict given about Barwa' bint Washiq, a woman from us. So Ibn Mas'ud was pleased with that. And [Ibn Mas'ud] did not act by this hadith [of the Prophet] but gave his opinion: that she inherits, has no dowry, and must observe the waiting period, based on his opinion that the object of the contract (the woman's self) returned to her safely, so she does not deserve a mahr in exchange, just as if he divorced her before consummation without fixing a mahr. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) acts by what Ibn Mas'ud acted by, which is his qiyas, and rejects this khabar because it is disputed, so qiyas is preferred over it. We act by this hadith because reliable narrators transmitted it from him, such as Ibn Mas'ud (from the first generation), 'Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and al-Hasan (from the second generation). So his reliability is established through their narration from him and their acting by his khabar, especially since it is also supported by qiyas: that death confirms the mahr of the like just as it confirms the specified mahr.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage deals with the acceptance of hadith from an unknown (majhul) narrator. It outlines five categories of unknown narrators based on how they are known and how their reports are treated. The first category: if earlier reliable narrators (salaf) narrated from him or remained silent about criticism, his hadith becomes like a well-known hadith. Second: if he is criticized after his narration becomes known. Third: if he is known for fiqh, reliability, and precision, his hadith is accepted and given precedence over qiyas. The text then gives a detailed example: the case of a woman whose husband dies before consummation without fixing a dowry. Ibn Mas'ud initially ruled that she gets mahr al-mithl (the dowry of her peers), waiting period, and inheritance. Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan reminded him of the Prophet's verdict in the case of Barwa' bint Washiq: she inherits, has no dowry, and observes waiting period. Ibn Mas'ud was pleased but stuck to his opinion, applying qiyas: since the contract did not specify a dowry and the marriage was not consummated, no mahr is due, analogous to divorce before consummation without specified dowry. The Hanafi school, however, accepts the hadith because reliable narrators (including Ibn Mas'ud himself and later successors like 'Alqama, Masruq, etc.) transmitted and acted upon it. Furthermore, death strengthens the case for mahr al-mithl, just as it confirms a specified mahr. Thus, the Hanafi position gives mahr al-mithl plus inheritance and waiting period. The Shafi'i school sides with Ibn Mas'ud's qiyas and rejects the hadith because it is disputed. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that a hadith from a narrator whose reliability is established through the acceptance of the salaf is given precedence over qiyas, even if the narrator was originally unknown.

Key Terms
مجهول (majhul): A narrator whose reliability and identity are not well-known, only known through the hadiths he narrated.
عدالة (adala): Reliability/trustworthiness: being a Muslim of sound faith, avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins, maintaining good character.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dowry of a woman's peers (women of similar status, family, beauty, etc.), used when no specific dowry was fixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis accept the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq regarding the woman whose husband dies before consummation without a fixed mahr?
A) Because Ibn Mas'ud himself accepted it and later acted by it.
B) Because it is a mutawatir hadith.
C) Because reliable narrators transmitted it from the Prophet and the salaf accepted it, plus it is supported by qiyas.
D) Because it agrees with the qiyas of the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the hadith of an unknown narrator if the salaf transmitted from him and acted upon his report, thereby establishing his reliability.

Classifying Unknown Narrators: Five Categories in Hanafi Usul
Classifying unknown narrators into five categories with acceptance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five categories of unknown narrators according to Hanafi usul and determine the legal effect (acceptance/rejection) of each.

Core Idea
The Salaf's treatment of a narrator—testimony, silence, or rejection—determines whether his hadith is accepted or rejected.

The Hanafi school has a detailed classification for unknown narrators (majhool) based on how the pious predecessors (salaf) interacted with their narrations. This classification helps us understand when a hadith from an unknown source can override qiyas. In this lesson, we break down the five categories and their rulings, supported by examples from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Define the unknown narrator (majhool)
Identify the definition: a narrator not known in terms of hadith narration and integrity, except through his own narration of one or two hadith. Example: Wabisa ibn Ma'bad.
Not unknown in lineage, but in riwayah and 'adalah.
2
Outline the five categories
List the five categories based on the Salaf's response: (1) Salaf narrate and testify to truthfulness; (2) Salaf criticize after narration but narrator has fiqh and integrity; (3) Reliable narrators disagree about him; (4) Salaf reject and abandon his hadith (mustanqir); (5) Salaf neither accept nor reject (mustatir).
Categories 1-3 lead to acceptance and precedence over qiyas.
3
Examine acceptance conditions
For categories 1-3, acceptance is based on the Salaf's positive or neutral stance. For category 4, rejection because Salaf's opposition indicates suspicion. For category 5, permissibility only if the hadith agrees with qiyas.
The Salaf's practice is authoritative.
4
Apply to examples
Use the passage examples: Barwa' hadith (category 3 – accepted because Salaf narrated and acted), Fatima bint Qays (category 4 – mustanqir because Salaf rejected).
Understand the reasoning behind each classification.
5
Note the temporal shift
In the early generations, integrity was the norm, so even an unknown narrator could be accepted. In later times, due to widespread corruption, such narrators are not accepted.
This is the fifth category's nuance.

وإن لم يظهر في السلف إلا الرد لم يقبل حديثه وصار مستنكراً. وإن كان لم يظهر الراوي حديثه في السلف ولم يقابل برد ولا قبول لم يجب العمل به، لكن العمل به جائز؛
أي بهذا الحديث
لأن العدالة أصل في ذلك الزمان، حتى أن رواية مثل هذا المجهول في زماننا لايحلّ العمل به لظهور الفسق، فصار المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين والمشهور علم الطمأنينة وخبر الواحد علم غالب الرأي، والمستنكر منه يفيد الظن، وإن الظنّ لا يغني من الحق شيئاً، والمستتر منه في حيز الجواز للعمل به أي بالمستتر
وإن لم يظهر في إلخ: هذا هو القسم الرابع، فلايجوز به العمل إذا خالف القياس؛ لأنهم لم يكونوا يردّون الحديث الثابت عن النبي و لم يكونوا يتركون العمل به، فإذا ردّوه وتركوه علم أنهم اتهموه في هذه الرواية، وهو دون الموضوع في احتمال الكذب. ومثاله ماروى الترمذي عن المغيرة عن الشعبي قال: قالت فاطمة بنت قيس: طلقني على عهد رسول الله ، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا سكنى لك ولا نفقة". قال مغيرة: فذكرته لإبراهيم فقال: قال عمر : لاندعُ كتاب الله وسنة نبينا ل بقول ،امرأة، لاندري أحفظت أم نسيت؟ [رقم: ۱۱۸۰] وقال عمر ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة، فلم ينكره أحد، فصار إجماعاً على أن الحديث مستنكر.

جائز: بشرط أن لا يخالف القياس بل يكون موافقاً له، وفائدة إضافة الحكم حينئذ إلى الحديث مع كونه ثابتاً بالقياس أيضاً هو أن لا يتمكن الخصم فيه من المنع عن الحكم، كما يتمكن في القياس. ذلك الزمان: أي الصدر الأول، قال النبي "خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم" الحديث [الترمذي رقم: ۲۲۲۱] في زماننا : في أهل هذا الزمان، وهذا هو القسم الخامس من المجهول.
Chapter of Sunnah: The report of an unknown narrator. The second foundation: Sunnah. If the narrator is unknown, not known except by a hadith he narrated or two hadiths, like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad al-Muhabbaq, then if the Salaf narrate from him and testify to his truthfulness, or remain silent about criticism, his hadith becomes like the hadith of a known narrator. And if there is disagreement about him alongside transmission of reliable narrators from him, it is likewise according to us... And al-Shafi'i and Malik (may Allah have mercy on them) held that tasriyah (tying udders of milch animal) is a defect, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes he may return it and a sa' of dates, or keep it, acting on the apparent meaning of the hadith. This: Know that this is the madhhab of 'Isa ibn Aban. But according to al-Karkhi and those who follow him from our companions, the narrator's fiqh is not a condition for preferring hadith over qiyas; rather, the report of every just, precise narrator is accepted if it does not contradict the Book and the well-known Sunnah, and it is given precedence over qiyas. This is the manifest truth, and most scholars lean towards it, and it is the transmitted way from the Companions and Followers. Unknown means in narrating hadith and integrity, not in lineage, since he is not known etc. By one hadith he narrated or two hadiths: his case is not free from five categories. If the Salaf narrate from him etc. this is the first category of the five: criticism after his narration reached them, that is the second category: known for fiqh, integrity, and precision, so it is accepted and given precedence over qiyas. In it: i.e., in his hadith, by accepting some and rejecting some alongside transmission of reliable narrators from him, this is the third category. Likewise, i.e., like the hadith of a known narrator, so it is accepted and given precedence over qiyas according to us. Its example: what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he was asked about a man who married a woman, did not fix a dower for her, and did not consummate until he died. Ibn Mas'ud said: She has the mahr al-mithl of her peers, no reduction and no excess, she must observe 'iddah, and she inherits. Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan al-Ashja'i stood and said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) judged concerning Barwa' bint Washiq, a woman from us, similar to what you judged, so he [Ibn Mas'ud] rejoiced... and did not act on this hadith... but acted on his opinion, that the object of contract returned to her intact, so she does not deserve a dower in exchange, like if he divorced her before consummation and did not name a dower. So al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) acts on what he acted on, which is his qiyas, and rejects this report because it is disputed, so qiyas takes precedence over it. And we acted on this hadith because reliable narrators transmitted this report from him, such as Ibn Mas'ud from the first century, 'Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and al-Hasan from the second century. So their narration from him and their acting on his report established his integrity, especially since it is also supported by qiyas, which is that death confirms mahr al-mithl just as it confirms the named dower. If no opposition appears among the Salaf except rejection, his hadith is not accepted and becomes mustanqir (rejected). And if the narrator's hadith does not appear among the Salaf and is not met with rejection or acceptance, it is not obligatory to act on it, but acting on it is permissible. That is because integrity was the norm in that era. So the hadith of such an unknown person in our time is not permissible to act on due to the prevalence of corruption. And he said: The mutawatir produces certain knowledge, the mashhur produces tranquility, the solitary produces dominant opinion, and the mustanqir from it produces mere assumption, and assumption avails nothing against truth. And the mustatir from it is in the realm of permissibility to act on. Then the commentary: This is the fourth category. It is not permissible to act on it if it opposes qiyas because they would not reject an established hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and they would not abandon acting on it. So if they rejected and abandoned it, it is known that they suspected this narration, and it is less than the fabricated [hadith] in probability of lying. Its example is what al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Mughira from al-Sha'bi who said: Fatima bint Qays said: My husband divorced me three times during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "No housing and no maintenance for you." Al-Mughira said: I mentioned it to Ibrahim who said: 'Umar said: We do not leave the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the saying of a woman; we do not know whether she remembered or forgot. And 'Umar said that in the presence of the Companions, and no one denied it, so it became a consensus that the hadith is mustanqir. Permissible: on condition that it does not oppose qiyas but rather agrees with it. The benefit of attributing the ruling then to the hadith, while it is also established by qiyas, is so that the opponent cannot prevent the ruling from it, as he can in qiyas. That time: i.e., the first generation. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "The best of centuries is my century, then those who follow them." In our time: i.e., among the people of this time. This is the fifth category of the unknown.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work explains the rules for accepting hadith from an unknown narrator (majhool). The author first outlines the issue: an unknown narrator is one who is not known except through one or two hadith he narrates. The Hanafi position is that if the pious predecessors (salaf) narrate from him and testify to his truthfulness, or remain silent (which implies acceptance), his hadith is treated like that of a known narrator. If reliable narrators differ about him, the hadith is still accepted and given precedence over qiyas. The author then contrasts this with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions using the example of the tasriyah hadith, where they reject it in favor of qiyas. The key point of contention is whether the narrator's knowledge of fiqh is a condition for preferring his hadith over qiyas. The Hanafi school, represented by al-Karkhi, holds that it is not a condition; rather, any just and precise narrator’s hadith is accepted if it does not contradict clear texts, and it takes precedence over qiyas. This is supported by the example of the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, where the Prophet’s ruling on mahr al-mithl in case of death is accepted by Hanafis despite opposition to qiyas, because reliable narrators from the first and second centuries transmitted it. The passage then details five categories of unknown narrators: 1) Those from whom salaf narrate and attest—accepted; 2) Those who are criticized after their narration but are known for fiqh and integrity—still accepted and preferred over qiyas; 3) Those about whom reliable narrators differ—accepted; 4) Those whose hadith is rejected by salaf—rejected and labeled mustanqir, like the hadith of Fatima bint Qays about no housing and maintenance, which was rejected by 'Umar and the Companions; 5) Those whose hadith is not known among salaf but also not rejected—it is permissible to act on it if it agrees with qiyas. The commentary also notes that in the early generations, integrity was the norm, so even an unknown narrator could be accepted, but in later times due to widespread corruption, such reports are not accepted.

Key Terms
المجهول (al-majhool): An unknown narrator: one not known in terms of hadith narration and integrity, except through his own narration of one or two hadith.
المستنكر (al-mustanqir): A hadith that is rejected because the salaf opposed it and did not act on it, indicating suspicion of the narrator.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogic reasoning; here it is the method of deriving rulings that is opposed to the hadith in some cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of a narrator whose hadith appears among the Salaf but is met with rejection and abandonment?
A) It is accepted and given precedence over qiyas.
B) It becomes mustanqir and is not accepted.
C) It is permissible to act on it if it agrees with qiyas.
D) It is equal to a fabricated hadith.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of an unknown narrator's hadith depends on the Salaf's response, not on the narrator's fame.

The Condition of Narrator's Fiqh: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Maliki
Classifying unknown narrators into five categories with acceptance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that narrator's fiqh is not a condition for preferring hadith over qiyas, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i/Maliki argument using the Barwa' and tasriyah examples.

Core Idea
A just, precise narrator's hadith is accepted over qiyas—his fiqh knowledge is irrelevant.

A key point of contention in usul al-fiqh is whether a narrator must be a faqih for his hadith to take precedence over qiyas. The Hanafis reject this condition, citing the practice of the Salaf. This lesson examines the dispute with the examples of tasriyah and Barwa' bint Washiq, highlighting the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Narrator's fiqh is not a condition; any just, precise narrator's hadith is accepted and preferred over qiyas if it does not contradict clear texts.
This is the view of al-Karkhi and the majority of Hanafis, considered 'the manifest truth'.
2
Identify the opposing view
Shafi'i and Maliki schools require the narrator to be knowledgeable in fiqh, otherwise his hadith may be rejected when it conflicts with qiyas, especially if there is disagreement among narrators.
They reject hadith like tasriyah and Barwa' on this basis.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Salaf accepted narrators like Wabisa and Ibn Mas'ud, who were not necessarily faqihs in the sense required. Their acceptance shows that fiqh is not a condition.
The example of Barwa' hadith: Hanafis accept it because reliable narrators transmitted it, even though it contradicted a qiyas.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'is argue that the hadith of tasriyah (milking animal) conflicts with qiyas that no defect exists, and since the narrators are not all faqihs, they reject it in favor of qiyas. Similarly, the Barwa' hadith is disputed, so they prefer qiyas.
The passage mentions 'Isa ibn Aban as holding a similar view to Shafi'is.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis accept the hadith and rule that the buyer can return the animal without a sa' of dates (or accept the Barwa' hadith for mahr al-mithl). Shafi'is/Malikis reject the hadith and follow qiyas.
In the Barwa' case, Hanafis give the woman mahr al-mithl; Shafi'is give her no mahr (according to the passage's version).

في القسمين
وذهب الشافعي ومالك رحمها إلى أن التصرية عيب حتى كان للمشتري الخيار إن شاء ردّها وصاعاً من تمر، وإن شاء أمسكها عملاً بظاهر الحديث.
هذا
ف: اعلم أن هذا مذهب عيسى بن أبان، وأما عند الكرخي ومن تابعه من أصحابنا فليس فقه الراوي شرطا لتقدم الحديث على القياس، بل يقبل خبر كل عدل ضابط إذا لم يكن مخالفا للكتاب والسنة المشهورة، ويقدم على القياس، وهذا هو الحق المبين، وإليه مال أكثر العلماء، وهو المأثور من الصحابة والتابعين. مجهولا أي في رواية الحديث والعدالة لا في النسب من حيث لا يعرف إلخ. بحديث رواه أو بحديثين: فحاله لايخلو عن خمسة أقسام. فإن روى عنه إلخ هذا هو القسم الأول من الأقسام الخمسة الطعن فيه بعد ما بلغتهم روايته، هو القسم الثاني المعروف بالفقه والعدالة والضبط، حتى يقبل ويقدّم على القياس فيه: أي في حديثه بأن قبل البعض وردّ البعض مع نقل الثقات عنه، هذا هو القسم الثالث. فكذلك أي كحديث المعروف حتى يقبل ويقدّم على القياس عندنا مثاله ماروى الترمذي عن ابن مسعود لله أنه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقاً ولم يدخل بها حتى مات، فقال ابن مسعود: لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط، وعليها العدة، ولها الميراث، فقام معقل بن سنان الأشجعي فقال: قضى في بروع بنت واشق امرأة منا مثل ما قضيت، ففرح بها ** ابن مسعود رقم : ١١٤٥ و لم يعمل بهذا الحديث على وقال لها الميراث، ولا صداق لها، وعليها العدة عملاً برأيه، وهو أن المعقود عليه عاد إليها سالماً، فلا تستحق بمقابلته مهراً كما لو طلّقها قبل الدخول و لم يسمّ لها مهراً ، فالشافعي ليه يعمل بما عمل به على وهو قياسه، ويردّ هذا الخبر لكونه مختلفاً فيه، فيقدم القياس عليه. ونحن عملنا بهذا الحديث؛ لأن الثقات رووا هذا الخبر منه، مثل ابن مسعود له من القرن الأول، وعلقمة و مسروق ونافع بن جبير والحسن من القرن الثاني، فثبت بروايتهم عنه وعملهم بخبره عدالته، مع أنه مؤكد بالقياس أيضاً، وهو أن الموت يؤكد مهر المثل كما يؤكد المسمّى.
* لاوكس: الوكس ،النقصان والشطط الزيادة. ** بها: الموافقة.

وإن لم يظهر في السلف إلا الرد لم يقبل حديثه وصار مستنكراً. وإن كان لم يظهر الراوي حديثه في السلف ولم يقابل برد ولا قبول لم يجب العمل به، لكن العمل به جائز؛
أي بهذا الحديث
لأن العدالة أصل في ذلك الزمان، حتى أن رواية مثل هذا المجهول في زماننا لايحلّ العمل به لظهور الفسق، فصار المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين والمشهور علم الطمأنينة وخبر الواحد علم غالب الرأي، والمستنكر منه يفيد الظن، وإن الظنّ لا يغني من الحق شيئاً، والمستتر منه في حيز الجواز للعمل به أي بالمستتر
وإن لم يظهر في إلخ: هذا هو القسم الرابع، فلايجوز به العمل إذا خالف القياس؛ لأنهم لم يكونوا يردّون الحديث الثابت عن النبي و لم يكونوا يتركون العمل به، فإذا ردّوه وتركوه علم أنهم اتهموه في هذه الرواية، وهو دون الموضوع في احتمال الكذب. ومثاله ماروى الترمذي عن المغيرة عن الشعبي قال: قالت فاطمة بنت قيس: طلقني على عهد رسول الله ، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا سكنى لك ولا نفقة". قال مغيرة: فذكرته لإبراهيم فقال: قال عمر : لاندعُ كتاب الله وسنة نبينا ل بقول ،امرأة، لاندري أحفظت أم نسيت؟ [رقم: ۱۱۸۰] وقال عمر ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة، فلم ينكره أحد، فصار إجماعاً على أن الحديث مستنكر.

جائز: بشرط أن لا يخالف القياس بل يكون موافقاً له، وفائدة إضافة الحكم حينئذ إلى الحديث مع كونه ثابتاً بالقياس أيضاً هو أن لا يتمكن الخصم فيه من المنع عن الحكم، كما يتمكن في القياس. ذلك الزمان: أي الصدر الأول، قال النبي "خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم" الحديث [الترمذي رقم: ۲۲۲۱] في زماننا : في أهل هذا الزمان، وهذا هو القسم الخامس من المجهول.
Chapter of Sunnah: The report of an unknown narrator. The second foundation: Sunnah. If the narrator is unknown, not known except by a hadith he narrated or two hadiths, like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad al-Muhabbaq, then if the Salaf narrate from him and testify to his truthfulness, or remain silent about criticism, his hadith becomes like the hadith of a known narrator. And if there is disagreement about him alongside transmission of reliable narrators from him, it is likewise according to us... And al-Shafi'i and Malik (may Allah have mercy on them) held that tasriyah (tying udders of milch animal) is a defect, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes he may return it and a sa' of dates, or keep it, acting on the apparent meaning of the hadith. This: Know that this is the madhhab of 'Isa ibn Aban. But according to al-Karkhi and those who follow him from our companions, the narrator's fiqh is not a condition for preferring hadith over qiyas; rather, the report of every just, precise narrator is accepted if it does not contradict the Book and the well-known Sunnah, and it is given precedence over qiyas. This is the manifest truth, and most scholars lean towards it, and it is the transmitted way from the Companions and Followers. Unknown means in narrating hadith and integrity, not in lineage, since he is not known etc. By one hadith he narrated or two hadiths: his case is not free from five categories. If the Salaf narrate from him etc. this is the first category of the five: criticism after his narration reached them, that is the second category: known for fiqh, integrity, and precision, so it is accepted and given precedence over qiyas. In it: i.e., in his hadith, by accepting some and rejecting some alongside transmission of reliable narrators from him, this is the third category. Likewise, i.e., like the hadith of a known narrator, so it is accepted and given precedence over qiyas according to us. Its example: what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that he was asked about a man who married a woman, did not fix a dower for her, and did not consummate until he died. Ibn Mas'ud said: She has the mahr al-mithl of her peers, no reduction and no excess, she must observe 'iddah, and she inherits. Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan al-Ashja'i stood and said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) judged concerning Barwa' bint Washiq, a woman from us, similar to what you judged, so he [Ibn Mas'ud] rejoiced... and did not act on this hadith... but acted on his opinion, that the object of contract returned to her intact, so she does not deserve a dower in exchange, like if he divorced her before consummation and did not name a dower. So al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) acts on what he acted on, which is his qiyas, and rejects this report because it is disputed, so qiyas takes precedence over it. And we acted on this hadith because reliable narrators transmitted this report from him, such as Ibn Mas'ud from the first century, 'Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and al-Hasan from the second century. So their narration from him and their acting on his report established his integrity, especially since it is also supported by qiyas, which is that death confirms mahr al-mithl just as it confirms the named dower. If no opposition appears among the Salaf except rejection, his hadith is not accepted and becomes mustanqir (rejected). And if the narrator's hadith does not appear among the Salaf and is not met with rejection or acceptance, it is not obligatory to act on it, but acting on it is permissible. That is because integrity was the norm in that era. So the hadith of such an unknown person in our time is not permissible to act on due to the prevalence of corruption. And he said: The mutawatir produces certain knowledge, the mashhur produces tranquility, the solitary produces dominant opinion, and the mustanqir from it produces mere assumption, and assumption avails nothing against truth. And the mustatir from it is in the realm of permissibility to act on. Then the commentary: This is the fourth category. It is not permissible to act on it if it opposes qiyas because they would not reject an established hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and they would not abandon acting on it. So if they rejected and abandoned it, it is known that they suspected this narration, and it is less than the fabricated [hadith] in probability of lying. Its example is what al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Mughira from al-Sha'bi who said: Fatima bint Qays said: My husband divorced me three times during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "No housing and no maintenance for you." Al-Mughira said: I mentioned it to Ibrahim who said: 'Umar said: We do not leave the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the saying of a woman; we do not know whether she remembered or forgot. And 'Umar said that in the presence of the Companions, and no one denied it, so it became a consensus that the hadith is mustanqir. Permissible: on condition that it does not oppose qiyas but rather agrees with it. The benefit of attributing the ruling then to the hadith, while it is also established by qiyas, is so that the opponent cannot prevent the ruling from it, as he can in qiyas. That time: i.e., the first generation. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "The best of centuries is my century, then those who follow them." In our time: i.e., among the people of this time. This is the fifth category of the unknown.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work explains the rules for accepting hadith from an unknown narrator (majhool). The author first outlines the issue: an unknown narrator is one who is not known except through one or two hadith he narrates. The Hanafi position is that if the pious predecessors (salaf) narrate from him and testify to his truthfulness, or remain silent (which implies acceptance), his hadith is treated like that of a known narrator. If reliable narrators differ about him, the hadith is still accepted and given precedence over qiyas. The author then contrasts this with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions using the example of the tasriyah hadith, where they reject it in favor of qiyas. The key point of contention is whether the narrator's knowledge of fiqh is a condition for preferring his hadith over qiyas. The Hanafi school, represented by al-Karkhi, holds that it is not a condition; rather, any just and precise narrator’s hadith is accepted if it does not contradict clear texts, and it takes precedence over qiyas. This is supported by the example of the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, where the Prophet’s ruling on mahr al-mithl in case of death is accepted by Hanafis despite opposition to qiyas, because reliable narrators from the first and second centuries transmitted it. The passage then details five categories of unknown narrators: 1) Those from whom salaf narrate and attest—accepted; 2) Those who are criticized after their narration but are known for fiqh and integrity—still accepted and preferred over qiyas; 3) Those about whom reliable narrators differ—accepted; 4) Those whose hadith is rejected by salaf—rejected and labeled mustanqir, like the hadith of Fatima bint Qays about no housing and maintenance, which was rejected by 'Umar and the Companions; 5) Those whose hadith is not known among salaf but also not rejected—it is permissible to act on it if it agrees with qiyas. The commentary also notes that in the early generations, integrity was the norm, so even an unknown narrator could be accepted, but in later times due to widespread corruption, such reports are not accepted.

Key Terms
المجهول (al-majhool): An unknown narrator: one not known in terms of hadith narration and integrity, except through his own narration of one or two hadith.
المستنكر (al-mustanqir): A hadith that is rejected because the salaf opposed it and did not act on it, indicating suspicion of the narrator.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogic reasoning; here it is the method of deriving rulings that is opposed to the hadith in some cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why do they accept the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq despite it contradicting qiyas?
A) Because the narrator was a famous faqih.
B) Because the hadith is mutawatir.
C) Because reliable narrators transmitted it and the Salaf acted on it, establishing its integrity.
D) Because it agrees with the qiyas of the majority.

Key Takeaway
The narrator's fiqh is irrelevant for accepting his hadith; what matters is his integrity and precision.

The Epistemological Hierarchy of Hadith in Hanafi Usul
Differentiating hadith by certainty: mutawatir, mashhur, ahad, mustanqir, mustatir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the five epistemological categories of hadith (mutawatir, mashhur, khabar wahid, mustanqir, mustatir) according to Hanafi usul, and state the legal consequence (hukm) of each category.

Core Idea
The authority of a hadith in Hanafi usul is determined by its epistemological level — from certain (mutawatir) to permissible (mustatir).

This passage from Muntakhab al-Husami summarizes the Hanafi classification of hadith according to the certainty they produce. Understanding this hierarchy is foundational for usul al-fiqh because it governs whether a report can be used as proof (hujja) and what weight it carries. The author distinguishes five categories, from the highest level of certainty to the weakest, and explains their legal effect.

Guided Path
1
List the five categories
Recall the names: mutawatir, mashhur, khabar wahid, mustanqir, mustatir. These cover the spectrum from highest certainty to weakest.
2
Identify the epistemological level of each
For each category, state the kind of knowledge it produces: yaqin (certainty), tuma'nina (tranquility), ghalib al-ra'y (dominant opinion), zann/wahm (weak assumption), jawaz (permissibility).
The passage defines each explicitly.
3
Understand the opposites
Note which categories are opposed: mutawatir has no opposite; mashhur is opposed by mustanqir; khabar wahid produces dominant opinion which is stronger than mustanqir's wahm; mustatir is neither accepted nor rejected.
The text says 'yuqabiluhu al-mustanqir' in relation to tranquility.
4
Apply the legal consequence
Mutawatir obligates belief and action; mashhur obligates action with high confidence; khabar wahid is acceptable for action; mustanqir is not acted upon; mustatir is permissible if not opposing qiyas.
This determines whether a hadith can be used as proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ المصنّف من هذا لخص كلامه وبين حاصله فقال: فصار المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين والمشهور علم الطمأنينة وخبر الواحد علم غالب الرأي، والمستنكر منه يفيد الظن، وإن الظنّ لا يغني من الحق شيئاً، والمستتر منه في حيز الجواز للعمل به أي بالمستتر
أي بهذا الحديث
لأن العدالة أصل في ذلك الزمان، حتى أن رواية مثل هذا المجهول في زماننا لايحلّ العمل به لظهور الفسق، فصار المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين والمشهور علم الطمأنينة وخبر الواحد علم غالب الرأي، والمستنكر منه يفيد الظن، وإن الظنّ لا يغني من الحق شيئاً، والمستتر منه في حيز الجواز للعمل به أي بالمستتر
ويقابله الموضوع حيث ينقطع عنه احتمال كونه حجة بالكلية. علم الطمأنينة : وهو العلم الحاصل في القلب يحتمل جانب المخالف احتمالاً ضعيفاً جدا، بخلاف اليقين حيث لا يحتمله ويقابله المستنكر، كما ستعرف غالب الرأي وهو ما كان جهة الثبوت فيه راجحاً، والمراد به الظنّ، فإن قلت: ما الفرق بينه وبين علم الطمانينة؟ قلتُ: فرق ظاهر؛ إذ في الأول جهة العدم مرجوح جدا، وفي الثاني أيضا مرجوح لكن لا بتلك المرتبة فهو أقوى من الثاني. يفيد الظنّ أي الوهم وهو ما كان عدم الثبوت فيه راجحاً. لا يغني: أي لا يفيد شيئاً، وهذا إشارة إلى أنه لا يجوز به العمل كما مرّ.
والمستتر منه أي من الخبر الواحد وهو الذي لم يعرف في السلف ولم يقابل بردّ ولا قبول.
When the author finished this, he summarized his speech and clarified its gist, saying: So the mutawatir obligates certain knowledge, the mashhur obligates tranquility, the solitary report obligates dominant opinion, and the mustanqir from it yields assumption, and assumption avails nothing against truth. And the mustatir from it is in the realm of permissibility to act on it, i.e., the mustatir. That is, by this hadith, because integrity was the norm in that era, so much so that narration of such an unknown person in our time is not permissible to act on due to the prevalence of corruption. So the mutawatir obligates certain knowledge, the mashhur obligates tranquility, the solitary report obligates dominant opinion, and the mustanqir from it yields assumption, and assumption avails nothing against truth. And the mustatir from it is in the realm of permissibility to act on. It is opposed by the fabricated (mawdu'), where the possibility of it being an argument is completely cut off. Tranquility is the knowledge that occurs in the heart, which allows a very weak possibility of the opposite side, unlike certainty which allows none. It is opposed by the mustanqir, as you will know. Dominant opinion is that for which the aspect of establishment is preponderant, and it is intended to mean assumption. If you say: What is the difference between it and tranquility? I say: A clear difference: in the first, the aspect of non-existence is very weak, and in the second also weak but not to that degree; so it is stronger than the second. Yields assumption means wahm, which is that for which non-establishment is preponderant. Does not avail: i.e., does not benefit anything. This indicates that it is not permissible to act on it, as passed. Al-mustatir minhu: i.e., from the solitary report, which is one not known among the Salaf and not met with rejection or acceptance.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on unknown narrators by classifying all reports into an epistemological hierarchy. The author summarizes the levels: Mutawatir (mass-transmitted) produces certain knowledge (yaqin) that cannot be doubted. Mashhur (well-known among the early generations but not reaching tawatur) produces tranquility of the heart (tuma'nina), meaning a high degree of confidence but theoretically open to a very weak possibility of error. Khabar wahid (solitary report) produces dominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), which is the basis for action in Hanafi fiqh but falls short of certainty. Mustanqir (rejected report) yields mere assumption (zann) or even wahm (imagining), which is not sufficient for action. Mustatir (concealed report), which is not known among the Salaf but also not rejected, is permissible to act on if it does not oppose qiyas. The commentary elaborates that the mustatir is different from the mustanqir; it is in the realm of permissibility (jawaz). The fabricated hadith (mawdu') is completely cut off from being a proof. The hierarchy is important for usul because it determines the epistemological weight and consequently the legal force of each type of hadith.

Key Terms
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A hadith transmitted by such a large number at each level that collusion on falsehood is impossible, giving certain knowledge.
المشهور (al-mashhur): A hadith known among the Salaf but not reaching tawatur; gives tranquility (tuma'nina).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary report that does not reach the level of tawatur or shuhra; gives dominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y).
المستنكر (al-mustanqir): A hadith that the Salaf rejected and abandoned, indicating suspicion; yields weak assumption (wahm).
المستتر (al-mustatir): A hadith not known among the Salaf and not rejected; permissible to act on if agreeing with qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of hadith, according to this passage, produces 'tranquility' (tuma'nina) and is opposed by the mustanqir?
A) Mutawatir
B) Mashhur
C) Khabar wahid
D) Mustatir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy of hadith—from mutawatir (certainty) to mustatir (permissibility)—determines the epistemological weight and legal force of each report, guiding which can be used as proof in fiqh.

Mustankar and Mustatar: Epistemic Classification of Khabar Wahid
Classifying epistemic categories of khabar wahid based on Salaf response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a solitary hadith as mustankar or mustatar based on the response of the Salaf, and determine whether it can be acted upon in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The Salaf's response to a hadith determines its epistemic value: rejection invalidates action if opposed to qiyas; silence permits action without obligation.

In the Hanafi school, not all solitary hadiths carry equal weight. The early generations (Salaf) either accepted, rejected, or remained silent about certain narrations. This passage classifies these responses into distinct categories that affect whether a hadith can be used as a legal proof. Understanding this classification is essential for a mufti evaluating the reliability of a hadith report.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Salaf's response
Examine whether the hadith was explicitly rejected by the Salaf, or if it was neither accepted nor rejected.
The response can be rejection (رد) or silence (لا رد ولا قبول).
2
Classify the hadith type
If rejected, it is mustankar (rejected). If neither rejected nor accepted, it is mustatar (hidden).
3
Determine permissibility of action
Mustankar cannot be acted upon if it contradicts qiyas. Mustatar can be acted upon but is not obligatory.
For mustatar, action is permissible (ja'iz) not wajib.
4
Place in epistemic hierarchy
Mustankar yields zann (weak conjecture); mustatar yields jawaz (permissibility). Compare to mutawatir (yaqin) and mashhur (tam'nina).
The hierarchy establishes different binding forces.

وإن لم يظهر في السلف إلا الرد لم يقبل حديثه وصار مستنكراً. وإن كان لم يظهر الراوي حديثه في السلف ولم يقابل برد ولا قبول لم يجب العمل به، لكن العمل به جائز؛ أي بهذا الحديث لأن العدالة أصل في ذلك ، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا سكنى لك ولا نفقة". قال مغيرة: فذكرته لإبراهيم فقال: قال عمر : لاندعُ كتاب الله وسنة نبينا ل بقول ،امرأة، لاندري أحفظت أم نسيت؟ [رقم: ۱۱۸۰] وقال عمر ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة، فلم ينكره أحد، فصار إجماعاً على أن الحديث مستنكر. جائز: بشرط أن لا يخالف القياس بل يكون موافقاً له، وفائدة إضافة الحكم حينئذ إلى الحديث مع كونه ثابتاً بالقياس أيضاً هو أن لا يتمكن الخصم
